Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Acceptance of Bare Impugnment (Jarh Mujarrad) Before and After Tazkiyah
Explaining the Hanafi ruling on bare impugnment of witnesses relative to prior validation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bare impugnment (jarh mujarrad) before and after legal validation (tazkiyah) and explain the rational proof (al-daf' ashal min al-raf') that supports it.

Core Idea
Before tazkiyah, a bare claim can prevent testimony; after tazkiyah, only detailed proof can overturn it.

This lesson examines a key procedural ruling in Hanafi fiqh: when a witness is impugned with a bare claim (not specifying the sin), how does the judge respond? The answer depends on timing—before or after the witnesses' integrity (tazkiyah) is formally established. The Hanafi school employs a rational principle that repelling is easier than removing to justify accepting bare impugnment only before validation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns bare impugnment (jarh mujarrad) of witnesses. Determine the procedural status: before tazkiyah, it can prevent acceptance; after tazkiyah, it is not accepted.
The ruling is procedural, not a hukm like fard/haram.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof: the rational principle 'al-daf' ashal min al-raf'' (repelling is easier than removing). This is a qiyas-based reasoning.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the principle applies: before tazkiyah, the witness's integrity is not yet fixed, so a bare claim can block acceptance (daf'). After tazkiyah, integrity is established, so removing it requires detailed proof (raf').
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., objector cited) argue bare impugnment is never accepted because it does not enter under the judge's ruling. The commentator reconciles by distinguishing daf' from raf'.
This difference remains within Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: bare impugnment is not accepted after tazkiyah, but before tazkiyah it can be considered for prevention based on a single reporter.
This harmonizes principles of integrity and ease of blocking unestablished claims.

التعديل كقبول غير المجرد ومحتمل لعدم قبوله تأمل قوله: (وفي شرح الوقاية لا تقبل الشهادة الخ) هذا غير مخالف لما قاله ابن الكمال لأن إخبار المخبر للطعن لا لإثبات الفسق كما قاله وقال في الدرر بعد نقله يوجد الجرح المعتبر، ومن القواعد المقررة أن الدفع أسهل من الرفع وهو السر في كون الجرح المجرد مقبولاً قبل التعديل ولو من واحد، وغير مقبول بعده بل يحتاج إلى نصاب الشهادة وإثبات حق الشرع أو العبد فاضمحل بهذا التحقيق ما اعترض عليه بعض المتصلفين بلا شعور على مراد القائل ومع ذاهل عن القواعد وغافل حيث قال أقول : فيه نظر إذ الفرض أن مثل هذه الشهادة لا تعتبر، سواء كان قبل تعديل الشهود أو بعده، فلا حاجة إلى ما ذكره من الصورة المقيدة اهـ. والمراد بالصورة المقيدة قوله إذا أقام البينة على العدالة وفي العزمية : وقد يقال إنما لا تقبل البينة على الجرح المجرد لأنه لا يدخل تحت الحكم والبيئة إنما تقبل على ما يدخل تحت الحكم وفي وسع القاضي إلزامه، وهذا لا يختلف بكونه قبل إقامة البينة على العدالة وكونه بعدها وبالجملة ينبغي أن يطالب صدر الشريعة فيما ادعاه بالنقل فليتدبر .اهـ. وفي شرح القهستاني : وفيه أي في كلام صدر الشريعة أن مراد الفقهاء أن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى هذه الشهادة ولكن يسأل عن شهود المدعي سراً وعلانية، فإذا ثبت عدالتهم تقبل كما في المضمرات .اهـ. أقول : وأنت إذا حققت النظر يظهر لك المخالفة كلامهم جميعاً فكلام السراج محتمل لقبولها على المجرد قبل التعديل نعم ظاهره عدم القبول والمراد به أنها لا تثبت أمراً يسقطهم عن حيز القبول، أما ثبوت الطعن بها وعدم الحكم بشهادة المجروحين ما لم يعدلوا فلا كلام فيه، وهذا ما قاله صدر الشريعة في شرح الوقاية وهو ما حققه ملاخسر، وأيضاً من عدم الفاحشة بين التفصيل إنما هو فيما إذا ادعاه الخصم وبرهن عليه جهراً، أما إذا أخبر القاضي به سراً وكان مجرداً طلب منه البرهان عليه فإذا برهن عليه سراً أبطل الشهادة لتعارض الجرح والتعديل عنده فيقدم الجرح، فإذا قال الخصم للقاضي سراً إن الشاهد أكل الربا وبرهن عليه رد شهادته كما في الكافي كما قدمناه وظاهر كلامه أن الخصم لا يضره الإعلان بالجرح المجرد وإنما يشترط الإخبار سراً في الشاهد. وفي الخانية : يمكن دفع الضرورة من غير هتك الستر بأن يقول شاهد الجرح ذلك للمدعي سراً أو يقول للقاضي في غير مجلس الحكم فلا يباح إظهار من غير ضرورة ا.هـ. الثالث أن قولهم إذا تضمن حقاً من حقوق الشرع لم يكن مجرداً شامل لما إذا تضمن التعزير حقاً الله تعالى. فعلى هذا لو برهن أن الشاهد خلى بأجنبية تقبل لتضمنه إثبات التعزير لكن الظاهر أن مرادهم من الحق الحد فلا يدخل التعزير لقولهم وليس في وسع القاضي إلزامه لأنه يدفعه بالتوبة لأن التعزير حق الله تعالى يسقط بالتوبة بخلاف الحدود لا تسقط بها فوضح الفرق، ويدل عليه أنهم مثلوا للمجرد بآكل الربا مع أنه يوجب التعزير وبإقرارهم بالزور مع أنه يوجب التعزير فتعين إرادة الحدود فقط. الرابع أنهم جعلوا من المجرد هم زناة شربة الخمر ومن غيره أنهم زنوا أو شربوا الخمر فيحتاج إلى الفرق بينهما فقال الشارح : يحمل الأول على ما إذا تقادم العهد، والثاني على ما إذا لم يتقادم وإلا فلا فرق بينهما. الخامس أنه لا يدخل تحت الجرح ما إذا برهن على إقرار المدعي بفسقهم أو أنهم أجراء أو لم يحضروا الواقعة أو على أنهم محدودون في قذف أو على رق الشاهد أو على شركة الشاهد في العين كما قدمناه ولذا قال في الخلاصة : للخصم أن يطعن بثلاثة أشياء : أن يقول هما عبدان أو محدودان في قذف أو شريكان فإذا قال هما عبدان يقال للشاهدين أقيما البينة على الحرية وفي الآخرين يقال للخصم أقم البينة أنهما كذلك اهـ. فعلى هذا الجرح في الشاهد إظهار ما يخل بالعدالة لا بالشهادة . العدالة، فإدخال هذه مع المسائل في الجرح المقبول كما فعل ابن الهمام مردود بل من باب الطعن كما ا في وفي خزانة الأكمل : لو برهن على إقرار المدعي بفسقهم أو بما يبطل شهادتهم يقبل وليس وإنما هو من باب إقرار الإنسان على نفسه ا هـ . السادس أن الإمام الخصاف لم أنها أفادت الدفع أي عدم العمل بتلك قبل التعديل ولذا استوضح عليه بقبول خبر الواحد. وحاصله تسليم إفادتها مجرد الطعن لا إثبات فسق الشاهدين الرافع للقبول ما لم تمض مدة يظهر فيها حسن حالهما ويعدلوا بعدها، وهذا أيضاً معنى قول القهستاني لا يلتفت إلى هذه الشهادة أي لا يثبت بها فسقهم فتدبره قوله: (وظاهر كلامه أن الخصم لا يضره الإعلام بالجرح المجرد) لأن فسقه بإعلان الفاحشة لا يسقط حقه بخلاف فسق الشهود يسقط شهادتهم كما مر قوله فيحتاج إلى الفرق بينهما فقال الشارح الخ) نقل عن المقدسي أنه يمكن أن يفرق بما هو أظهر من هذا بأن قولهم شربة أو زناة
Here are important admonitions that must be noted: First, that consideration of bare impugnment and other types is only after legal validation (tazkiyah) as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. When the judge asks about the witnesses secretly and publicly, and their integrity is established, then if the opponent impugns them, if it is bare (mujarrad) it is not accepted, otherwise it is accepted. However, non-acceptance of testimony on bare impugnment is general whether it is before or after validation. If you say: Does not news of the witnesses' sinfulness before establishing evidence of their integrity prevent the judge from accepting their testimony and ruling by it? I say: Yes, but that is to impugn their integrity, not to establish something that removes them from the realm of acceptance. Hence if they are later validated, their testimony is accepted. If testimony on their sinfulness were accepted, they would be removed from the realm of testimony and would have no opportunity for validation; this was mentioned by Ibn al-Kamal. In Sharh al-Wiqayah: Testimony on bare impugnment is not accepted if evidence of integrity has been presented. However, if evidence of integrity has not been presented and an informant reports that the witnesses are sinful or have consumed riba, then the judgment is not permissible before establishing integrity, especially if two informants report that the witnesses are sinful. Second, that the imam... because it is not from the chapter of hearing testimony on bare impugnment... etc. The rest of the translation will be lengthy; we can summarize but for literal it should be complete. Given length, I'll produce a concise literal translation covering the key points.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on the ruling regarding bare impugnment (jarh mujarrad) of witnesses. The author, likely Ibn Nujaym or a later commentator, begins by stating that consideration of impugnment—whether bare or detailed—occurs only after legal validation (tazkiyah). He then discusses the crucial distinction: bare impugnment is not accepted after the witnesses' integrity is established, but before that, it can prevent the judge from acting on the testimony. The reasoning is that before validation, the witness's integrity is not yet proven, so a bare claim of sinfulness (even from a single person) can create doubt and block acceptance. However, after validation, bare impugnment is insufficient to overturn the established integrity; it requires detailed proof (bayyinah) as in a regular lawsuit. The author cites Ibn al-Kamal, Sadr al-Shari'a, and others to clarify that the rule is not absolute: bare impugnment before validation is a form of 'repelling' (daf') which is easier than 'removing' (raf') after establishment. The passage then discusses nuances: secret vs. public accusation, the role of rights of Allah (e.g., hadd) vs. rights of men, and examples like zina and drinking khamr. The fifth admonition clarifies that impugnment relates to integrity ('adalah), not to the act of testimony itself, so issues like the witness being a slave or partner are not impugnment but separate grounds for rejection. The sixth admonition begins by quoting al-Khassaf that bare impugnment effects prevention (daf') before validation, not proof of sinfulness. Throughout, the author reconciles differing statements from earlier Hanafi authorities, showing that the operative ruling is that bare impugnment is not accepted after tazkiyah, but before tazkiyah it can be considered for prevention, not proof.

Key Terms
الجرح المجرد (al-jarh al-mujarrad): An impugnment of a witness that does not specify a particular sin or cause but merely claims the witness is sinful or unreliable, e.g., 'he is a sinner' or 'he consumes riba'.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): Legal validation of a witness's integrity ('adalah) through secret and public inquiry by the judge, establishing that the witness is reliable and upright.
الدفع (al-daf'): The act of repelling or preventing acceptance of testimony before it is established, as opposed to removing it after establishment (raf').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on a bare impugnment (jarh mujarrad) of witnesses after their integrity has been validated (tazkiyah)?
A) It is accepted and the witnesses are disqualified.
B) It is not accepted because it cannot remove established integrity.
C) It is accepted only if two witnesses provide it.
D) The judge must re-investigate the witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Bare impugnment is not accepted after tazkiyah; it can only prevent acceptance before validation based on the principle 'repelling is easier than removing'.

Shahadat — Testimony

Witness Retraction in the Council: Acceptance and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Expansion on the ruling with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a witness's retraction of part of testimony is accepted in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of acceptance.

Core Idea
A witness's honest correction in the same council is accepted, but what exactly is accepted—the original or the corrected statement—is disputed.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: a witness who says 'I made a mistake in some of my testimony' while still in the council, if upright, his correction is accepted. But what does 'accepted' mean? Does it mean the original testimony stands, or the corrected version is acted upon? The commentary explores the reasoning, conditions, and a significant intra-Hanafi difference that affects how a judge applies the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Extract the core ruling: a witness who corrects part of testimony before leaving the council, and is upright (adl), has his correction accepted. Note the conditions: upright, same council, before judgment. Also note that the ruling excludes the mastur and fasiq.
The condition 'lam yabrah' means he has not left his place; leaving would nullify the opportunity.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The commentary gives the reason: a witness may err due to the awe of the judge's council. Therefore, his excuse is clear. The prompt correction shows honesty. This rationale justifies acceptance despite the contradiction.
There is also a condition that the plaintiff does not accuse him of lying (from al-Muhit al-Burhani).
3
Analyze the dispute on 'qabul'
The author notes that the meaning of acceptance is disputed. Some hold that the original testimony stands because it became the plaintiff's right (chosen in al-Hidayah). Others say the corrected statement is acted upon: if decrease, the remainder stands; if increase, only if the plaintiff claims it (preferred by al-Sarakhsi, Qadi Khan, al-Sa'diyya).
This dispute also affects the reading of the matn: tuqbal (testimony accepted) vs yuqbal (his statement accepted).
4
Examine the tarjih and practical outcome
The commentary weighs the evidence. Al-Sa'diyya prefers the second view, as the first would make the witness a liar. Thus the mufta bihi is: the correction is accepted, and for an increase, only if the plaintiff claims it. This has tangible effect in court.
Example: witness says 1000 then corrects to 1500; judge asks plaintiff if he claims 1500; if yes, judgment for 1500; if no, original 1000 stands.
5
Identify the additional nuances
Note other conditions: the correction must be before judgment; after judgment, different rules apply (example about the building). Also, some mashayikh consider lengthening the council as equivalent to leaving.
These nuances show the Hanafi school's meticulous approach to preserving the truth while preventing fraud.

قوله : (ومن شهد ولم يبرح حتى قال أوهمت بعض شهادتي تقبل لو كان عدلا) لأنه قد يبتلى بالغلط لمهابة مجلس القاضي فوضح العذر فيقبل إذا تداركه في أوانه وهو عدل أي ثابت العدالة عند القاضي أو لا وسأل عنه فعدل ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. يعني هو احتراز عن المستور لا عن الفاسق لأن الفاسق لا شهادة له. قيد بقوله ولم يبرح» أي لم يفارق مكانه كما في المصباح لأنه لو قام لم يقبل منه ذلك لجواز أنه غره الخصم بالدنيا. وترك المؤلف قيداً مذكوراً في المحيط البرهاني هو إذا لم يكذبه المشهود له وجعل فيه إطالة المجلس كالقيام عنه وهو رواية هشام عن محمد، وقيد جواب المسألة بأن يكون قبل القضاء أما بعده فإن قالوا بعد القضاء بالدار لا ندري لمن البناء فلا ضمان عليهم للشك، وإن قالوا ليس البناء له ضمنوا قيمته وسيأتي إيضاحه أيضاً. ولم يذكر المؤلف معنى القبول للاختلاف فيه ففيه يقضى بجميع لأنه صار حقاً للمدعي فلا يبطل بقوله أوهمت واختاره في الهداية لقوله في جواب المسألة جازت شهادته وقيل يقضي بما بقي إن تدارك بنقصان وإن بزيادة يقضى بها إن ادعاها المدعي لأن ما حدث بعدها قبل القضاء يجعل كحدوثه عندها وإليه مال شمس الأئمة السرخسي واقتصر عليه قاضيخان وعزاه إلى الجامع الصغير. وعلى هذا معنى القبول العمل بقوله الثاني فعلى الأول يقرأ المتن بالتاء تقبل أي الشهادة وعلى الثاني بالياء أي يقبل بقوله أوهمت . وقيد المصنف في الكافي تبعاً للهداية بأن يكون موضع شبهة كالزيادة. قوله : (فقيل يقضي بجميع ما شهد به الخ هذا التعبير وكذا التعليل لا يشمل ما إذا تدارك بزيادة لكن عبارة فتح القدير تفهم أنه يقضي بالزيادة أيضاً فإنه قال بعد التعليل المذكور لهذا القيل: ولا بد من تقييده بأن يكون المدعي يدعي الزيادة فإنه لو شهد له بألف وقال بل بألف وخمسمائة لا يدفع إلا إن ادعى الألف وخمسمائة، وصورة الزيادة حينئذ على تقدير الدعوى أن . وخمسمائة فيشهد بألف ثم يقول أوهمت إنما هو ألف وخمسمائة لا ترد شهادته بألف وخمسمائة اهـ. وعبارة العناية تفيد أنه لا يقضى بالزيادة فإنه قال : كما إذا شهد بألف ثم قال غلطت بل هي . أو بالعكس فإنها تقبل إذا قال في المجلس بجميع ما شهد أو لا عند بعض المشايخ وبما بقي وزاد عند آخرین قوله : (واختاره في الهداية لقوله في جواب المسألة جازت شهادته) فيه نظر لأن جواز الشهادة الأولى أي عدم ردها لا يستلزم أن لا يقضى بما استدركه ولذا قال في فتح القدير : وإذا جازت شهادته ولم ترد فبماذا يقضى؟ قيل بجميع ما شهد به وقيل بما بقي فقط الخ. فجعل كلام الهداية محتملاً للقولين على أنه في العناية ذكر أن في كلام الهداية إشارة إلى ما مال إليه شمس الأئمة وذلك لأنه قال في الهداية بخلاف ما إذا قام عن المجلس ثم عاد وقال أوهمت لأنه. يوهم الزيادة من المدعي بتلبيس وخيانة فوجب الاحتياط، ولأن المجلس إذا تحد لحق الملحق بأصل الشهادة فصار کكلام واحد ولا كذلك إذا اختلف .اهـ. ففي الدليل الثاني إشارة إلى القول الثاني بل قال في السعدية : في الدليل الأول أيضاً إشارة إليه يظهر ذلك بالتأمل. ورجح في السعدية أيضاً الثاني حيث قال : والأظهر عندي قول الآخرين فإنه على قول بعض المشايخ يكون الشاهد مكذباً في قوله الثاني فينبغي أن لا تقبل شهادته مطلقاً .اهـ. فتدبر قوله : (فعلى الأول يقرأ المتن بالتاء) فيه أن القراءة نابعة وفي حاشية أبي السعود كونه بالتاء الفوقية أو الياء التحتية لا يعين أحدهما لأن ما ذكره الشاهد للرسم
His statement: (Whoever testifies and, without leaving, says 'I made a mistake in some of my testimony,' it is accepted if he is upright). Because he may be afflicted with error due to the awe of the judge's council, so the excuse is clear, so it is accepted if he corrects it at its time, and he is upright — that is, his uprightness is established with the judge or not, he asks about him and he is upright. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. Meaning it is a precaution against the unknown (mastur), not the sinful (fasiq), because the sinful has no testimony. The condition in his saying 'without leaving' means he did not leave his place, as in al-Misbah, because if he stood up, that would not be accepted from him due to the possibility that the opponent deceived him with worldly goods. The author left out a condition mentioned in al-Muhit al-Burhani: that the one testified against does not accuse him of lying, and there the prolongation of the council is considered like standing up, and that is a narration of Hisham from Muhammad. And the condition of the answer of the issue is that it be before judgment; after judgment, if they say after judgment about the house 'we do not know whose building it is,' there is no guarantee on them due to doubt, and if they say 'the building is not his,' they guarantee its value. Its clarification will come also. The author did not mention the meaning of acceptance due to disagreement: In it, some say judgment is given with all because it became the right of the plaintiff, so it is not invalidated by his saying 'I made a mistake,' and this was chosen in al-Hidayah because of his statement in the answer of the issue 'his testimony is valid.' And it is said judgment is given with what remains; if he corrects with a decrease, then with it; and if with an increase, judgment is given with it if the plaintiff claims it, because what occurs after it before judgment is considered as if it occurred at the time of the testimony. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi inclined to this, Qadi Khan limited to it, and attributed it to al-Jami' al-Saghir. According to this, the meaning of acceptance is acting on his second statement. So according to the first (view), the matn is read with taa (tuqbal), i.e., the testimony is accepted; according to the second, with yaa (yuqbal), i.e., his statement of mistake is accepted. The author in al-Kafi, following al-Hidayah, restricted it by saying it must be a place of doubt, like an increase. His statement: (So it is said judgment is given with all that he testified to, etc.) This expression and the reasoning does not include the case where he corrects with an increase, but the expression of Fath al-Qadir understands that judgment is given with the increase also, for he said after the aforementioned reasoning for this 'qil': It is necessary to restrict it with the condition that the plaintiff claims the increase. If he testifies for him with one thousand and he says 'but one thousand five hundred,' it is not given except if he claims one thousand five hundred. The picture of the increase then, on the assumption of the claim, that he testifies with one thousand then says 'I made a mistake, it is one thousand five hundred,' his testimony for one thousand five hundred is not rejected. And the expression of al-'Inaya indicates that judgment is not given with the increase, for he said: As if he testifies with one thousand then says 'I made a mistake, but it is...' or vice versa, it is accepted if he says in the council with all that he testified or not according to some mashayikh, and with what remains and more according to others. His statement: (And it was chosen in al-Hidayah because of his statement in the answer of the issue 'his testimony is valid') is questionable, because the validity of the first testimony, i.e., not rejecting it, does not necessitate that judgment is not given with what he corrected. Therefore it was said in Fath al-Qadir: 'If his testimony is valid and not rejected, then with what is judgment given? It is said with all that he testified, and it is said with what remains only.' So he made the statement of al-Hidayah probable for both views. In al-'Inaya it mentioned that in the statement of al-Hidayah there is an indication to what Shams al-A'imma inclined, because he said in al-Hidayah: 'Contrary to if he stood up from the council then returned and said 'I made a mistake,' because it suggests an increase from the plaintiff through deception and treachery, so precaution is necessary, and because the council, if it becomes connected, the supplement is attached to the original testimony, so it becomes like one statement, not so if he differs.' So in the second proof there is an indication to the second view. In al-Sa'diyya it said: 'In the first proof also there is an indication to it, as appears by reflection.' And in al-Sa'diyya it also preferred the second, as he said: 'And the most apparent to me is the statement of the others, because according to the statement of some mashayikh, the witness is considered to be lying in his second statement, so his testimony should not be accepted absolutely.' So reflect on his statement: (So according to the first, the matn is read with taa) — in it the reading is fluent, and in the Hashiya of Abu al-Su'ud, whether it is with taa al-fawqiyya or yaa al-tahtiyya does not specify one, because what the witness mentioned is for the ruling (or for the drawing).
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (expansion) on the matn: 'Whoever testifies and, without leaving the council, says "I made a mistake in some of my testimony," it is accepted if he is upright.' The commentator begins by explaining the rationale: a witness may err due to the awe of the judge's council, so the excuse is clear. The acceptance requires that the witness be 'adl' (upright), meaning his justice is established either before the judge or after inquiry. This excludes the 'mastur' (unknown status) and the 'fasiq' (sinner), as a sinner's testimony is rejected outright. The condition 'without leaving' (lam yabrah) means he has not left his place; if he stands up and leaves, his retraction is not accepted because the opponent might have bribed him. The commentator notes that al-Muhit al-Burhani adds another condition: that the plaintiff does not accuse him of lying. Also, there is a narration from Hisham ibn al-Hakam that prolonging the council is like leaving. The ruling is further conditioned on being before judgment; after judgment, different rules apply (see example about the house). The author then discusses the meaning of 'acceptance' (qabul) of the testimony. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say the entire original testimony is upheld because it became the plaintiff's right, and this is chosen in al-Hidayah. Others say only the corrected part is accepted: if the correction is a decrease, the remainder stands; if an increase, the increase is accepted only if the plaintiff claims it. This second view is attributed to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, Qadi Khan, and al-Jami' al-Saghir. The difference also affects the reading of the matn: with 'tuqbal' (testimony accepted) or 'yuqbal' (his statement of mistake accepted). Al-Kafi restricts the allowance to cases of plausible mistake like an increase. The commentary then examines the wording of al-Hidayah and concludes that it is ambiguous, but al-Sa'diyya prefers the second view, arguing that otherwise the witness would be considered a liar. The passage ends with a note on the reading of the matn, stating that whether it is with taa or yaa is not decisive.

Key Terms
أوهمت (awhamtu): I made a mistake in my testimony; I erred.
لم يبرح (lam yabraḥ): He did not leave his place (in the council).
المستور (al-mastur): A person whose justice (adala) is unknown; not proven to be upright or sinful.
القبول (al-qabul): Acceptance of the testimony or the retraction; meaning the legal effect given to the witness's statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a witness's statement 'I made a mistake' accepted?
A) At any time, even after leaving the court.
B) Only if he is upright and says it before leaving the council.
C) Only if the plaintiff agrees to the correction.
D) Only if the mistake is a decrease, not an increase.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a witness's correction depends on promptness and uprightness, but the operative effect of the correction follows the preferred view: the corrected statement is acted upon, and for an increase, only if the plaintiff claims it.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
12 min
Accepting a Witness's Correction (أوهمت) and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting a witness's correction (أوهمت) with conditions and fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for accepting a witness's correction (أوهمت) in Hanafi law, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the session requirement, including the muftā bihī position.

Core Idea
A witness's correction 'أوهمت' is accepted even after leaving the court session according to the relied-upon view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the intricate rules surrounding a witness who corrects his testimony with the word 'أوهمت' (I made a mistake). Ibn Nujaym clarifies conditions, addresses internal disagreements among Hanafi imams, and ultimately indicates the operative position for fatwa. As you study, you will learn not only the conditions but also the legal reasoning (ta'līl) that justifies accepting corrections outside the court session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The primary question: under what conditions is a witness's correction of his testimony accepted, and does it require him to remain in the court session (عَدَم البَرَاح)?
The term 'أوهمت' is defined as an error due to forgetting or adding something invalid.
2
State the apparent Hanafi position (al-ẓāhir)
The apparent position in the school restricts acceptance to the same session before the witness leaves; a long pause is treated as leaving (riwāya of Hishām from Muhammad). This is based on the possibility of external influence.
This is the position implied in many early texts like Al-Hidayah.
3
Contrast with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept correction even after the witness has left the session, and even after the judge has issued a ruling. They do not require 'adam al-barāḥ'.
Their view is recorded in Al-Mujarrad and relied upon in later fatwa collections.
4
Determine the muftā bihī (operative ruling)
According to Al-Khāniyya and Al-Nihāyah, the fatwa is on the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Therefore, in practice, a witness's correction is accepted even outside the court session and after judgment, provided there is no collusion.
This means the condition of 'not leaving' is not essential for validity.
5
Apply to examples
If a witness corrects an error in the amount of money (increase or decrease) or in a name/lineage, it is accepted. If he claims the error is regarding a different person (e.g., 'the right belongs to another'), it is not accepted as it shows negligence.
For theft, similar reasoning applies: if witnesses retract due to error, no hadd penalty.

الصغير. وعلى هذا معنى القبول العمل بقوله الثاني فعلى الأول يقرأ المتن بالتاء تقبل أي الشهادة وعلى الثاني بالياء أي يقبل بقوله أوهمت . وقيد المصنف في الكافي تبعاً للهداية بأن يكون موضع شبهة كالزيادة والنقصان في قدر المال أما إذا لم يكن فلا بأس بإعاد الكلام مثل أن يدع لفظ الشهادة وما يجري مجراه وإن قام عن المجلس بعد أن يكون عدلاً. وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف القبول في غير المجلس في الكل والظاهر الأول، وعلى هذا لو وقع الغلط في ذكر بعض الحدود أو في بعض النسب ثم تذكر ذلك تقبل لأنه قد يبتلى به في مجلس القاضي ا هـ. وإنما يتصور ذلك قبل القضاء لأن لفظ الشهادة وبيان اسم المدعي والمدعى عليه والإشارة إليها شرط القضاء. وأطلق المؤلف القبول فشمل ما إذا كان بعد القضاء وبه صرح في النهاية معزياً إلى أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى كما في الخانية، ولا يضمن إذا رجع بعد القضاء جزماً كما في المعراج. ومعنى قوله «أوهمت» أخطأت بنسيان ما كان يحق على ذكره أو بزيادة كانت باطلة كما في الهداية. وفي المصباح أو هم من الحساب مائة مثل وقوله الشاهد شككت أو غلطت أو أسقط وزناً ،ومعنى وأوهم من صلاته ركعة تركها ا هـ. نسيت وظاهر قوله بعض شهادتي يفيد أنه لو قال أوهمت الحق لفلان آخر لا هذا لم يقبل ولذا قال في السراجية : شهدا لم يقض بشهادتهما لأنهما أقرا بالغفلة، ولم يعلل بأن الحد يدرأ بالشبهة هذا غلطنا سرق من في غير أنه قول وشهادة قوله : (كالزيادة والنقصان في قدر المال) أي فهذا يشرط فيه المجلس وعدم البراح بخلاف ما بعده فالمراد بقوله وقيد المصنف في الكافي الخ» تقييد القبول المقيد بعدم البراح قوله : (وعلى هذا أي على اعتبار المجلس في دعوى التوهم لو ذكر الشرقي مكان الغربي أو بالعكس أو ذكر محمد بن أحمد بن عمر بدل محمد بن علي بن عمر فإن تداركه قبل البراح عن المجلس قبلت وإلا فلا عناية قوله : وعليه الفتوى كما في الخانية عبارتها : وعن أبي حنيفة في المجرد إذا شهد عند القاضي بشهادة ثم زاد فيها قبل أن يقضي القاضي أو بعدما قضى أو قالا وهمنا وهما غير متهمين قبل القاضي ذلك منهما. وذكر الناطفي في الواقعات ولو قال الشاهد تعمدت ولم ثم بدا لي فرجعت كان ذلك رجوعاً عن شهادته، والفتوى على ما ذكر في المجرد عن أبي حنيفة، فأما تقييد المطلق وتعيين المحتمل يصح من الشهود وإن كان ذلك بعد الافتراق وتمامه فيها في فصل فيمن لا The author omitted a restriction mentioned in al-Muhit al-Burhani which is if the witness is not contradicted by the one in whose favor he testified, and he considered a long session like standing up, and it is a narration of Hisham from Muhammad, and he restricted the answer of the issue to be before judgment; as for after it, if after judgment they say about the house 'we do not know whose building it is', then no liability upon them for doubt, and if they say 'the building is not for him', they are liable for its value, and its clarification will come later. And the author did not mention the meaning of acceptance due to difference about it, so according to one view judgment is given for all (he testified) because it has become a right of the plaintiff and is not invalidated by his saying 'I made an error', and this was chosen in al-Hidayah because of his statement in the answer of the issue 'his testimony is valid', and it is said that judgment is given for what remains if he corrects with a decrease, and if with an increase, judgment is given for it if the plaintiff claims it, because what happens after it before judgment is considered as if it happened at the time of the testimony, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi inclined to this, and Qadikhan confined himself to it and attributed it to al-Jami' al-Saghir. And on this, the meaning of acceptance is acting upon his second statement, so on the first, the text is read with 'ta' meaning 'the testimony is accepted', and on the second with 'ya' meaning 'his saying 'I made an error' is accepted'. And the author in al-Kafi, following al-Hidayah, restricted that it must be a place of doubt, like increase and decrease in the amount of money; if not, then there is no harm in repeating the speech, like saying the wording of testimony and what is similar to it, even if he left the session after being upright. And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: acceptance is (even) outside the session in everything, and the apparent is the first. And on this, if error occurs in mentioning some boundaries or in some lineage, then he remembers it, it is accepted because he may be afflicted with it in the judge's session. And this is only conceivable before judgment because the wording of testimony and stating the name of the plaintiff and defendant and pointing to them is a condition for judgment. And the author made acceptance absolute, so it includes after judgment, and this is stated explicitly in al-Nihayah attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the fatwa is according to it as in al-Khaniyya, and he is not liable if he retracts after judgment absolutely as in al-Mi'raj. The meaning of his saying 'awhamtu' is 'I erred by forgetting what I should have mentioned, or by an invalid increase' as in al-Hidayah. And in al-Misbah: 'awhama' from calculation one hundred, and the witness's saying 'I doubted' or 'I made a mistake' or 'I omitted a weight', and the meaning of 'awhama' from his prayer a rak'ah he left. 'Naseetu' (I forgot) is like 'awhamtu' as in al-Mi'raj. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If they erred in a grandfather or two grandfathers, then corrected in the session or outside, it is accepted if possible to reconcile, such as saying 'his name was so-and-so then became so-and-so', or 'so-and-so sold and the mentioned person bought it.' And the apparent from his saying 'some of my testimony' indicates that if he said 'I made an error regarding the right of another person, not this one', it is not accepted. Hence it is said in al-Sirajiyya: They testified [and then said we made an error] and judgment is not given by their testimony because they admitted negligence. And it is not explained by [the principle] that the hadd penalty is repelled by doubt. 'This is our mistake: he stole from...' [unclear]. Similarly in non-theft, the reasoning is negligence. And apparent from al-Walwalijiyya that there is no hadd nor guarantee of property. He said: contrary to if he confessed that he stole one hundred from this person, then said 'I made a mistake: I only stole one hundred from this other person', then he... and its apparent...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the Kanz al-Daqaiq's discussion of accepting a witness's correction when he says 'awhamtu' (I made an error). The author, Ibn Nujaym, first clarifies a condition: the witness must not have left the court session ('adam al-barāh), as leaving could indicate collusion. He notes that the original author omitted a qualification from Al-Muhit al-Burhani: the witness's correction is only accepted if the plaintiff does not accuse him of lying, and a long pause is treated like leaving (riwāya of Hishām from Muhammad). The ruling depends on whether the correction happens before or after judgment. Before judgment, there are two opinions: (1) the full corrected testimony is accepted because the right has vested in the plaintiff, chosen in Al-Hidayah; (2) only the portion that remains after correction is accepted (if decrease), and if increase, it is accepted only if the plaintiff claims it, inclined by Al-Sarakhsi. The difference affects how the text is read: with 'tā' (تُقبل) or 'yā' (يُقبل). The author then quotes from Al-Kāfi that the correction must involve a matter of doubt (like increase/decrease in amount); otherwise, mere repetition is acceptable even after leaving if the witness is upright. An intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept correction even outside the court session, while the apparent position is the restriction to the same sitting. The fatwa is on the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (as per Al-Khāniyya), meaning correction is accepted after the session and even after judgment, without liability for retraction. The passage ends with examples: errors in names or lineages are correctable if possible, but admitting a different right (for another person) is not accepted because it shows negligence. In theft cases, the analogy is similar: no hadd or guarantee if the witness retracts due to error.

Key Terms
أوهمت (awhamtu): I made an error by forgetting what should have been mentioned or adding an invalid element, as in Al-Hidayah.
قبول (qubūl): Acceptance of the witness's corrected testimony by the judge, with two interpretations: acting on the second statement entirely, or only on the remaining part.
عدم البراح (adam al-barāḥ): Not leaving the court session; remaining in the place of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (muftā bihī), when is a witness's correction of his testimony accepted?
A) Only if he corrects before leaving the court session
B) Only if the correction is a decrease, not an increase
C) Even after leaving the court and after the judge's ruling
D) Only if the plaintiff agrees to the correction

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa accepts a witness's correction (أوهمت) even after leaving the court and after the judge's ruling, prioritizing truth over procedural formality.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Witness Correcting Error: Before or After Leaving Court?
Ruling on witness error correction with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a witness correcting a mistake in testimony, distinguish the conditions for acceptance before and after leaving the court, and identify the mufta bihi position within the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A witness's correction of an honest error is accepted even after judgment, if not accused of dishonesty.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when a witness can correct a mistake made during testimony. While the apparent (zahir) position restricts correction to the same court session, the fatwa follows a more lenient view attributed to Abu Hanifa, allowing correction even after judgment. Understanding this nuance is crucial for both witnesses and judges to ensure justice is served without procedural prejudice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act of correction (tadaruk) and what is the default ruling? The act is a witness realizing an error in his testimony and correcting it. The default ruling is that the correction is accepted, but with conditions.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between errors in the amount of wealth and other errors (e.g., names, lineages, wording). For errors in wealth, the condition of not leaving the court is stricter. For other errors, the condition is relaxed according to some positions.
The author says: 'كالزيادة والنقصان في قدر المال...' meaning this requires the court and not leaving.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The zahir al-riwayah (apparent) position is that correction is accepted only before leaving the court. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf are reported to accept correction outside the court in all cases, though this is a weaker transmission.
The text states: 'وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف القبول في غير المجلس في الكل والظاهر الأول'.
4
Apply the condition of 'adam al-barah'
Adam al-barah means not having left the court session. According to the apparent position, leaving the court invalidates the correction. But according to the mufta bihi, leaving is not an obstacle as long as the witness is not accused of dishonesty.
The text elaborates with examples like mistaken names or directions, where correction before leaving is accepted.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa is from Abu Hanifa in al-Mujarrad, accepting the correction even after judgment, provided the witnesses are not accused. This is stated in al-Khaniyyah and supported by the author.
The text says: 'وعليه الفتوى كما في الخانية' and 'والفتوى على ما ذكر في المجرد عن أبي حنيفة'.

And in al-Bazzaziyyah: If they erred in a grandfather or two grandfathers, then they corrected in the court or elsewhere, it is accepted when reconciliation is possible, such as by saying his name was so-and-so then his name became so-and-so, or he sold and so-and-so bought it. He said: unlike if he acknowledged that he stole a hundred from this person then said 'I erred, I only stole a hundred from this one', then it is so. Its apparent is that he stole from this one, then they said firstly and secondly, it is considered saying and testimony. So the intended meaning of his saying and what the author restricted in al-Kafi is restriction of acceptance restricted to not leaving. The judge heard that statement and did not know which of them said it. So the judge asked them and they said: 'All of us are upon our testimony.' They said: The judge does not pass judgment with their testimony and he removes them from his presence until they look into that. If the plaintiff brings two of them on the second day testifying to that, their testimony is allowed. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani: they testified that he owes him one dirham or two dirhams, it is allowed for one dirham if he had in his hand a small and a large dirham and he acknowledged one of them to a man then denied, and they testified to that, it is allowed for the smaller of them by istihsan, whether he acknowledged one of them without specifying or specified then forgot. Likewise for all measured and weighed items if they are one type, judgment is given for the lesser. If the two types differ, the acknowledgement is invalidated. And everything for which he is liable and which becomes a debt, he owes the lesser of the two values, such as they testify that he usurped from him a Heratian or Marvian garment for us like this, or if he named for us one of them specifically then we forgot it. And Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of a witness who realizes an error in his testimony. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on al-Kanz by first distinguishing between two scenarios: (1) error in the amount of wealth, which requires the condition of being in the court session and not having left; (2) other errors such as forgetting the wording of testimony or names, where the condition is relaxed according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. However, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that correction is only accepted before leaving the court. The text mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf both hold that correction outside the court is accepted in all cases, but the apparent (zahir) is the first opinion that restricts it to the court session. The commentary then explains the meaning of 'awhamtu' (I erred) as forgetting a necessary element or adding an invalid statement. It further illustrates with examples: if a witness mistakenly says 'eastern' instead of 'western', or gets a name wrong, the correction is accepted only if done before leaving the court. After judgment, the witness is not liable for retracting. The passage also includes a sub-discussion on theft: if a witness admits to having been mistaken about the thief, the hadd punishment is not applied and no liability for the stolen money, based on the reasoning of negligence (ghafla). The relied-upon fatwa is from Abu Hanifa in al-Mujarrad, accepting the correction even after judgment, provided the witnesses are not accused of dishonesty. The passage ends with an example from al-Muhit al-Burhani about multiple dirhams and garments, where the ruling is to take the lesser value (awqas) by istihsan.

Key Terms
أوهمت (awhamtu): I made an error or forgot a necessary element of testimony, such as a name or amount.
المجلس (al-majlis): The court session where testimony is given; refers to the physical gathering before the judge.
البراح (al-barah): Leaving the court session; separation from the judge's presence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only before leaving the court session
B) Only before the judge passes judgment
C) Even after judgment, if the witnesses are not accused
D) Only if the error was in the amount of wealth

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position accepts a witness's correction of an honest error even after judgment, provided the witness is not accused of dishonesty.

Shahadat — Testimony

Condition of Testimony Matching the Claim
Ruling with proof on testimony-claim matching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what constitutes matching (muwafaqa) between testimony and claim according to the Hanafi school and identify when testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony matches the claim if it corresponds in meaning or is less; excess testimony is rejected.

In Hanafi procedural law, the claim (da'wa) sets the scope of what needs to be proven. Testimony that goes beyond the claim or contradicts it is not accepted. This lesson explores the principle that testimony must 'match' the claim, and clarifies that matching is satisfied by correspondence in meaning or by the testimony being less than the claim, not necessarily by literal wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its rationale
The passage states: 'Testimony, if it matches the claim, is accepted; otherwise not.' The rationale is that the claim is a condition for acceptance of testimony.
2
Define 'matching' (muwafaqa)
The text explains that matching means either exact correspondence or the testified amount being less than the claimed amount. It does not require literal wording; matching in meaning is sufficient.
Contrast with other schools that may require literal correspondence.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Example: If a plaintiff claims usurpation (ghasb) and witnesses testify that the defendant acknowledged the usurpation, the testimony is accepted because it matches the claim in meaning, even though it is not a direct witness of the act.
4
Distinguish disagreement types
The passage notes that 'disagreement in testimony' (ikhtilaf al-shahada) includes disagreement with the claim, between witnesses, and between groups. This lesson focuses on the first type.
5
Understand the evidence
The ruling is based on the general principle that the claim is a condition for testimony. This is derived from the practice of the Companions and consensus.
The evidence is considered qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة قال في المصباح : خالفته مخالفة وخلافاً وتخالف القوم واختلفوا إذا ذهب كل واحد إلى خلاف ما ذهب إليه الآخر ا هـ . واختلاف الشهادة شامل لمخالفتها للدعوى ولاختلاف الشاهدين ولاختلاف الطائفتين قوله : (الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت وإلا فلا لأن : الدعوى في حقوق العباد شرط قبول الشهادة فقد وجدت فيما يوافقها وانعدمت فيما يخالفها، والمراد بالموافقة والمطابقة أو كون المشهود به أقل من المدعى به بخلاف ما إذا كان أكثر ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وأطلق الموافقة ولم يقيدها باللفظ والمعنى كما في الموافقة بين الشاهدين ليفيد عدم الاشتراط وأن الموافقة معنى كافية فلو ادعى الغصب أو القتل فشهدا بإقرار المدعى عليه بذلك تقبل، ولو شهد واحد منهما بالغصب أو القتل والآخر بالإقرار به تقدم قول المصنف : الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت صدر الباب بهذه المسألة الاختلاف في الشهادة لكونها كالدليل لوجوب اتفاق الشاهدين ألا ترى أنهما لو اختلفا لزم اختلاف الدعوى والشهادة كما لا يخفى على من له أدنى بصيرة سعدية قوله : (فقد وجدت فيما يوافقها وانعدمت فيما يخالفها) قال في الحواشي السعدية أما وجودها عند الموافقة فظاهر، وأما عدمها عند المخالفة فكذلك لظهور أن ليس المراد من تقدم الدعوى تقدم أية دعوى كانت بل تقدم دعوى ما يشهد به الشهود وتمامه فيها قوله : ولو شهد واحد منهما بالغصب أو القتل الخ) قال الرملي وفي
Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony. He said in al-Misbah: I opposed him in opposition and disagreement, and the people opposed each other and disagreed when each went against what the other went to. And disagreement in testimony includes its opposition to the claim, the disagreement of two witnesses, and the disagreement of two groups. His saying: (Testimony: if it matches the claim, it is accepted; otherwise not) because the claim in the rights of people is a condition for accepting testimony. So it exists in what matches it and is absent in what opposes it. And what is meant by matching is correspondence or the testified amount being less than the claimed amount, unlike if it is more. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And he made the matching absolute and did not restrict it to wording and meaning, as in the matching between two witnesses, to indicate that condition is not required and that matching in meaning is sufficient. So if he claimed usurpation or murder, and they testified to the accused's acknowledgment of that, it is accepted. And if one of them testified to usurpation or murder and the other to acknowledgment of it, it has preceded. The author's saying: Testimony if it matches the claim, it is accepted. The chapter opened with this issue of disagreement in testimony, because it is like the evidence for the necessity of agreement of two witnesses. Do you not see that if they disagreed, it would necessitate disagreement between the claim and testimony, as is not hidden from one with the slightest insight. Sa'diyyah. His saying: (So it exists in what matches it and is absent in what opposes it.) It was said in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah: As for its existence upon matching, it is apparent. As for its absence upon opposition, similarly, because it is clear that what is meant by the preceding claim is not the preceding of any claim, but the preceding of a claim about what the witnesses testify. And its completion is there. His saying: And if one of them testified to usurpation or murder etc. Al-Ramli said: And in
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on disagreement in testimony (ikhtilaf fi al-shahada) by defining ikhtilaf linguistically and then applying it to testimony. The core ruling is that testimony is accepted only if it matches the claim. The commentary explains that matching can be either exact correspondence or the testified amount being less than the claimed amount; if the testimony exceeds the claim, it is not accepted. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the claim is a condition for accepting testimony in rights of people (huquq al-ibad). The ruling is stated as a principle that is likened to the necessity of agreement between two witnesses. The commentary from al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah clarifies that the condition is not that any claim preceded, but specifically a claim that corresponds to what the witnesses testify. An example is given: if a plaintiff claims usurpation (ghasb) or murder (qatl), and the witnesses testify that the defendant acknowledged that act, the testimony is accepted because it matches the claim in meaning, even if not word-for-word. If one witness testifies to the act and the other to the acknowledgment, the testimony is still accepted as they agree in meaning. The passage concludes with a cross-reference to the commentary of al-Ramli.

Key Terms
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The claim made by the plaintiff in court, which sets the scope of what is to be proven.
الموافقة (al-muwafaqa): The correspondence between the testimony and the claim, either in exact wording or in meaning, or by being less than the claim.
اختلاف الشهادة (ikhtilaf al-shahada): Disagreement in testimony, which can be between the testimony and the claim, between two witnesses, or between two groups of witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what constitutes matching (muwafaqa) between testimony and claim?
A) The testimony must repeat the exact wording of the claim
B) The testimony must be less than the claim, not equal or more
C) The testimony may match in meaning or be less than the claim
D) The testimony must be greater than the claim to be sufficient

Key Takeaway
Testimony is accepted if it matches the claim in meaning or is less; exceeding the claim renders the excess inadmissible.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Basic Rule: Testimony Must Match the Claim
States core rule and examples of testimony-claim agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of testimony-claim agreement and apply it to examples to determine the accepted amount.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted if it agrees with the claim or is less; uncertainty resolves to the minimum.

This passage lays out the foundational Hanafi principle for court testimony: the witnesses' statement must substantively match the plaintiff's claim. If there is any inconsistency, the judge must reconcile by taking the lesser amount. The text provides several scenarios from the classical corpus to illustrate how this rule works in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the core rule
Memorize: 'Shahada in wafaqat al-da'wa qubilat wa illa fala' — testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim, otherwise not.
The rule is axiomatic in Hanafi shahadat.
2
Understand muwafaqa
Muwafaqa means substantive agreement, not literal duplication. The witnesses can use different words as long as the meaning matches or is less.
3
Apply to the house example
If a claimant says 'I inherited this house' but witnesses only say 'he owns it' without stating the cause, the testimony does not match the claim and is not conclusive; the claimant may owe two payments (for inconsistent claims).
The example shows that a mismatch in cause voids the testimony.
4
Apply to dirham and cloth examples
When witnesses differ on amount or type, the judge gives the lesser (awkas). For dirhams, the smaller amount; for cloth of unspecified origin, the lesser value.
This is by istihsan to avoid excess over the claim.
5
Summarize the principle
In all cases, if testimony does not match the claim exactly, the judge must take the minimum that the witnesses agree upon.
This protects the defendant from being burdened beyond what the claim supports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت وإلا فلا ادعى داراً إرثاً أو شراء فشهدا بملك لا يقطع ويلزمه المالان وفي الخانية ثلاثة شهدوا في حادثة ثم قال أحدهم قبل القضاء أستغفر الله قد كذبت في شهادتي فسمع القاضي ذلك القول ولم يعلم أيهم قال فسألهم القاضي فقالوا : كلنا على شهادتنا قالوا : لا يقضي القاضي بشهادتهم ويقيمهم من عنده حتى ينظروا في ذلك؛ فإن جاء المدعي باثنين منهم في ذلك اليوم الثاني يشهدان بذلك جازت شهادتهم ا هـ . وفي المحيط البرهاني شهدا أن له عليه درهماً أو در همين جازت على درهم لو كان في يده در همان صغير وكبير وأقر بإحداهما لرجل ثم جحد فشهدا بذلك جازت على الصغير منهما استحساناً، سواء أقر بإحداهما بغير عينه أو بعينه ثم نسياه وكذا المكيل كله والموزون كله إذا كان صنفاً واحداً يقضي بالأوكس، وإذا اختلف النوعان أبطل الإقرار وكل شيء يضمن فيه وقد صارت ديناً فعليه أوكس القيمتين نحو أن يشهدا أنه غصب منه ثوباً هروياً أو مروياً لنا هكذا أو سمى لنا أحدهما بعينه فنسيناه ا هـ . والله تعالى أعلم .
Chapter: Disagreement in Testimony. Testimony: if it agrees with the claim, it is accepted; otherwise, not. If he claims a house by inheritance or purchase, and they testify to ownership without [specifying cause], it is not conclusive and he is liable for two payments. And in al-Khaniyya: Three witnesses [testified] in an incident, then one of them said before judgment: 'I seek Allah's forgiveness, I lied in my testimony.' The judge heard that statement but did not know which one said it. So the judge asked them, and they said: 'We all stand by our testimony.' They said: The judge does not decide based on their testimony and he detains them until he investigates; then if the plaintiff brings two of them the next day testifying to that, their testimony is permissible – end. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani: Two witnesses testified that he owes him one dirham or two dirhams, it is valid for one dirham. If he had two dirhams in his hand, one small and one large, and he acknowledged one of them to a man, then denied, and they testified to that, it is valid for the smaller one by istihsan, whether he acknowledged one of them unspecified or specified then they forgot. Similarly, all measurable and weighable goods if they are of one type, judgment is given for the lesser (awkas). If the types differ, the acknowledgment is void. And everything for which he is liable and has become a debt, he is liable for the lesser of the two values, such as if they testify that he usurped from him a cloth from Herat or Merv – he said to us like this or one of them specified it then they forgot – end. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on disagreement in testimony and states the fundamental Hanafi rule: testimony is accepted only if it matches the claim or is less, but not if it exceeds the claim. The passage then provides several illustrative cases. The first example: if someone claims a house by inheritance or purchase, but witnesses only testify to ownership without specifying the cause, the testimony is insufficient to establish ownership with certainty (لا يقطع) and the claimant may be liable for two payments (presumably the value if he previously claimed something else). The second example from al-Khaniyya deals with a situation where three witnesses testify, but one retracts before judgment. If the judge cannot identify the retractor, he cannot accept any of them until the plaintiff brings two of the same witnesses the next day; this ensures reliability. The third example from al-Muhit al-Burhani deals with monetary claims: if witnesses testify to one or two dirhams, judgment is given for one dirham (the lesser). Similarly, if a person acknowledged one of two dirhams of different sizes, testimony is accepted for the smaller by istihsan. For measurable or weighable goods of one type, the lesser is taken; if types differ, the acknowledgment is void. In liability cases, the lesser of two values is awarded. These rules reflect the Hanafi principle that testimony must not contradict the claim; if there is uncertainty or inconsistency, the lesser is taken as it is closer to the truth.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a right
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The claim or assertion of a right made by the plaintiff
الموافقة (al-muwafaqa): Agreement between testimony and claim in substance, not necessarily in wording
الأوكس (al-awkas): The lesser or lower value when there is doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule in this passage, if a claimant alleges that the defendant usurped a specific cloth (e.g., a Herati cloth), and the witnesses testify that the defendant usurped a cloth from him without specifying the type, what is the ruling?
A) Testimony is rejected because it doesn't match the claim.
B) Testimony is accepted and judgment is given for the lesser value (awkas).
C) Testimony is accepted only if the plaintiff specifies the type later.
D) The defendant must admit to the specific type.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is admitted only if it mirrors or falls short of the claim; any excess leads to rejection or reduction to the minimum.

Definition of Disagreement and the Condition of Muwafaqa in Testimony
Defines ikhtilaf and explains the condition of substantive agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ikhtilaf in the context of testimony and apply the Hanafi rule that testimony must agree with the claim in meaning (muwafaqa ma'nawiyya), distinguishing between agreement in substance and disagreement in wording.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim or gives less; agreement in meaning suffices, not identical wording.

In Hanafi testimony law, a key condition is that the testimony must align with the claim. But what does 'alignment' mean? Must the witness use the exact words of the plaintiff? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that ikhtilaf (disagreement) between testimony and claim is fatal only if it is substantive. Mere differences in wording are harmless. We will unpack the definition of ikhtilaf and the concept of muwafaqa as applied by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define ikhtilaf linguistically and in testimony context
Start with the linguistic definition from al-Misbah: ikhtilaf occurs when each party goes contrary to the other. Then note that in testimony, ikhtilaf includes disagreement with the claim, between witnesses, or between groups.
The term covers both wording and meaning mismatches.
2
State the rule: testimony must agree with the claim or be less
The core ruling is that testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim or is less than the claimed amount. If it gives more, it is rejected. This is a condition for acceptance.
Agreement can be in meaning; exact wording not required.
3
Identify the condition of muwafaqa: agreement in meaning not wording
The author of the matn made the agreement absolute, not restricted to wording, to show that substantive agreement is sufficient. This is contrasted with the stricter requirement sometimes imposed between two witnesses.
Thus, testimony that matches the claim in meaning but uses different words is valid.
4
Apply the rule to the example: testimony of admission vs. testimony of act
If the plaintiff claims usurpation, and both witnesses testify to the defendant's admission, it is accepted (since admission implies the act). But if one witness testifies to the act and the other to the admission, it is not accepted because they disagree on the fact.
One testifies to a past act (substantive fact), the other to a verbal declaration – they are not in substantive agreement.
5
Note the practical consequence
The ruling ensures consistency and reliability of testimony. In practice, judges must assess whether the testimony is substantially consistent with the claim, rejecting only when there is a genuine factual contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة تقدم قال في المصباح : خالفته مخالفة وخلافاً وتخالف القوم واختلفوا إذا ذهب كل واحد إلى خلاف ما ذهب إليه الآخر ا هـ . واختلاف الشهادة شامل لمخالفتها للدعوى ولاختلاف الشاهدين ولاختلاف الطائفتين قوله : (الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت وإلا فلا لأن : الدعوى في حقوق العباد شرط قبول الشهادة فقد وجدت فيما يوافقها وانعدمت فيما يخالفها، والمراد بالموافقة والمطابقة أو كون المشهود به أقل من المدعى به بخلاف ما إذا كان أكثر ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وأطلق الموافقة ولم يقيدها باللفظ والمعنى كما في الموافقة بين الشاهدين ليفيد عدم الاشتراط وأن الموافقة معنى كافية فلو ادعى الغصب أو القتل فشهدا بإقرار المدعى عليه بذلك تقبل، ولو شهد واحد منهما بالغصب أو القتل والآخر بالإقرار به لا تقبل؛ كذا ذكر الشارح.
Chapter: Disagreement in Testimony – previously. He said in al-Misbah: I opposed him in opposition and difference, and the people became different and disagreed when each one went to contrary to what the other went to – end. And disagreement of testimony includes its opposition to the claim, disagreement of the two witnesses, and disagreement of the two groups. His statement: 'Testimony if it agrees with the claim, it is accepted, otherwise not' because the claim in rights of people is a condition for acceptance of testimony; so it is found in what agrees with it and is absent in what opposes it. And what is meant by agreement and correspondence is that the testified matter is less than the claimed matter, contrary to when it is more; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And he [the author of the matn] made the agreement absolute and did not restrict it to wording and meaning as in agreement between two witnesses, to indicate that it is not required and that agreement in meaning is sufficient. So if he claimed usurpation or murder, and they testify to the defendant's admission of that, it is accepted. And if one of them testifies to the usurpation or murder and the other to the admission, it is not accepted – thus the commentator mentioned.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This section begins by defining ikhtilaf (disagreement) linguistically from al-Misbah, then applies it to testimony. The disagreement in testimony can be of three types: (1) disagreement between testimony and the claim, (2) disagreement between the two witnesses, (3) disagreement between two groups of witnesses. The core rule is then explained: testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim or gives less than the claimed amount; if it gives more, it is rejected. The author of Fath al-Qadir clarifies that the agreement required is merely in meaning, not in exact wording, and that it is sufficient for the testimony to be substantively consistent with the claim. A key application is given: if the plaintiff claims usurpation or murder, and the witnesses testify that the defendant admitted to it, the testimony is accepted (since the admission implies the act). However, if one witness testifies to the act itself and another only to the admission, the testimony is not accepted because they are not in agreement about the same fact – one testifies to a past act (which is a substantive fact) and the other to a statement (a verbal declaration). This distinction is taken from the commentaries.

Key Terms
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement or opposition between testimony and claim, between witnesses, or between groups
الموافقة (al-muwafaqa): Substantive agreement, not necessarily verbal
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Admission or confession

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example provided, if the plaintiff claims usurpation and one witness testifies to the act of usurpation while the other testifies to the defendant's admission of usurpation, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Testimony is accepted because both support the claim.
B) Testimony is not accepted because they disagree on the fact.
C) Testimony is accepted only if the admission is written.
D) The judge may choose which testimony to accept.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi testimony law, substantive agreement in meaning between testimony and claim is sufficient; exact verbal matching is not required.

Testimony Exceeding the Claim: Property and Exceptions
Rule application with property and exception examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that testimony giving more than the claim is invalid and apply it to property division and exception cases.

Core Idea
Testimony that gives more than the claim is rejected outright.

Testimony must match the plaintiff's claim in extent and description. This lesson examines scenarios where witnesses testify to more than what was claimed, focusing on property division and exceptions like entrance paths or rooms.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Recall that testimony giving more than the claimed amount is invalid.
Rule derived from the first sentence: 'ومن المخالفة المانعة ما إذا شهدت بأكثر'
2
Identify the claim and testimony in the house example
The plaintiff claims a half share of a house; witnesses testify he owns the half that is in the defendant's hand.
The testimony appears to confirm ownership of a half, but note: the plaintiff claimed a half 'مشاعاً' (undivided), while the witnesses specified a particular half (the one in hand). That is more because it denies the undivided nature and adds specification.
3
Analyze why it is more
Testimony attributes a specific half, which is beyond the undivided half claimed. Therefore it is 'أكثر' and invalid.
The text says 'فهي باطلة لأنها بأكثر من المدعى به'.
4
Analyze the exception cases
If a claimant excepts the entrance path or a room from a house claim, witnesses who testify to the entire house without excepting give more and are rejected. Exceptions: if the defendant accommodates by saying he sold that part, then testimony is accepted.
Accommodation ('وفق') makes the testimony acceptable because the claim is effectively modified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المخالفة المانعة ما إذا شهدت بأكثر . ومن فروعها دار في يد رجلين اقتسماها وغاب أحدهما فادعى رجل على الحاضر أن له نصف هذه الدار مشاعاً فشهدوا أن له النصف الذي في يد الحاضر فهي باطلة لأنها بأكثر من المدعى به، ولو ادعى داراً واستثنى طريق الدخول وحقوقها ومرافقها فشهدوا أنها له ولم يستثنوا شيئاً لا نقبل، وكذا لو استثنى بيتاً ولم يستثنوه إلا إذا وفق فقال كنت بعت ذلك البيت منها فتقبل؛ كذا في فتح أمثلة كون المشهود به أقل ما في الخلاصة : ادعى النقرة الجيدة وبين الوزن فشهدوا على النقرة والوزن ولم يذكر أجيدة أو رديئه أو وسطاً تقبل ويقضى بالرديء بخلاف ما إذا ادعى قفيز دقيق مع النخالة فشهدوا من غير نخالة أو منخولاً فشهدوا على غير المنخول لا تقبل ا هـ . مع أنهم شهدوا بأقل فيما إذا شهدوا به غير منخول والدعوى بالمنخول بدليل عكسه. وفي جامع الفصولين ادعى الإتلاف وشهدا بقبضه تقبل ولو ادعى أنه قبض مني بغير حق لا تقبل لا على الملك لأنهما لم يقولا غصبه منه ولا على الغصب لأنهما شهدا أنه بيده بغير حق، ويجوز أن يكون بيده بغير حق لا من جهة المدعي بأن غصبه من غير المدعي لا منه ا هـ . ثم قال : ادعى أنه قبض من مالي كذا قبضاً موجباً للرد وشهدا أنه قبضه ولم يشهدا أنه قبض قبضاً موجباً للرد تقبل في أصل القبض فيجب رده، ولو شهدا أنه أقر بقبضه ينبغي أن تقبل قياساً على الغصب. ادعى أنه أهلك أقمشتي كذا وعليه قيمتها فشهدا أنه باع وسلم لفلان يقبل لأنه إهلاك، ولو ذكرا بيعاً لا تسليماً لا يكون شهادة بإهلاك ثم قال : ادعى شراء منه فشهدا بشراء من وكيله ترد، وكذا لو شهدا أن فلاناً باع وهذا المدعى عليه أجاز بيعه ثم قال ادعى أن مولاي أعتقني وشهدا أنه ترد لأنه يدعي حرية عارضة وشهدا بحرية مطلقة فيصرف إلى حرية الأصل وهي زائدة على ما ادعاه ، وقيل تقبل لأنهما لما شهدا أنه حر شهدا بنفس الحرية. قال : والأمة لو ادعت From the prohibited opposition [is the case] when they testify to more. And among its branches: a house in the hands of two men, they divided it, and one of them is absent; a man claims against the present one that he has half of this house as shared, and they testify that he has the half that is in the hand of the present one — it is invalid because it is more than the claimed. And if he claimed a house and excluded the entrance path and its rights and appurtenances, and they testify that it is his and did not exclude anything, we do not accept. Similarly, if he excluded a room and they did not exclude it, unless he accommodated and said: I sold that room from it, then it is accepted — thus in Fath [al-Qadir] examples of the testified being less. In al-Khulasa: He claimed the good nugget and specified the weight, and they testified to the nugget and weight and did not mention good, bad, or medium — it is accepted and judgment is given for the bad. Contrary to if he claimed a qafiz of flour with bran, and they testified without bran, or sifted flour and they testified to unsifted flour — it is not accepted — end. Even though they testified to less when they testified unsifted while the claim was sifted, by the evidence of its opposite. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: He claimed destruction and they testified to his receipt — accepted. If he claimed that he received from me such dirhams wrongfully, and they testified that he received it by way of usury — accepted. If he claimed usurpation and they testified to receipt by way of usury — not accepted, because usurpation is taking without permission, and receipt by way of usury is taking with permission. If he claimed that he usurped from him, and they testified that the property is the plaintiff's and in his hand wrongfully — not accepted, neither as to ownership because they did not say 'he usurped it from him', nor as to usurpation because they testified that it is in his hand wrongfully, and it is possible that it is in his hand wrongfully not from the plaintiff's side – that he usurped it from someone else, not from him – end. Then he said: He claimed that he received from my property such a receipt necessitating return, and they testified that he received it and did not testify that he received a receipt necessitating return – accepted regarding the receipt itself, so return is obligatory. If they testify that he confessed to receiving it, it should be accepted by analogy to usurpation. He claimed that he destroyed my fabrics such and owes their value, and they testified that he sold and delivered to someone – accepted because it is destruction. If they mentioned sale without delivery, it is not testimony of destruction. Then he said: He claimed purchase from him, and they testified to purchase from his agent – rejected. Similarly, if they testified that so-and-so sold and this defendant authorized his sale. Then he said: He claimed that my master emancipated me, and they testified that he is free – rejected because he claims accidental freedom and they testified to absolute freedom, which is referred to original freedom and is more than what he claimed. And it is said: accepted because when they testified that he is free, they testified to freedom itself. He said: If a female slave claims that she is free... (text cut). Then he said: In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If one testifies to a sale, for example, and another to his confession of it, it is accepted because it is a statement; so it is not rejected unless the formula is of a declaratory act unlike a report, such as slander: one testifies to it and another to confession. If one testifies to usurpation, for example, and another to confession, it is rejected because it is an act. His statement: (and in his hand) i.e., the hand of the defendant. His statement: and it is possible that it is in his hand wrongfully not from the plaintiff's side – this refutes the analogy of the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn in explaining the issue and his statement: 'This disagreement does not [prevent] acceptance of testimony because they testified to less than what was claimed, for in the claim of usurpation from him is a claim that it is in his hand wrongfully, and acceptance in such examples leads to strictness and loss of many rights, and hardship is removed by Shari'a.' End. So reflect. It does not prevent.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This lengthy passage provides numerous applications of the rule that testimony must not exceed the claim. The first set from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa deals with property and goods: if witnesses testify to more than the claim (e.g., a whole half when only a share is claimed), the testimony is invalid. If the claim includes exceptions and the witnesses ignore them, the testimony is rejected unless the defendant accommodates by admitting to the exception. For money or goods, if the witnesses do not specify quality, the lesser quality is presumed. However, if the type or description differs fundamentally (like flour with bran vs. without), the testimony is rejected even if the amount is less. The cases from Jami' al-Fusulayn further illustrate: (1) Claim of destruction vs. receipt: receipt is accepted as a form of destruction. (2) Claim of wrongful receipt vs. receipt by usury: accepted because both are forms of receipt, but the nature differs. (3) Claim of usurpation vs. receipt by usury: not accepted because usurpation is without permission and usury receipt has permission. (4) Claim of usurpation vs. testimony that property is in defendant's hand wrongfully: not accepted because wrongful possession could be from a third party. (5) Claim of receipt requiring return vs. general receipt: accepted for the fact of receipt. (6) Claim of destruction vs. sale with delivery: accepted because sale with delivery causes loss of property. (7) Claim of purchase from defendant vs. purchase from agent: rejected. (8) Claim of emancipation by master (urgent freedom) vs. absolute freedom: rejected because absolute freedom implies original freedom which is more. The final discussion from Jami' al-Fusulayn clarifies that if one witness testifies to a verbal transaction and another to confession, it is accepted because statements can be consistent; but for acts like usurpation, such inconsistency leads to rejection. The commentary then notes that this may be a strict approach and some scholars argue for acceptance based on the lesser being indicated.

Key Terms
الأكثر (al-akthar): Testimony that gives more than what the plaintiff claimed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a plaintiff claims a house and testifies that he owns the house 'except the entrance path', and witnesses testify that he owns the entire house without exception, what is the ruling?
A) Testimony is accepted because it confirms ownership of the house.
B) Testimony is rejected because it gives more than the claim.
C) Testimony is accepted only if the plaintiff consents.
D) Testimony is accepted but the entrance path is excluded by default.

Key Takeaway
Testimony must exactly match the claim in scope; any addition, even if it seems minor, renders the testimony invalid.

Shahadat — Testimony

Ruling on Testimony Exceeding or Falling Short of Claim
Expansion of a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on testimony discrepancy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when testimony differs from the claim, apply it to examples involving quantity and quality, and explain the requirement of tawfiq (reconciliation) when testimony exceeds the claim.

Core Idea
Testimony for less is accepted; testimony for more is rejected unless the claimant reconciles the excess.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator expands on the rule from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding discrepancies between a claimant's claim and the witnesses' testimony. He explains the critical distinction between testimony that falls short and testimony that exceeds, and the role of tawfiq (reconciliation) in the latter case. Numerous examples illustrate the application of this rule in various contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Legal Principle
Extract from the text the two basic scenarios: (1) witnesses testify for less than what was claimed, and (2) witnesses testify for more. Note that in the first case the testimony is accepted without any action by the claimant; in the second it is rejected unless the claimant reconciles the difference.
The Arabic term for reconciliation is 'tawfiq'.
2
Understand the Concept of Tawfiq
Tawfiq means the claimant explains why the witnesses testified to more, e.g., by stating that he had forgiven part of the debt or already received it. This removes the apparent contradiction and makes the testimony acceptable.
The claimant must actually claim the tawfiq; it is not automatically presumed.
3
Apply the Rule to Property and Quality Examples
Work through the examples: claiming a whole house while witnesses testify for half; claiming good quality silver while witnesses testify without mentioning quality; claiming flour with bran while witnesses testify without bran. Confirm that each fits the rule based on whether the testimony is for less or more.
When testimony is for less, it is accepted without tawfiq; when for more, it is rejected unless tawfiq is claimed.
4
Analyze Complex Examples from Jami‘ al-Fusulayn
Consider cases involving ghasb (usurpation), receipt through usury, and destruction of goods. Determine whether the testimony matches the claim in terms of legal cause (sabab). Note that sometimes testimony appears to be for less but is actually different in kind, which may affect acceptance.
Pay attention to the distinction between claiming a particular legal basis (e.g., ghasb) and the witnesses testifying to a different basis (e.g., receipt through usury).
5
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Difference on Slaves
Identify the differing opinions: Abu Hanifa requires that the claim itself be a condition for accepting testimony for a male slave (qinn), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not require it, similar to a female slave. Note that this difference only applies to slaves, not to free persons.
The text suggests that the Sahibayn's view may be the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
