والحاصل أنهم إذا شهدوا بأقل مما ادعى تقبل بلا توفيق وإن كان بأكثر لم تقبل إلا إذا وفق، فلو ادعى ألفاً فشهدا بألف وخمسمائة فقال المدعي كان لي عليه ألف وخمسمائة إلا أني أبرأته من خمسمائة أو قال استوفيت منه خمسمائة ولم يعلم به الشهود تقبل، وكذا في الألف والألفين ولا يحتاج إلى إثبات التوفيق بالبينة لأن الشيء إنما يحتاج إلى إثباته بالبينة إذا كان سبباً لا يتم بدونه ولا ينفرد بإثباته كما إذا ادعى الملك بالشراء فشهد الشهود بالهبة فإن ثمة يحتاج إلى إثباته بالبينة، أما الإبراء فيتم به وحده ولو أقر بالاستيفاء يصح إقراره ولا يحتاج إلى إثباته لكن لا بد من دعوى التوفيق هنا استحساناً، والقياس أن التوفيق إذا كان ممكناً يحمل عليه وإن لم يدع التوفيق تصحيحاً للشهادة وصيانة لكلامه وجه الاستحسان أن المخالفة بين الدعوى والشهادة ثابتة صورة فإذا كان التوفيق مراداً تزول المخالفة، وإن لم يكن التوفيق مراداً لا تزول بالشك، فإذا ادعى التوفيق ثبت التوفيق وزالت المخالفة. وذكر الشيخ الإمام المعروف بـخواهر زاده أن محمداً شرط في بعض المواضع دعوى التوفيق ولم يشترط في البعض، وذاك محمول على ما إذا ادعى التوفيق أو ذاك جواب القياس فلا بد من دعوى التوفيق، فلو قال المدعي ما كان لي عليه إلا ألف درهم فقط لا تقبل شهادتهم كذا في الخانية. ولا فرق في كون المشهود به أقل بين أن يكون في الدين أو في العين، فلو ادعى كل الدار فشهدا بنصفها قضى بالنصف من غير توفيق؛ كذا في الخانية.
قوله : (والحاصل أنهم إذا شهدوا بأقل مما ادعى تقبل بلا توفيق انظر ما سنذكره في شرح
Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Disagreement in Testimony. It is not accepted. ... The summary is that if they testify for less than what was claimed, it is accepted without reconciliation, and if it is more, it is not accepted unless he reconciles. So if one claims one thousand and they testify for one thousand five hundred, and the claimant says, 'He owed me one thousand five hundred but I discharged him from five hundred,' or says, 'I collected five hundred from him and the witnesses did not know it,' it is accepted. ... There is no difference whether the testimony for less is in debt or property. So if one claims the entire house and they testify for half of it, he is adjudicated half without reconciliation. So it is in al-Khaniyyah.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the acceptability of testimony that differs from the claimant's claim. The commentator presents numerous examples to illustrate the rule: if witnesses testify for less than what was claimed, the testimony is accepted without any need for the claimant to reconcile the discrepancy. If they testify for more, the testimony is rejected unless the claimant explains the excess, e.g., by stating that he had forgiven part of the debt or had already received it. The commentary also addresses cases where the nature of the object differs (e.g., better vs. poorer quality, with or without bran) and discusses when reconciliation is required. Key authorities cited include al-Khaniyyah, Jami' al-Fusulayn, and al-Khalasah. The commentator also notes a difference of opinion regarding the requirement of a claim for a male slave versus a female slave, following Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The passage concludes with the firm rule that testimony for less is always accepted without reconciliation, and testimony for more is only accepted with the claimant's reconciliation claim.

Key Terms
التوفيق (al-tawfiq): The act of the claimant reconciling the discrepancy between his claim and the witnesses' testimony by explaining that the extra amount was due to a separate cause (e.g., forgiveness, receipt).
المشهود به أقل (al-mashhud bihi aqall): The subject matter of the testimony (e.g., amount, property) is less than what the claimant originally claimed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a claimant claims a whole house and witnesses testify that he owns half of it, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The testimony is rejected because it is less than the claim.
B) The testimony is accepted without the claimant needing to reconcile.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the claimant explains why he claimed the whole house.
D) The testimony is rejected because it does not match the claim.

Key Takeaway
Testimony for less than the claim is always accepted without reconciliation; testimony for more is only accepted if the claimant reconciles the excess.

Ruling When Claimant Discredits His Witnesses
Ruling with proof on discrediting witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a claimant discredits his own witnesses and apply Abu Yusuf's two opinions to a post-judgment scenario.

Core Idea
Discrediting one's own witnesses voids their testimony and creates liability post-judgment.

When a claimant declares that his own witnesses lied, the legal consequences depend on timing. Before judgment, the case collapses; after judgment, the claimant's admission creates a complex liability. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and Abu Yusuf's two opinions on the post-judgment scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its immediate ruling
The claimant discredits his witnesses (either fully or partially). The immediate ruling: their testimony becomes void (batil).
The text says 'batalat shahadatuhum'.
2
Understand the rationale
Two reasons are given: either it constitutes an accusation of fisq against the witness, or it is a retraction of the claim itself, and testimony without a claim is not accepted.
3
Examine the illustrative scenario
Witnesses testify that a house belongs to the claimant but specify that a room belongs to a third party. The claimant says 'that room is not mine', discrediting the witnesses.
Focus on the timing bifurcation.
4
Apply timing bifurcation
If the discrediting occurs before judgment, no ruling is given for anyone. If after judgment, the matter is more complex, and Abu Yusuf offers two opinions.
5
Analyze Abu Yusuf's two opinions
First opinion: accept the claimant's admission, give the room to the third party, and the claimant guarantees its value to the original defendant. Second opinion: the original judgment stands, but the claimant guarantees the room's value to the defendant.
The text does not specify a preferred view (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن المدعي إذا أكذب شهوده في جميع ما شهدوا به له أو بعضه بطلت شهادتهم، إما لأنه تفسيق للشاهد أو لأن الشهادة لا تقبل بدون الدعوى، فلو شهد الشهود بدار لرجل فقالوا هذا البيت من هذه الدار لفلان رجل آخر غير المدعي فقال المدعي ليس هو لي فقد أكذب شهوده، وإن قال هذا قبل القضاء لا يقضى له ولا لفلان بشيء، فإن كان بعد القضاء فقال هذا البيت لم يكن لي إنما هو لفلان قال أبو يوسف أجزت إقراره لفلان وجعلت له البيت وأراد ما بقي من الدار على المقضى عليه ويضمن قيمة البيت للمشهود عليه، ولأبي يوسف قول آخر أنه يضمن قيمة البيت للمشهود عليه ويكون ما بقي من الدار للمشهود له؛
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated that if the claimant discredits his witnesses in all or part of what they testified for him, their testimony becomes void, either because it is a declaration of the witness's sinfulness or because testimony is not accepted without a claim. So if witnesses testify for a man regarding a house and say, 'This room of this house belongs to another man besides the claimant,' and the claimant says, 'It is not mine,' then he has discredited his witnesses. If he says this before judgment, nothing is adjudicated for him or for the other man. If it was after judgment and he says, 'This room was not mine; it is for so-and-so,' Abu Yusuf said: I accept his admission for so-and-so, assign the room to him, and what remains of the house is for the defendant, and he guarantees the value of the room to the one against whom judgment was given. Abu Yusuf has another opinion: he guarantees the value of the room to the one against whom judgment was given, and what remains of the house is for the one in whose favor judgment was given.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the claimant, after his witnesses have testified, says that their testimony is false, either entirely or partially. The commentator explains that such a statement invalidates the testimony either because it accuses the witnesses of sin (fisq) or because testimony requires a claim and the claimant is effectively retracting his claim. The passage then provides a detailed example: witnesses testify that a house belongs to the claimant, but specify that a certain room belongs to a third party. If the claimant then says 'that room is not mine,' he has discredited the witnesses. The timing matters: if he says this before the judge's ruling, no judgment is given for anyone. If he says it after the ruling, Abu Yusuf presents two opinions: one where the admission is accepted and the room goes to the third party, with the claimant guaranteeing its value to the original defendant; the other where the entire house remains with the successful claimant, but he must guarantee the room's value to the original defendant. This shows the complexity when a claimant contradicts his own witnesses post-judgment.

Key Terms
أكذب شهوده (akdhaba shuhudahu): The act of the claimant declaring that his own witnesses are lying or that their testimony is false.
المقضى عليه (al-maqdi 'alayhi): The party against whom judgment was initially given (the defendant).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the claimant discredits his witnesses after judgment regarding a room in a house, what is one possible outcome according to Abu Yusuf?
A) The judgment is entirely reversed and the original defendant gets everything.
B) The room is given to the third party, and the claimant guarantees its value to the original defendant.
C) The witnesses are punished for false testimony.
D) The case is reopened and retried.

Key Takeaway
Discrediting one's own witnesses voids their testimony and, if after judgment, creates a liability for the claimant according to Abu Yusuf's opinions.

Testimony Differing from the Claim: Hanafi Rules on Less and More
Ruling on acceptance of testimony that differs in amount from the claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when witnesses testify to less or more than the claim and apply the requirement of tawfiq (reconciliation) using the principle of istihsan.

Core Idea
Testimony for less than claimed is always accepted; testimony for more requires explicit reconciliation by the claimant.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of testimony depends not on exact verbal correspondence with the claim but on substantive consistency. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the nuanced rules when witnesses under-testify or over-testify. You will learn when reconciliation (tawfiq) is needed and why the Hanafi school prefers istihsan over strict qiyas in this matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on testimony for less
When witnesses testify to an amount less than the claim, the testimony is accepted without any need for reconciliation (tawfiq). The claimant's explanation is not required.
This applies to both debt and property, e.g., if he claims the whole house and they testify to half, half is decreed.
2
Identify the ruling on testimony for more
When witnesses testify to an amount greater than the claim, the testimony is rejected unless the claimant provides a reconciliation explanation, such as having forgiven part of the debt or received payment.
The reconciliation must be explicitly claimed; it is not automatically presumed.
3
Analyze the istihsan vs qiyas reasoning
By qiyas, if reconciliation is possible, it would be presumed even without claim to validate the testimony. But by istihsan, the overt discrepancy remains, so the claimant must actively remove it by claiming tawfiq.
The reconciliation itself (e.g., ibra') is self-complete and needs no proof, but the claim of tawfiq is necessary.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of the claim
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a male slave (qinn) and a female slave (umm walad) regarding whether the claim is a condition for testimony. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad treat both slaves equally, holding that the claim is not a condition.
This dispute shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning and impacts when exact matching is required.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school requires testimony to match the claim exactly; any variance invalidates the testimony. The Hanafi school, through istihsan, accepts less without reconciliation and more with reconciliation.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi courts, the claimant can still recover the amount testified to less than claimed, or recover the claimed amount after reconciling the excess.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلاناً أعتقني وشهدا أنها حرة تقبل إذ الدعوى ليست بشرط هنا فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكون الخلاف المذكور في القن على قول أبي حنيفة، أما على قولهما ينبغي أن يقبل في القن رواية واحدة كما في الأمة إذ الدعوى ليست بشرط في القن عندهما كالأمة، ولو ادعى حرية الأصل وشهدا أن فلاناً حرره قيل ترد وقيل تقبل لأنهما شهدا بأقل ما ادعاه ا هـ. وبه علم أن المطابقة بين الدعوى والشهادة إنما هي شرط فيما إذا كانت الدعوى فيه شرطاً وإلا فلا، ولذا لو ادعت الطلاق فشهدا بالخلع تقبل كما سيأتي . والحاصل أنهم إذا شهدوا بأقل مما ادعى تقبل بلا توفيق وإن كان بأكثر لم تقبل إلا إذا وفق، فلو ادعى ألفاً فشهدا بألف وخمسمائة فقال المدعي كان لي عليه ألف وخمسمائة إلا أني أبرأته من خمسمائة أو قال استوفيت منه خمسمائة ولم يعلم به الشهود تقبل، وكذا في الألف والألفين ولا يحتاج إلى إثبات التوفيق بالبينة لأن الشيء إنما يحتاج إلى إثباته بالبينة إذا كان سبباً لا يتم بدونه ولا ينفرد بإثباته كما إذا ادعى الملك بالشراء فشهد الشهود بالهبة فإن ثمة يحتاج إلى إثباته بالبينة، أما الإبراء فيتم به وحده ولو أقر بالاستيفاء يصح إقراره ولا يحتاج إلى إثباته لكن لا بد من دعوى التوفيق هنا استحساناً، والقياس أن التوفيق إذا كان ممكناً يحمل عليه وإن لم يدع التوفيق تصحيحاً للشهادة وصيانة لكلامه وجه الاستحسان أن المخالفة بين الدعوى والشهادة ثابتة صورة فإذا كان التوفيق مراداً تزول المخالفة، وإن لم يكن التوفيق مراداً لا تزول بالشك، فإذا ادعى التوفيق ثبت التوفيق وزالت المخالفة. وذكر الشيخ الإمام المعروف بـخواهر زاده أن محمداً شرط في بعض المواضع دعوى التوفيق ولم يشترط في البعض، وذاك محمول على ما إذا ادعى التوفيق أو ذاك جواب القياس فلا بد من دعوى التوفيق، فلو قال المدعي ما كان لي عليه إلا ألف درهم فقط لا تقبل شهادتهم كذا في الخانية. ولا فرق في كون المشهود به أقل بين أن يكون في الدين أو في العين، فلو ادعى كل الدار فشهدا بنصفها قضى بالنصف من غير توفيق؛ كذا في الخانية.
A person said: 'So-and-so emancipated me' and they (witnesses) testified that she is free, it is accepted because the claim is not a condition here. So accordingly, the mentioned disagreement regarding a male slave (qinn) is according to Abu Hanifa's view. As for their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it should be accepted in the case of a male slave as one narration, like the female slave, because the claim is not a condition in a male slave according to them, as with the female slave. And if he claimed original freedom and they testified that so-and-so emancipated him, it is said it is rejected and it is said it is accepted because they testified to the least of what he claimed, end. And by this it is known that matching between the claim and testimony is a condition only where the claim is a condition; otherwise not. Hence, if a woman claimed divorce and they testified for khul', it is accepted as will come. The summary: If they testify to less than what was claimed, it is accepted without reconciliation; if it is more, it is not accepted unless reconciled. So if he claimed a thousand and they testified to a thousand five hundred, and the claimant said: 'He owed me a thousand five hundred, but I released him from five hundred' or said: 'I received from him five hundred and the witnesses did not know about it,' it is accepted. Similarly for a thousand and two thousand, and he does not need to prove the reconciliation by evidence, because a thing needs to be proven by evidence only if it is a cause that is not complete without it and cannot be proven alone, like when he claims ownership by purchase and witnesses testify to a gift – there he needs to prove it by evidence. As for release (ibra'), it is complete by itself; and if he acknowledges receipt, his acknowledgment is valid and does not need proof. However, claiming reconciliation is necessary here by istihsan. By qiyas, if reconciliation is possible, it is presumed even if he does not claim it, to validate the testimony and protect his speech. The justification for istihsan is that the discrepancy between claim and testimony is apparent in form; if reconciliation is intended, the discrepancy is removed, but if reconciliation is not intended, it is not removed by doubt. So if he claims reconciliation, it is established and the discrepancy is removed. The Shaykh al-Imam known as Khwaharzada mentioned that Muhammad stipulated claiming reconciliation in some places and did not stipulate in others, and that is interpreted as when he claims reconciliation; otherwise, that is the answer of qiyas, so claiming reconciliation is necessary. If the claimant said: 'He owed me nothing but exactly one thousand dirhams,' their testimony is not accepted. Similarly in al-Khaniyya. And there is no difference in the subject matter being less whether it is in debt or in property; if he claimed the entire house and they testified to half of it, half is decreed without reconciliation; similarly in al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the acceptance of testimony that differs in amount from the claim. It opens by discussing a case where a slave claims freedom and witnesses testify that he is free. The author notes that here the claim is not a condition for testimony, so even if the testimony does not exactly match the claim, it is accepted. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, there is a difference between a male slave (qinn) and a female slave (umm walad) regarding the necessity of the claim; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), both are treated alike – the claim is not a condition. Then the principle is summarized: if witnesses testify to less than what was claimed, their testimony is accepted without any need for reconciliation (tawfiq). If they testify to more, it is rejected unless the claimant provides a reconciliation explanation, such as claiming that he had forgiven part of the debt or received payment, and the witnesses did not know. This reconciliation does not need to be proven by evidence because the claimant's statement alone suffices, but it must be explicitly claimed. The passage also notes a difference between Muhammad and others regarding when claiming reconciliation is required – in some cases it is conditional, in others not, and the relied-upon view is that it is necessary. Finally, it clarifies that the rule applies equally to debts and physical property.

Key Terms
توفيق (tawfiq): A reconciliation between the claim and testimony by the claimant explaining the discrepancy (e.g., by stating that part was forgiven or received).
قن (qinn): A male slave owned outright; contrasted with umm walad (a slave mother of her master's child).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a claimant demands 1000 dirhams, but two witnesses testify that the defendant owes 1500 dirhams, and the claimant says 'I released him from 500,' what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The testimony is rejected outright because it exceeds the claim.
B) The testimony is accepted because the claimant provided a reconciliation explanation.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the claimant proves the release with evidence.
D) The testimony is rejected because the witnesses contradicted each other.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to accept testimony exceeding the claim if the claimant provides a plausible reconciliation, facilitating justice without strict formality.

Claimant Discrediting Witnesses: Ruling and Examples
Effect of claimant discrediting witnesses before or after judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a claimant discredits his witnesses, distinguish between discrediting before and after judgment, and apply the rule regarding partial discrediting of extra statements.

Core Idea
Discrediting witnesses invalidates testimony only on the point discredited; extra statements may still be accepted.

When a claimant contradicts his own witnesses, the testimony is compromised. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position: general invalidation due to tafsiq or loss of claim, the difference between pre-judgment and post-judgment scenarios, and the critical nuance that discrediting only affects the specific point denied. We will work through examples from al-Khaniyya to solidify the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that if the claimant discredits his witnesses wholly or partially regarding the subject of the claim, their testimony becomes invalid. Two reasons are given: it implies the witnesses are sinful (tafsiq), or the claimant contradicts the very claim needed for testimony to be accepted. Recognize that this is the baseline ruling.
2
Differentiate before vs. after judgment
Before judgment, if the claimant discredits the witnesses, no judgment is given for him or any third party mentioned. After judgment, the situation is more complex: the claimant's acknowledgment may be treated as an admission benefiting the third party, but he must compensate the original defendant. Note the two opinions of Abu Yusuf on how the remaining property is handled.
The first opinion of Abu Yusuf (validating the acknowledgment and giving the room to the third party) is implied as the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze partial discrediting
The passage clarifies that if the claimant confirms the witnesses on the core claim but denies an extra statement they added (e.g., the return of a slave, a release from debt), the testimony is accepted for the core claim. The discrediting only invalidates the extra part. This is crucial: the claimant's denial of the extra does not negate the main claim.
This prevents the defendant from escaping liability by having the claimant accidentally deny a beneficial extra.
4
Apply the rule to examples from al-Khaniyya
Work through the three examples: (1) usurpation with alleged return, (2) usurpation with alleged killing by the owner, (3) debt with alleged release. In each, if the claimant denies the extra (return, killing, release) and the defendant does not claim that extra, the witnesses' testimony on the core claim (usurpation, debt) stands, and the defendant is liable.
The key is that the claimant did not discredit the witnesses regarding the original claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن المدعي إذا أكذب شهوده في جميع ما شهدوا به له أو بعضه بطلت شهادتهم، إما لأنه تفسيق للشاهد أو لأن الشهادة لا تقبل بدون الدعوى، فلو شهد الشهود بدار لرجل فقالوا هذا البيت من هذه الدار لفلان رجل آخر غير المدعي فقال المدعي ليس هو لي فقد أكذب شهوده، وإن قال هذا قبل القضاء لا يقضى له ولا لفلان بشيء، فإن كان بعد القضاء فقال هذا البيت لم يكن لي إنما هو لفلان قال أبو يوسف أجزت إقراره لفلان وجعلت له البيت وأراد ما بقي من الدار على المقضى عليه ويضمن قيمة البيت للمشهود عليه، ولأبي يوسف قول آخر أنه يضمن قيمة البيت للمشهود عليه ويكون ما بقي من الدار للمشهود له؛ كذا في الخانية. ثم اعلم أن المدعي إذا كذب شهوده إنما ترد شهادتهم إذا كذبهم فيما وقعت الدعوى به، أما إذا صدقهم فيها وكذبهم في شيء زادوه فإنها تقبل له فيما ادعاه إن لم يدعه المدعى عليه، وعلى هذا قال في الخانية : شهد الرجل أن فلاناً غصب عبده ولكنه قد رده عليه بعده فمات عنده مولاه فقال المغصوب منه لم يرده علي وإنما مات عند الغاصب وقال المشهود عليه ما غصبته عبداً ولا رددته عليه وما كان هذا من شيء قال : إذا لم يدع شهادتهما ضمنته القيمة. وكذا لو شهدا أنه غصبه عبداً له فجاء مولاه قتله عند الغاصب فقال المغصوب منه ما قتلته ولكنه قد غصبه ومات عنده وقال المشهود عليه ما غصبته عبداً ولا قتل المدعي عبداً له في يدي كان عليه قيمته، وكذا لو شهدا أن لهذا علي هذا ألف درهم ولكنه قد أبرأه منها وقال المدعي ما أبرأته عن شيء وقال المشهود عليه ما كان له علي شيء ولا أبرأني عن شيء قال : إذا لم يدع شهادتهما على البراءة قضيت عليه بالألف ا هـ .
The author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated that if the claimant discredits his witnesses regarding all or part of what they testified for him, their testimony becomes invalid, either because it is a declaration of sinfulness (tafsiq) of the witness or because testimony is not accepted without a claim. So if witnesses testified for a man regarding a house, and they said: 'This room of this house belongs to another man, not the claimant,' and the claimant said: 'It is not mine,' then he has discredited his witnesses. If he said this before judgment, nothing is decreed for him or for the other man. If after judgment he said: 'This room was never mine; it belongs to So-and-so,' Abu Yusuf said: 'I validate his acknowledgment for So-and-so, give him the room, and the rest of the house remains against the defendant, and he (the claimant) guarantees the value of the room to the person against whom judgment was given.' Abu Yusuf has another opinion: that he guarantees the value of the room to the person against whom judgment was given, and the rest of the house belongs to the claimant. Similarly in al-Khaniyya. Then know that if the claimant discredits his witnesses, their testimony is only rejected if he discredits them regarding that which the claim was made. If he affirms them in that but discredits them in something extra, then it is accepted for what he claimed, provided the defendant does not claim that extra. On this basis, it is said in al-Khaniyya: A man testified that So-and-so usurped his slave, but later returned him to him, and then the slave died in the possession of his master (the original owner). The victim (the person from whom the slave was usurped) said: 'He did not return him to me; rather he died with the usurper.' The defendant said: 'I did not usurp any slave nor return him to him; none of this happened.' He said: If he did not claim their testimony regarding the return, I would hold him liable for the value. Similarly, if they testified that he usurped his slave and then his (the owner's) master came and killed him in the presence of the usurper, and the victim said: 'I did not kill him, but he did usurp him and he died with him,' and the defendant said: 'I did not usurp a slave nor did the claimant kill a slave of mine in my possession' – he would be liable for his value. Similarly, if they testified that this man owes this man a thousand dirhams but he has released him from it, and the claimant said: 'I did not release him from anything,' and the defendant said: 'He owed me nothing and did not release me from anything,' he said: If he does not claim their testimony regarding the release, I would decree the thousand against him. End.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage deals with the consequences of the claimant discrediting (takdhib) his own witnesses. The author first states a general rule: if the claimant discredits his witnesses wholly or partially, their testimony is invalidated. This is because discrediting implies the witnesses are sinful (tafsiq) or because testimony requires a claim that the claimant now contradicts. Two scenarios are distinguished: before judgment and after judgment. Before judgment, if the claimant says something like 'this room is not mine,' contradicting his witnesses, no judgment is made for him or for any third party. After judgment, the situation is more complex: the claimant's acknowledgment may be treated as an admission that benefits a third party, but he must compensate the original defendant. Abu Yusuf offers two opinions on whether the remaining property goes to the claimant or the defendant. The passage then clarifies that discrediting only invalidates testimony regarding the point of the claim. If the claimant confirms the witnesses on the claimed amount but disputes something extra they added, the testimony is accepted for the claimed amount unless the defendant also claims that extra. Several examples from al-Khaniyya illustrate this: in cases of usurpation, if the claimant denies that the slave was returned, the witnesses' testimony about the return is disregarded, and the defendant is liable for the value. Similarly, in debt cases, if the claimant denies release, the original debt is upheld.

Key Terms
تكذيب (takdhib): The claimant's statement that contradicts or denies what his witnesses have testified, thereby discrediting them.
تفسيق (tafsiq): Declaring a witness to be sinful (fasiq), which makes his testimony rejected in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case where witnesses testify that the defendant owes 1000 dirhams and has been released from it, the claimant says 'I did not release him.' What is the ruling?
A) The testimony about the release is accepted, and the debt is waived.
B) The claimant's denial of release is a discrediting, so the entire testimony is rejected.
C) The testimony about the debt is accepted, and the defendant must pay, because the claimant did not discredit the debt claim.
D) The case is dismissed due to contradiction.

Key Takeaway
The claimant's discrediting of witnesses only invalidates the testimony on the specific point denied; the core claim remains valid if not discredited.

Ambiguous Discrediting and Post-Judgment Acknowledgment
Ruling on ambiguous statements by the claimant that may discredit witnesses, before and after judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ambiguous and definitive discrediting of witnesses and state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a judgment after each case.

Core Idea
A judgment stands after ambiguous discrediting; only definitive takdhib invalidates it.

When a claimant makes a statement that could discredit his witnesses, the timing and certainty matter. Before judgment, the case is dismissed. After judgment, the ruling remains valid unless the claimant's words are unequivocally a discrediting. This lesson examines the nuanced rules of takdhib and the effect of acknowledgment after judgment, drawing on key Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing
Determine whether the ambiguous statement occurs before or after the judge's ruling. This is the primary factor in the ruling.
Before judgment: case is not decided. After judgment: existing ruling may or may not be invalidated.
2
Assess certainty of discrediting
If after judgment, evaluate whether the statement is definitively a discrediting (takdhib qat'i) or could bear another interpretation. Only definitive statements invalidate.
Ambiguity preserves the judgment.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the examples: (1) Claimant says house belongs to another after winning a case – possible interpretations preserve judgment. (2) Claimant says building on property is not his but defendant's – if witnesses mentioned building, it is takdhib and judgment invalidated.
The distinction hinges on whether the statement contradicts the basis of the claim (the witnesses' testimony).
4
Analyze combined acknowledgment and negation
If the claimant says 'To So-and-so, it was never mine,' the judgment's fate depends on whether the acknowledged party affirms or denies, and whether the statement is connected or disconnected.
Connected statement (nataqa bi al-nafy wa al-iqrar bi al-wasl) vs. disconnected (fasl) has different rules.
5
Examine partial receipt acknowledgment
If claimant acknowledges receiving part of a claimed amount after winning, the effect depends on whether the receipt was before or after the claim/witnesses. If before, it discredits the witnesses; if after, it does not.
The timing of the receipt relative to the claim is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن المدعي إذا تكلم بكلام يحتمل أن يكون تكذيباً فإن كان قبل القضاء لا يقضى له، وإن كان بعده لم يبطل إلا أن يكون تكذيباً للشاهد قطعاً، فلو قضى له بالدار بالبينة فأقر أنها لرجل غير المقضى عليه لا حق للمدعي فيها وصدقه فلان أو كذبه لم يبطل القضاء لاحتمال النفي من الأصل واحتمال أنه ملكها إياه بعد القضاء، وإن كان في مجلس القضاء فلا يبطل بالشك، فلو قال بعد القضاء لفلان لم تكن لي قط فإن بدأ بالإقرار وثنى بالنفي أو عكسه فإن صدقه المقر له في الجميع بطل القضاء ويرد على المقضى عليه ولا شيء للمقر له، وإن كذبه في النفي وصدقه في الإقرار كان للمقر له وضمن المقر قيمة الدار للمقضى عليه، سواء بدأ بالإقرار أو بالنفي؛ كذا ذكر في الجامع . قالوا : هذا إذا بدأ بالنفي وثنى بالإقرار موصولاً، أما إذا كان مفصولاً لم يصح وتمامه في الخانية بخلاف المقر له إذا قال لفلان ما كان لي قط لأن للثالث فيسلم له وهنا المقضى عليه ينازعه ؛ كذا في التلخيص . وفي المحيط البرهاني: قضى له بالدار ببنائها ببينة ثم قال ليس البناء لي وإنما هو للمدعى عليه بطل القضاء لأنه إكذاب للشاهد بخلاف ما إذا قال البناء له فليس بإكذاب في الأقضية. وفرق بين ما إذا ذكروا البناء في شهادتهم فيكون إكذاباً أو لا فلا في شهادات الأصل، وإذا ذكروه فلا فرق بين النفي والإثبات فقط في كونه تكذيباً. ولو ادعى قدراً وبرهن عليه ثم أقر بقبض بعضه فإن أقر بما يدل على قبضه قبل الدعوى والبينة فهو تكذيب لشهوده وإلا فلا ولو ادعى أربعمائة درهم وقضى له ببينة ثم أقر أن للمدعى عليه
Then know that if the claimant speaks words that could be a discrediting, if it is before judgment, no judgment is given for him; if after judgment, it does not invalidate unless it is definitely a discrediting of the witness. So if judgment was given to him for the house by evidence, and then he acknowledged that it belongs to someone other than the defendant – there is no right for the claimant in it, and whether that person affirms or denies, the judgment is not invalidated because of the possibility of negation from the beginning and the possibility that he owned it to him after the judgment. Even if it was in the court session, it is not invalidated by doubt. So if he said after judgment: 'To So-and-so, it was never mine' – if he began with acknowledgment and then with negation, or vice versa, if the acknowledged-to person affirms it all, the judgment is invalidated and is returned to the defendant, and nothing for the acknowledged-to person. If he denies the negation but affirms the acknowledgment, then it belongs to the acknowledged-to person, and the acknowledger guarantees the value of the house to the defendant, whether he began with acknowledgment or negation; thus mentioned in al-Jami'. Its completion is in al-Khaniyya, unlike the case where the acknowledged-to person says: 'It was never mine for So-and-so' because there is a third party, so it is valid; here the defendant disputes. Thus in al-Talkhis. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani: Judgment was given for him for the house with its building by evidence, then he said: 'The building is not mine; it belongs to the defendant' – the judgment is invalidated because it is a discrediting of the witness, unlike if he said: 'The building is his' – it is not a discrediting in judgments. And a distinction is made between whether they mentioned the building in their testimony – then it is a discrediting – or not – then it is not a discrediting in original testimonies. And if they mentioned it, there is no difference between negation and affirmation only in being a discrediting. And if he claimed an amount and proved it, then acknowledged receipt of part of it, if his acknowledgment indicates receipt before the claim and evidence, it is a discrediting of his witnesses; otherwise not. Even if he claimed four hundred dirhams and judgment was given to him by evidence, then he acknowledged that the defendant has
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage addresses situations where the claimant makes a statement that could be interpreted as discrediting his witnesses but is ambiguous. The key distinction is timing: if the ambiguous statement occurs before judgment, no judgment is given. If after judgment, the judgment remains valid unless the statement is a definitive discrediting (takdhib qat'i). Examples are given: if after winning a house case, the claimant says the house belongs to a third party, the judgment stands because of possible interpretations (the claimant might have owned it after judgment or negated ownership from the beginning). However, if the claimant's words clearly negate his ownership from the start, the judgment is nullified, but careful rules apply when the statement combines acknowledgment and negation. The passage also cites al-Muhit al-Burhani regarding a building on the property: if the claimant denies ownership of the building, and the witnesses mentioned the building, it discredits them and invalidates the judgment; if the witnesses did not mention the building, it does not. Finally, it discusses acknowledgment of partial receipt: if the acknowledgment indicates receipt before the claim, it discredits the witnesses; if after, it does not. The text ends abruptly but covers the main rules.

Key Terms
إكذاب (ikdhab): A definitive discrediting of the witness that invalidates the testimony and, if done after judgment, may nullify the judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The judgment is voided only if Zaid confirms the claim.
D) The judgment stands and the claimant is ordered to pay the defendant.

Key Takeaway
After judgment, only a definitive discrediting of witnesses by the claimant invalidates the ruling; ambiguous statements preserve the judgment due to possible alternative interpretations.

Ruling on Plaintiff Denying His Witnesses
States ruling and gives three examples from al-Khaniya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a plaintiff's denial of his witnesses' testimony regarding the subject of the claim invalidates the testimony, but denial of an additional detail does not, using the examples from al-Khaniya.

Core Idea
A plaintiff's denial of an added detail does not invalidate the testimony; it stands for the original claim.

This lesson addresses a subtle but important point in Hanafi courtroom procedure: what happens when the plaintiff calls witnesses and then contradicts part of their testimony. The general rule is that if the plaintiff denies the very subject of the claim, the testimony is rejected. However, if he only denies an additional element added by the witnesses, the testimony remains valid for the original claim. We will examine the ruling and three illustrative cases from al-Khaniya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and the denial
First, determine what the plaintiff originally claimed and what part of the testimony he denied. Is the denial on the subject of the lawsuit or on a supplementary fact?
The subject of the claim is the core right the plaintiff seeks to prove.
2
Distinguish between denial of the claim and denial of an addition
If the plaintiff denies the very thing he sued for (e.g., 'I never claimed he owed me money'), that is a denial of the claim. If he confirms the claim but denies an extra fact the witnesses added (e.g., 'I did not discharge him'), that is a denial of an addition.
This distinction is critical for the ruling.
3
Apply the rule
If the denial is of the claim, the testimony is rejected entirely. If the denial is of an addition, the testimony is accepted for the original claim.
This rule is based on the principle that the plaintiff's denial of an addition does not contradict the core claim.
4
Verify with the examples
Work through each of the three examples from al-Khaniya. For each, identify the claim, the addition, and what the plaintiff denied. Confirm that the ruling matches the stated rule.
The examples are: (1) witness adds return of slave, (2) witness adds killing, (3) witness adds discharge. In all, plaintiff denies only the addition.
5
Consider the defendant's position
Note that the testimony is accepted only if the defendant does not also claim the addition. In the examples, the defendant denies everything, so the addition becomes irrelevant.
If the defendant also claimed the addition, it would be a separate matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
۱۷۷
هذا
كذا في الخانية. ثم اعلم أن المدعي إذا كذب شهوده إنما ترد شهادتهم إذا كذبهم فيما وقعت الدعوى به، أما إذا صدقهم فيها وكذبهم في شيء زادوه فإنها تقبل له فيما ادعاه إن لم يدعه المدعى عليه، وعلى هذا قال في الخانية : شهد الرجل أن فلاناً غصب عبده ولكنه قد رده عليه بعده فمات عنده مولاه فقال المغصوب منه لم يرده علي وإنما مات عند الغاصب وقال المشهود عليه ما غصبته عبداً ولا رددته عليه وما كان هذا من من شيء ء قال : إذا لم يدع شهادتهما ضمنته القيمة. وكذا لو شهدا أنه غصبه عبداً له فجاء مولاه قتله عند الغاصب فقال المغصوب منه ما قتلته ولكنه قد غصبه ومات عنده وقال المشهود عليه ما غصبته عبداً ولا قتل المدعي عبداً له في يدي كان عليه قيمته، وكذا لو شهدا أن لهذا علي هذا ألف درهم ولكنه قد أبرأه منها وقال المدعي ما أبرأته عن شيء وقال المشهود عليه ما كان له علي شيء ولا أبرأني عن شيء قال : إذا لم يدع شهادتهما على البراءة قضيت عليه بالألف ا هـ .
Chapter of Testimonies: Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony. 177. This is as in al-Khaniya. Then know that if the plaintiff denies his witnesses, their testimony is only rejected if he denies them regarding that which the claim was made. As for if he confirms them regarding that and denies them regarding something they added, then it is accepted for him regarding what he claimed, if the defendant does not claim it. According to this, it is said in al-Khaniya: A man testified that so-and-so usurped his slave but then returned it to him afterwards, and then his master died with him. The one from whom the slave was taken said: 'He did not return it to me; rather he died with the usurper.' The one against whom testimony was given said: 'I did not usurp a slave nor return it to him; this was nothing.' He said: If he does not deny their testimony, he is liable for its value. Similarly, if they testified that he usurped a slave belonging to him, and then his master came and killed him with the usurper, and the one from whom the slave was taken said: 'I did not kill him, but he usurped him and he died with him,' and the one against whom testimony was given said: 'I did not usurp a slave from him, nor did the plaintiff kill a slave belonging to him in my possession,' then he is liable for its value. Similarly, if they testified that this person owes that person a thousand dirhams but he has discharged him from it, and the plaintiff said: 'I did not discharge him from anything,' and the one against whom testimony was given said: 'I did not owe him anything nor did he discharge me from anything,' he said: If he does not deny their testimony regarding the discharge, I will rule against him for the thousand.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a ruling expansion from al-Khaniya on the effect of a plaintiff's statements regarding his witnesses. The general rule: if the plaintiff denies his witnesses regarding the very matter of the claim (i.e., the subject of the lawsuit), their testimony is rejected. But if he confirms them on the claim and only denies an additional element they added, the testimony is accepted for what he claimed, provided the defendant does not also claim that additional element. Three examples illustrate this: (1) A witness testifies that X usurped Y's slave but later returned it; the plaintiff denies the return, while the defendant denies everything. The testimony is accepted against the defendant because the plaintiff's denial is only of the return (an addition), not of the usurpation. (2) Similar case with killing after usurpation. (3) A witness testifies that the defendant owes the plaintiff 1000 dirhams but the plaintiff discharged him; the plaintiff denies the discharge. Again, the testimony is accepted for the debt because the denial is of the discharge (addition), not of the debt. These are classic Hanafi rulings on the effect of partial denial.

Key Terms
تكذيب الشهود (takhdhib al-shuhud): The plaintiff declaring that his witnesses are false in their testimony regarding the subject matter.
المدعي (al-mudda'i): The one who claims a right from another in court.
المشهود عليه (al-mashhud 'alayh): The defendant against whom testimony is given.
البراءة (al-bara'ah): Discharge or release from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the plaintiff confirms his witnesses regarding the original claim but denies an additional detail they mentioned, what is the ruling?
A) The entire testimony is rejected.
B) The testimony is accepted only for the original claim.
C) The testimony is accepted only for the additional detail.
D) The plaintiff must produce new witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The plaintiff's denial of an additional detail in his witnesses' testimony does not invalidate the testimony for the original claim.

Effect of Plaintiff's Ambiguous Speech and Post-Judgment Acknowledgment
Explains when ambiguous words by plaintiff affect judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that only a clear, unambiguous denial by the plaintiff invalidates a post-judgment, and evaluate scenarios involving contradictory acknowledgments.

Core Idea
Only a clear denial by the plaintiff can overturn a judgment; ambiguous words do not.

This passage from al-Talkhis and al-Jami' clarifies the nuanced rulings on a plaintiff's statements before and after a judgment. The key principle is the finality of judicial decisions: ambiguous words or statements that can be interpreted in multiple ways do not disrupt a judgment. Only a direct, unambiguous denial (takdhib qat') or a contradictory acknowledgment confirmed by the third party can invalidate it. We will dissect the rules by timing and content of the plaintiff's speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify timing of statement
Determine whether the plaintiff's statement was made before or after judgment. Before judgment, any ambiguous statement prevents judgment; after judgment, the judgment stands unless clear denial.
Before judgment: no judgment given; after: judgment usually stands.
2
Determine if statement is a definite denial
If after judgment, only a clearly unambiguous denial (takdhib qat') invalidates. Ambiguous statements like 'I have no right' are not enough.
Ambiguity allows alternative interpretations that do not contradict the judgment.
3
Analyze contradictory acknowledgment and negation
If plaintiff makes both acknowledgment to a third party and negation of his own right, check the third party's response. If he confirms both, judgment is invalidated. If he confirms only the acknowledgment, the acknowledgment stands and plaintiff must compensate defendant.
Order (acknowledgment then negation or vice versa) does not matter.
4
Check connectedness condition
The statements must be connected (not separated by other speech) for the invalidation to take effect. If disconnected, they are disregarded.
Connectedness is essential for the contradictory effect.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Work through the examples given in the passage: the house case, the acknowledgment to Zaid, etc. Ensure you can predict outcomes based on the rules.
Practice with different phrasings to master the nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن المدعي إذا تكلم بكلام يحتمل أن يكون تكذيباً فإن كان قبل القضاء لا يقضى له، وإن كان بعده لم يبطل إلا أن يكون تكذيباً للشاهد قطعاً، فلو قضى له بالدار بالبينة فأقر أنها لرجل غير المقضى عليه لا حق للمدعي فيها وصدقه فلان أو كذبه لم يبطل القضاء لاحتمال النفي من الأصل واحتمال أنه ملكها إياه بعد القضاء، وإن كان في مجلس القضاء فلا يبطل بالشك، فلو قال بعد القضاء لفلان لم تكن لي قط فإن بدأ بالإقرار وثنى بالنفي أو عكسه فإن صدقه المقر له في الجميع بطل القضاء ويرد على المقضى عليه ولا شيء للمقر له، وإن كذبه في النفي وصدقه في الإقرار كان للمقر له وضمن المقر قيمة الدار للمقضى عليه، سواء بدأ بالإقرار أو بالنفي؛ كذا ذكر في الجامع . قالوا : هذا إذا بدأ بالنفي وثنى بالإقرار موصولاً، أما إذا كان مفصولاً لم يصح وتمامه في الخانية بخلاف المقر له إذا قال لفلان ما كان لي قط لأن للثالث فيسلم له وهنا المقضى عليه ينازعه؛ كذا في التلخيص .
Then know that if the plaintiff speaks words that could be a denial: if it is before the judgment, no judgment is given for him; if it is after, the judgment is not invalidated unless it is a definite denial of the witness. So if judgment was given for him for the house by evidence, and then he acknowledged that it belongs to a man other than the one against whom judgment was given, and that the plaintiff has no right in it, and so-and-so confirmed him or denied him, the judgment is not invalidated due to the possibility of original negation and the possibility that he owned it to him after the judgment. Even if it was in the council of judgment, it is not invalidated by doubt. So if after judgment he said: 'To so-and-so, it was never mine,' then if he began with acknowledgment and followed with negation or vice versa, and the acknowledged one confirmed him in everything, the judgment is invalidated and it is returned to the one against whom judgment was given, and nothing belongs to the acknowledged one. If he denied the negation and confirmed the acknowledgment, then it belongs to the acknowledged one, and the acknowledger guarantees the value of the house to the one against whom judgment was given, whether he began with acknowledgment or negation. This is mentioned in al-Jami'. They said: This is if he began with negation and followed with acknowledgment in a connected manner; but if it was disconnected, it does not take effect. And its completion is in al-Khaniya, unlike the case where the acknowledged one says: 'To so-and-so, it was never mine,' because the third party [takes it] and it is surrendered to him, and here the one against whom judgment was given disputes it. So it is in al-Talkhis.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from al-Talkhis and al-Jami' deals with the effect of a plaintiff's ambiguous statements that could be interpreted as denial of his witnesses. The key distinction is timing: (1) Before judgment: if the plaintiff says something ambiguous, no judgment is given because the testimony is now doubtful. (2) After judgment: the judgment remains valid unless the statement is clearly a denial of the witness (i.e., unambiguous). For example, if after winning a case for a house, the plaintiff says 'this house belongs to X, and I have no right in it,' his statement is ambiguous because it could mean it was always X's or that he later transferred it. Thus, the judgment stands. (3) If the plaintiff makes a contradictory statement acknowledging ownership to someone else while also denying that he ever owned it: if he acknowledges and then denies, or denies and then acknowledges, and the acknowledged party confirms both, the judgment is invalidated because the plaintiff's acknowledgment contradicts the basis of the judgment. If the acknowledged party confirms the acknowledgment but denies the negation, the acknowledgment stands and the plaintiff must compensate the original defendant. The passage also notes a nuance about connected vs. disconnected statements, and a distinction between the plaintiff and a third party acknowledging.

Key Terms
تكذيباً قطعاً (takhdhiban qat'an): A definite and unambiguous denial of the witness's truthfulness.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): An admission or acknowledgment of a fact or right.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor an acknowledgment is made.
المقضى عليه (al-maqdi 'alayh): The person against whom a judgment has been passed (the original defendant).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the plaintiff wins a case for a house, and afterwards says 'the house is for Zaid, and I have no right in it,' what happens to the judgment?
A) The judgment is invalidated immediately.
B) The judgment remains valid because the statement is ambiguous.
C) The plaintiff must pay compensation.
D) The witnesses must be re-examined.

Key Takeaway
Only a clear, unambiguous denial by the plaintiff after judgment can overturn it; ambiguous statements or those that can be interpreted in multiple ways leave the judgment intact.

The General Rule on Discrepancy in Testimony
Provides the overarching rule and its rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on discrepancy between claim and testimony and apply it to identify whether testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony less than claim is accepted; testimony more than claim is rejected unless plaintiff disowns the excess.

In legal proceedings, the testimony of witnesses must match the claim. But what happens when they differ? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: the key is whether the testimony exceeds the claim or falls short. This lesson explores the foundational principle through examples from classical fatwa collections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
From the concluding remarks of the passage, extract the overarching principle: testimony that is less than the claim is accepted; testimony that is more is rejected.
The passage states: 'the discrepancy that prevents is that the testified amount is more... every case of acceptance despite discrepancy is because the testified amount is less.'
2
Apply the rule to a simple example
Consider the case of a claim for 1000 dirhams and testimony for 500 dirhams. Following the rule, the testimony is accepted for 500.
This is the default Hanafi position.
3
Identify exceptions
The passage mentions 23 'exceptional' cases where testimony differs but is accepted. Recognize that these are not true exceptions because the testified amount is always less.
Examples include emancipation of a slave-girl and divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط البرهاني: قضى له بالدار ببنائها ببينة ثم قال ليس البناء لي وإنما هو للمدعى عليه بطل القضاء لأنه إكذاب للشاهد بخلاف ما إذا قال البناء له فليس بإكذاب في الأقضية. وفرق بين ما إذا ذكروا البناء في شهادتهم فيكون إكذاباً أو لا فلا في شهادات الأصل، وإذا ذكروه فلا فرق بين النفي والإثبات فقط في كونه تكذيباً. ولو ادعى قدراً وبرهن عليه ثم أقر بقبض بعضه فإن أقر بما يدل على قبضه قبل الدعوى والبينة فهو تكذيب لشهوده وإلا فلا ولو ادعى أربعمائة درهم وقضى له ببينة ثم أقر أن للمدعى عليه المقولة الآتية عند مسألة دعوى النتاج وتأمله قوله : (ليس هو لي لعله له قوله : (إن لم يدعه المدعى عليه) يعني إن لم يدع الزائد لا ما ادعاه المدعي وإن أوهمه كلامه يظهر ذلك من التأمل في المسائل الآتية . وفي المحيط : شهدا له على رجل بألف وعلى آخر بمائة فصدقهم في الأول وكذبهم في الثاني بطلتا، وكذا لو شهدا بغصب ثوبين فصدقهما في أحدهما وكذبهما في الآخر بطلت فيهما، ولو قضى لثلاثة بميراث عن أبيهم ثم قال أحدهم مالي فيه حق وإنما هو لأخوي كان الكل لهما، فإن قال لم يكن لي فيه حق وإنما هو لهما بطلت حصته المقضى عليه ولو ادعى أنه أوصى له بألف درهم وبرهن عليه ثم ادعى أنه ابن الموصي ولم يبرهن فله الأقل من الميراث ومن الألف. وقال محمد: الوصية باطلة ولا شيء وفي البزازية : ادعى المديون الإيفاء فشهدا على إبراء الدائن أو على أنه حاله تقبل كما لو ادعى الغصب فشهدا على الإقرار به تقبل ادعى الكفيل بالأمر الإيفاء وشهدا على البراءة تقبل. ووضع المسألة على الإيفاء ليعلم أن الإيفاء غير مقتصر عليه ولهذا لا يرجع الكفيل على الأصيل ويرجع الطالب على الأصيل كأنه إبراء الكفيل وإبراء الكفيل لا يوجب إبراء الأصيل. وإنما ذكره ليؤذن أن المقضى به براءة الكفيل لا الإيفاء، وهذا لأن دعوى الكفيل تتضمن البراءة مع تمكنه بالرجوع على الأصيل وشاهداه شهدا على القطع ببعض دعواه فيقبل في ذلك لا في الزائد ا هـ . وفي السراجية : ادعى عشرة آلاف درهم فشهدا له بمبلغ عشرة آلاف درهم لم تقبل لأن مبلغ هذا المال مال آخر . شهدا على دعوى أرض أنها خمسة مكاييل وأصابا في بيان حدودها وأخطآ في المقدار قبلت ا هـ . وفي العرف أن المبلغ هو القدر فإنهم يقولون قبض مبلغ كذا أي قدر كذا لا مال آخر فينبغي أن تقبل الشهادة في عرفنا. وفي القنية: ادعى المديون الإيصال إلى الدائن متفرقاً وشهد شهوده بالإيصال مطلقاً أو جملة لا تقبل. ادعت على زوجها أنه وكل وكيلاً فطلقني وشهدا أنه طلقها بنفسه يقع الطلاق. ادعت الطلاق فشهدا لأن بالخلع تسمع وجه التوفيق ممكن، ولو ادعى المديون الإبراء وشهدوا أن المدعي صالح المدعى عليه بمال معلوم تقبل شهادتهم إن كان الصلح بجنس الحق لحصول الإبراء عن البعض بالاستيفاء عن البعض بالإسقاط، ولو ادعى عليه خمسة دنانير بوزن سمرقند فشهدوا فسألهم القاضي عن الوزن فقالوا بوزن مكة تقبل شهادتهم إن كان وزن مكة مثل وزن سمرقند أو أقل وإلا فلا ادعت أنها اشترت هذه الجارية من زوجها بمهرها وشهدوا أن زوجها أعطاها مهرها من غير أن يجري البيع بينهما تقبل ا هـ . وبما قررناه علم أن المستثنى من قوله «وإلا لا ثلاث عشرة مسألة وسيأتي قريباً ثمانٍ أخرى في الإقرار والإنشاء، واثنان في المقيد بسبب والمطلق فصارت ثلاثة وعشرين فليتأمل. ثم اعلم أن في الحقيقة لا استثناء لأن المخالفة المانعة أن يكون المشهود به أكثر ففي كل صورة قالوا بالمنع إنما هو لكونه أكثر من المدعي وفي كل موضع قالوا بالقبول مع صورة المخالفة فإنما هو لكون المشهود به أقل وكان كذلك في عتق الجارية وطلاق المرأة يعرف ذلك بالتأمل في كلامهم.
In al-Muhit al-Burhani: He gave judgment for him for the house with its building by evidence, then he said: 'The building is not mine; rather it belongs to the defendant.' The judgment is invalidated because it is a denial of the witness, unlike if he said 'the building is for him' which is not a denial in rulings. And there is a difference between whether they mentioned the building in their testimony (then it is a denial) or not (then it is not). And if they mentioned it, there is no difference between negation and affirmation only in being a denial. And if he claimed a quantity and proved it, then acknowledged receipt of part of it, if his acknowledgment indicates receipt before the claim and evidence, it is a denial of his witnesses; otherwise not. And if he claimed four hundred dirhams and judgment was given for him by evidence, then he acknowledged that the defendant owes [something] ... The following statement in the issue of claiming offspring and its reflection: his statement: 'It is not mine, perhaps it is his' and his statement: 'If the defendant does not claim it' means if he does not claim the excess, not what the plaintiff claimed, even if his words give that impression; this becomes clear from reflection on the following issues. And in al-Muhit: Two witnesses testified for him against a man for a thousand and against another for a hundred, and he confirmed them in the first and denied them in the second - both are invalidated. Similarly, if they testified about the usurpation of two garments, and he confirmed them in one and denied them in the other - both are invalidated. And if judgment was given for three in inheritance from their father, then one of them said: 'I have no right in it; it is only for my two brothers' - the whole is for them. If he said: 'I had no right in it; it is only for them' - his share is invalidated from the judgment. And if he claimed that he was bequeathed a thousand dirhams and proved it, then claimed that he is the son of the testator without proof - he takes the lesser of the inheritance and the thousand. Muhammad said: The bequest is invalid and nothing. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If the debtor claimed payment (ifa') and two witnesses testified to the creditor's discharge (ibra') or that it is his due, it is accepted, as if he claimed usurpation and they testified to an acknowledgment of it, it is accepted. If the guarantor (kafil) by order claimed payment and they testified to discharge, it is accepted. The issue was posed as payment to indicate that payment is not restricted to it; hence the guarantor does not have recourse against the principal, but the claimant has recourse against the principal, as if it were the discharge of the guarantor. And the discharge of the guarantor does not entail the discharge of the principal. He only mentioned it to indicate that the judgment is the discharge of the guarantor, not payment. This is because the claim of the guarantor includes discharge while he has the ability to have recourse against the principal. His two witnesses testified definitively to part of his claim; it is accepted for that, not for the excess. And in al-Sirajiyya: If he claimed ten thousand dirhams and two witnesses testified for him for the amount of ten thousand dirhams, it is not accepted because the amount is another sum of money. If they testified to a claim of land that it is five measures (makayil) and they were correct in describing its boundaries but erred in the amount, it is accepted. And customarily, 'amount' (mablagh) means quantity; they say 'received an amount of such-and-such' meaning a quantity, not another sum of money, so testimony should be accepted according to our custom. And in al-Qunyah: If the debtor claimed delivery (isal) to the creditor in installments and his witnesses testified to delivery in absolute terms or in total, it is not accepted. If a wife claimed that her husband appointed an agent to divorce her, and two witnesses testified that he divorced her himself, the divorce occurs. If she claimed divorce and they testified to khul', it is heard because reconciliation is possible. And if the debtor claimed discharge and they testified that the plaintiff settled with the defendant for a known amount, their testimony is accepted if the settlement was with the same type as the right, because discharge is obtained for part by collection and for part by renunciation. And if he claimed five dinars by the weight of Samarqand, and witnesses testified, and the judge asked them about the weight, and they said 'by the weight of Mecca,' their testimony is accepted if the weight of Mecca equals or is less than the weight of Samarqand; otherwise no. If she claimed that she bought this slave-girl from her husband for her mahr, and witnesses testified that her husband gave her her mahr without any sale taking place between them, it is accepted. By what we have established, it is known that the exceptions from his statement 'otherwise no' are thirteen issues, and soon another eight in acknowledgment and creation, and two in restricted and unrestricted due to cause, making twenty-three - so reflect. Then know that in reality there is no exception, because the discrepancy that prevents is that the testified amount is more. In every case they said it is prevented only because it is more than the plaintiff's claim, and in every place they said acceptance despite discrepancy, it is only because the testified amount is less. And that is the case in the emancipation of a slave-girl and the divorce of a woman; this is known by reflecting on their statements.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage compiles numerous rulings from several Hanafi fatwa collections (al-Muhit al-Burhani, al-Muhit, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Sirajiyya, al-Qunyah) on the topic of discrepancy between the claim (da'wa) and the testimony (shahada). The overarching principle: testimony is accepted if it does not exceed the claim; if it exceeds, it is rejected unless the plaintiff explicitly disowns the excess. However, if the testimony falls short of the claim (e.g., witnesses testify to a lesser amount), it is generally accepted for that lesser amount. The examples cover: (1) Building on a house: denial of ownership of the building after judgment invalidates if witnesses mentioned it. (2) Partial acknowledgment of receipt: if it predates the claim, it is denial. (3) Multiple defendants: if plaintiff confirms testimony for one but denies for another, both are invalidated because it shows untruth. (4) Inheritance: a brother's statement that he has no share affects distribution. (5) Bequest and relationship: conflict between two claims. (6) Guarantor's discharge: testimony accepted for the discharge but does not affect principal. (7) Amount vs. sum: testimony for 'mablagh' (amount) might be rejected if ambiguous. (8) Settlement (sulh): if settlement is with same type, testimony accepted. (9) Weight discrepancy: if witnesses mention a different weight, it's accepted if equal or less. (10) Purchase of slave-girl: testimony about mahr without sale is accepted. The passage concludes with a note that there are 23 exceptional cases where testimony despite discrepancy is accepted, but in reality they are not exceptions because the testified amount is less than the claim.

Key Terms
الإكذاب (al-ikdhab): Declaring a witness false; denial of the truth of testimony. In this context, if the plaintiff's subsequent statement contradicts the testimony, it may invalidate the judgment.
المبلغ (al-mablagh): The total sum or amount; in testimony, if ambiguous, custom may define it as quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A plaintiff claims 1000 dirhams. Witnesses testify that the defendant owes 1200 dirhams. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi rule in this passage?
A) The testimony is accepted for 1200 dirhams.
B) The testimony is rejected entirely.
C) The testimony is accepted for 1000 dirhams only.
D) The plaintiff must amend his claim to 1200 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule on discrepancy is straightforward: testimony less than or equal to the claim is accepted; testimony exceeding the claim is rejected—with no real exceptions.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Cases of Partial Denial and Multiple Witnesses
Applies the rule to specific multi-party and multi-item situations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule on discrepancy to cases involving multiple defendants, partial acknowledgment, and inheritance disputes among heirs.

Core Idea
If a plaintiff confirms testimony for one part and denies for another, both testimonies are invalidated.

When a plaintiff responds to testimony by confirming some witnesses but denying others, or confirms a witness for one defendant but denies the same witness for another, the Hanafi school treats this as a contradiction that undermines the credibility of all testimony. This lesson explores such scenarios from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of multiple defendants
Read the case from al-Muhit: two witnesses testify for the plaintiff against one defendant for 1000 and against another for 100. The plaintiff confirms the first and denies the second.
The text says both testimonies are invalidated.
2
Apply the same logic to similar cases
The same rule applies when witnesses testify about two items (e.g., two garments) and the plaintiff confirms one denial.
Consistency is required; partial confirmation and denial shows the witnesses are unreliable.
3
Understand the inheritance case
When one of three heirs says he has no right to the inheritance, the entire share goes to the others. This is a form of self-denial that affects the distribution.
This is not about testimony but about a party's own statement after judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط البرهاني: قضى له بالدار ببنائها ببينة ثم قال ليس البناء لي وإنما هو للمدعى عليه بطل القضاء لأنه إكذاب للشاهد بخلاف ما إذا قال البناء له فليس بإكذاب في الأقضية. وفرق بين ما إذا ذكروا البناء في شهادتهم فيكون إكذاباً أو لا فلا في شهادات الأصل، وإذا ذكروه فلا فرق بين النفي والإثبات فقط في كونه تكذيباً. ولو ادعى قدراً وبرهن عليه ثم أقر بقبض بعضه فإن أقر بما يدل على قبضه قبل الدعوى والبينة فهو تكذيب لشهوده وإلا فلا ولو ادعى أربعمائة درهم وقضى له ببينة ثم أقر أن للمدعى عليه المقولة الآتية عند مسألة دعوى النتاج وتأمله قوله : (ليس هو لي لعله له قوله : (إن لم يدعه المدعى عليه) يعني إن لم يدع الزائد لا ما ادعاه المدعي وإن أوهمه كلامه يظهر ذلك من التأمل في المسائل الآتية . وفي المحيط : شهدا له على رجل بألف وعلى آخر بمائة فصدقهم في الأول وكذبهم في الثاني بطلتا، وكذا لو شهدا بغصب ثوبين فصدقهما في أحدهما وكذبهما في الآخر بطلت فيهما، ولو قضى لثلاثة بميراث عن أبيهم ثم قال أحدهم مالي فيه حق وإنما هو لأخوي كان الكل لهما، فإن قال لم يكن لي فيه حق وإنما هو لهما بطلت حصته المقضى عليه ولو ادعى أنه أوصى له بألف درهم وبرهن عليه ثم ادعى أنه ابن الموصي ولم يبرهن فله الأقل من الميراث ومن الألف. وقال محمد: الوصية باطلة ولا شيء وفي البزازية : ادعى المديون الإيفاء فشهدا على إبراء الدائن أو على أنه حاله تقبل كما لو ادعى الغصب فشهدا على الإقرار به تقبل ادعى الكفيل بالأمر الإيفاء وشهدا على البراءة تقبل. ووضع المسألة على الإيفاء ليعلم أن الإيفاء غير مقتصر عليه ولهذا لا يرجع الكفيل على الأصيل ويرجع الطالب على الأصيل كأنه إبراء الكفيل وإبراء الكفيل لا يوجب إبراء الأصيل. وإنما ذكره ليؤذن أن المقضى به براءة الكفيل لا الإيفاء، وهذا لأن دعوى الكفيل تتضمن البراءة مع تمكنه بالرجوع على الأصيل وشاهداه شهدا على القطع ببعض دعواه فيقبل في ذلك لا في الزائد ا هـ . وفي السراجية : ادعى عشرة آلاف درهم فشهدا له بمبلغ عشرة آلاف درهم لم تقبل لأن مبلغ هذا المال مال آخر . شهدا على دعوى أرض أنها خمسة مكاييل وأصابا في بيان حدودها وأخطآ في المقدار قبلت ا هـ . وفي العرف أن المبلغ هو القدر فإنهم يقولون قبض مبلغ كذا أي قدر كذا لا مال آخر فينبغي أن تقبل الشهادة في عرفنا. وفي القنية: ادعى المديون الإيصال إلى الدائن متفرقاً وشهد شهوده بالإيصال مطلقاً أو جملة لا تقبل. ادعت على زوجها أنه وكل وكيلاً فطلقني وشهدا أنه طلقها بنفسه يقع الطلاق. ادعت الطلاق فشهدا لأن بالخلع تسمع وجه التوفيق ممكن، ولو ادعى المديون الإبراء وشهدوا أن المدعي صالح المدعى عليه بمال معلوم تقبل شهادتهم إن كان الصلح بجنس الحق لحصول الإبراء عن البعض بالاستيفاء عن البعض بالإسقاط، ولو ادعى عليه خمسة دنانير بوزن سمرقند فشهدوا فسألهم القاضي عن الوزن فقالوا بوزن مكة تقبل شهادتهم إن كان وزن مكة مثل وزن سمرقند أو أقل وإلا فلا ادعت أنها اشترت هذه الجارية من زوجها بمهرها وشهدوا أن زوجها أعطاها مهرها من غير أن يجري البيع بينهما تقبل ا هـ . وبما قررناه علم أن المستثنى من قوله «وإلا لا ثلاث عشرة مسألة وسيأتي قريباً ثمانٍ أخرى في الإقرار والإنشاء، واثنان في المقيد بسبب والمطلق فصارت ثلاثة وعشرين فليتأمل. ثم اعلم أن في الحقيقة لا استثناء لأن المخالفة المانعة أن يكون المشهود به أكثر ففي كل صورة قالوا بالمنع إنما هو لكونه أكثر من المدعي وفي كل موضع قالوا بالقبول مع صورة المخالفة فإنما هو لكون المشهود به أقل وكان كذلك في عتق الجارية وطلاق المرأة يعرف ذلك بالتأمل في كلامهم.
In al-Muhit al-Burhani: He gave judgment for him for the house with its building by evidence, then he said: 'The building is not mine; rather it belongs to the defendant.' The judgment is invalidated because it is a denial of the witness, unlike if he said 'the building is for him' which is not a denial in rulings. And there is a difference between whether they mentioned the building in their testimony (then it is a denial) or not (then it is not). And if they mentioned it, there is no difference between negation and affirmation only in being a denial. And if he claimed a quantity and proved it, then acknowledged receipt of part of it, if his acknowledgment indicates receipt before the claim and evidence, it is a denial of his witnesses; otherwise not. And if he claimed four hundred dirhams and judgment was given for him by evidence, then he acknowledged that the defendant owes [something] ... The following statement in the issue of claiming offspring and its reflection: his statement: 'It is not mine, perhaps it is his' and his statement: 'If the defendant does not claim it' means if he does not claim the excess, not what the plaintiff claimed, even if his words give that impression; this becomes clear from reflection on the following issues. And in al-Muhit: Two witnesses testified for him against a man for a thousand and against another for a hundred, and he confirmed them in the first and denied them in the second - both are invalidated. Similarly, if they testified about the usurpation of two garments, and he confirmed them in one and denied them in the other - both are invalidated. And if judgment was given for three in inheritance from their father, then one of them said: 'I have no right in it; it is only for my two brothers' - the whole is for them. If he said: 'I had no right in it; it is only for them' - his share is invalidated from the judgment. And if he claimed that he was bequeathed a thousand dirhams and proved it, then claimed that he is the son of the testator without proof - he takes the lesser of the inheritance and the thousand. Muhammad said: The bequest is invalid and nothing. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If the debtor claimed payment (ifa') and two witnesses testified to the creditor's discharge (ibra') or that it is his due, it is accepted, as if he claimed usurpation and they testified to an acknowledgment of it, it is accepted. If the guarantor (kafil) by order claimed payment and they testified to discharge, it is accepted. The issue was posed as payment to indicate that payment is not restricted to it; hence the guarantor does not have recourse against the principal, but the claimant has recourse against the principal, as if it were the discharge of the guarantor. And the discharge of the guarantor does not entail the discharge of the principal. He only mentioned it to indicate that the judgment is the discharge of the guarantor, not payment. This is because the claim of the guarantor includes discharge while he has the ability to have recourse against the principal. His two witnesses testified definitively to part of his claim; it is accepted for that, not for the excess. And in al-Sirajiyya: If he claimed ten thousand dirhams and two witnesses testified for him for the amount of ten thousand dirhams, it is not accepted because the amount is another sum of money. If they testified to a claim of land that it is five measures (makayil) and they were correct in describing its boundaries but erred in the amount, it is accepted. And customarily, 'amount' (mablagh) means quantity; they say 'received an amount of such-and-such' meaning a quantity, not another sum of money, so testimony should be accepted according to our custom. And in al-Qunyah: If the debtor claimed delivery (isal) to the creditor in installments and his witnesses testified to delivery in absolute terms or in total, it is not accepted. If a wife claimed that her husband appointed an agent to divorce her, and two witnesses testified that he divorced her himself, the divorce occurs. If she claimed divorce and they testified to khul', it is heard because reconciliation is possible. And if the debtor claimed discharge and they testified that the plaintiff settled with the defendant for a known amount, their testimony is accepted if the settlement was with the same type as the right, because discharge is obtained for part by collection and for part by renunciation. And if he claimed five dinars by the weight of Samarqand, and witnesses testified, and the judge asked them about the weight, and they said 'by the weight of Mecca,' their testimony is accepted if the weight of Mecca equals or is less than the weight of Samarqand; otherwise no. If she claimed that she bought this slave-girl from her husband for her mahr, and witnesses testified that her husband gave her her mahr without any sale taking place between them, it is accepted. By what we have established, it is known that the exceptions from his statement 'otherwise no' are thirteen issues, and soon another eight in acknowledgment and creation, and two in restricted and unrestricted due to cause, making twenty-three - so reflect. Then know that in reality there is no exception, because the discrepancy that prevents is that the testified amount is more. In every case they said it is prevented only because it is more than the plaintiff's claim, and in every place they said acceptance despite discrepancy, it is only because the testified amount is less. And that is the case in the emancipation of a slave-girl and the divorce of a woman; this is known by reflecting on their statements.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage compiles numerous rulings from several Hanafi fatwa collections (al-Muhit al-Burhani, al-Muhit, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Sirajiyya, al-Qunyah) on the topic of discrepancy between the claim (da'wa) and the testimony (shahada). The overarching principle: testimony is accepted if it does not exceed the claim; if it exceeds, it is rejected unless the plaintiff explicitly disowns the excess. However, if the testimony falls short of the claim (e.g., witnesses testify to a lesser amount), it is generally accepted for that lesser amount. The examples cover: (1) Building on a house: denial of ownership of the building after judgment invalidates if witnesses mentioned it. (2) Partial acknowledgment of receipt: if it predates the claim, it is denial. (3) Multiple defendants: if plaintiff confirms testimony for one but denies for another, both are invalidated because it shows untruth. (4) Inheritance: a brother's statement that he has no share affects distribution. (5) Bequest and relationship: conflict between two claims. (6) Guarantor's discharge: testimony accepted for the discharge but does not affect principal. (7) Amount vs. sum: testimony for 'mablagh' (amount) might be rejected if ambiguous. (8) Settlement (sulh): if settlement is with same type, testimony accepted. (9) Weight discrepancy: if witnesses mention a different weight, it's accepted if equal or less. (10) Purchase of slave-girl: testimony about mahr without sale is accepted. The passage concludes with a note that there are 23 exceptional cases where testimony despite discrepancy is accepted, but in reality they are not exceptions because the testified amount is less than the claim.

Key Terms
التصديق والتكذيب (al-tasdiq wa al-takdhib): Confirmation and denial of witnesses by the plaintiff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the inheritance case from al-Muhit, one of three heirs says 'I have no right; it is only for my two brothers.' What is the ruling?
A) His share is void and goes to the other two.
B) The inheritance is divided equally between the three anyway.
C) The statement is ignored as it is after judgment.
D) The two brothers must provide new evidence.

Key Takeaway
Partial confirmation and denial of testimony from the same witnesses leads to full invalidation, preserving consistency in the judicial process.
