Commentary
This final segment covers cases thirteen through twenty-three, focusing on testimonies about acknowledgments, birth, permissions, divorce, and manumission. A key principle is that if witnesses agree on the underlying fact (e.g., taking a slave, acknowledgment of ownership, birth, permission, or divorce) but differ on peripheral details (e.g., the source of the slave, gender of child, specific permission item, or number of divorces), the testimony is accepted for the agreed core, often ruling for the lesser or the common denominator. The thirteenth case: one witness says the defendant acknowledged taking the slave, the other says he acknowledged depositing it; accepted because both agree on acknowledgment of taking. The fourteenth: one says usurpation, the other says deposit; judgment for the plaintiff because both imply ownership. Fifteenth and sixteenth: birth/pregnancy and gender differences are accepted. Seventeenth: acknowledgment of ownership vs. residence; accepted. Eighteenth: explicit permission vs. observed conduct; the latter is not accepted if it contradicts explicit permission. Nineteenth: language differences in acknowledgment of wealth accepted, but not in divorce, because divorce requires precise wording. Twentieth: Arabic 'anta hurr' vs. Persian 'azadi' accepted. Twenty-first and twenty-second: differences in time of condition occurrence and timing of divorce; divorce occurs. The twenty-third case is particularly detailed: if one witnesses to three divorces absolutely and the other to two, the court accepts two divorces, allowing reconciliation. This is distinguished from manumission cases where disagreement on whole vs. half is not accepted. The author explains that in divorce, both witnesses agree on the fact of legal separation (baynuna) though differing on number, whereas in manumission, the difference in quantity changes the nature of the act. Further, a case from al-Uyun illustrates a nuance: if a woman was emancipated and then divorced, testimony that counts one divorce during slavery is invalid, leaving only two divorces after emancipation.

Key Terms
الإقرار بالأخذ (al-iqrār bi-l-akhdh): Acknowledgment of taking possession of an item, which implies some right or liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighteenth case, if one witness testifies that the owner gave explicit permission to the slave for clothes, and the other testifies that he saw the slave buying clothes and the owner remained silent, the testimony is:
A) Accepted because both witnesses agree on permission
B) Not accepted because the second witness infers permission from conduct
C) Accepted only for the explicit part
D) Requires a third witness to be accepted

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony when witnesses agree on the core fact, even if they differ on peripheral details, except when one witness infers permission from conduct.

Testimonies on Divorce, Conditional Divorce, and Manumission (Cases 20-23)
Twentieth to twenty-third cases, including conditional divorce and manumission, with a detailed discussion on number differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for testimony on divorce and manumission when witnesses differ on number or timing, and distinguish the treatment of numerical differences between divorce and manumission.

Core Idea
In divorce testimony, agreement on the fact of divorce suffices; disagreement on number yields the lower number and preserves revocability.

This lesson covers cases twenty through twenty-three, which involve testimonies on divorce, conditional divorce, and manumission. A key distinction emerges: in divorce, two witnesses who agree that a divorce occurred but differ on the number (e.g., two vs. three) lead to a judgment of the lower number, allowing revocability. This is contrasted with manumission, where disagreement on whole vs. half leads to rejection of testimony. The rationale is that in divorce, both witnesses agree on legal separation (baynuna), whereas in manumission, the quantity changes the nature of the act. Additionally, the lesson addresses conditional divorces and a nuanced case from al-Uyun about a slave-wife who was emancipated and then divorced.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the fact agreed upon
In case 23, both witnesses agree that the husband divorced his wife absolutely (al-batta). They disagree only on the number (two vs. three).
2
Apply the rule for peripheral numerical difference
Since the core fact (divorce) is agreed, the testimony is accepted for the lower number (two divorces). The court does not reject the testimony due to the numerical discrepancy.
3
Determine the legal consequence
With two divorces, the husband retains the right to take back his wife during the iddah (raj'a). The marriage is not irrevocably terminated.
4
Contrast with manumission
If one witness testifies to whole manumission and the other to half, the testimony is not accepted because the difference transforms the nature of the act (complete vs. partial freedom). In divorce, both numbers result in legal separation (baynuna), only the revocability differs.
The key illa (legal cause) is that in divorce, both witnesses agree on baynuna, while in manumission, whole and half are different in kind.
5
Analyze the conditional cases
In cases 21 and 22, witnesses differ on the time of the triggering event (morning vs. evening, today vs. yesterday). The condition is considered fulfilled and divorce occurs, because they agree on the occurrence of the event, only the time differs.
Similarly, in the al-Uyun case, the witnesses agree on the fact of divorce, but differ on whether it occurred during slavery or after emancipation; the court accepts the lower number of valid divorces.

الثالثة عشرة شهد أحدهما على إقراره أنه أخذ العبد والآخر على إقراره بأنه أودعه منه هذا العبد تقبل لاتفاقهما على الإقرار بالأخذ الرابعة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنه غصبه منه والآخر أن فلاناً أودع منه هذا العبد يقضى للمدعي ولا يقبل من المدعى عليه بينة بعده لأن الشاهدين شهدا على إقراره بالملك. الخامسة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنها ولدت منه والآخر أنها حبلت منه تقبل . السادسة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنها ولدت منه ذكراً وقال الآخر أنثى تقبل ؛ ؛ كذا في البزازية . السابعة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنه أقر أن الدار له والآخر أنه سكن فيها تقبل. الثامنة عشرة أنكر إذن عبده فشهد أحدهما على أنه أذن له في الثياب والآخر على أنه أذن له في الطعام تقبل بخلاف ما إذا قال أحدهما إنه أذنه صريحاً وقال الآخر رآه يشتري ويبيع فسكت لا تقبل . التاسعة عشرة اختلف شاهدا الإقرار بالمال في كونه أقر بالعربية أو بالفارسية تقبل بخلافه في الطلاق. العشرون شهد أحدهما بأنه قال لعبده أنت حر وقال الآخر قال له آزدي تقبل. الحادية والعشرون قال لامرأته إن كلمت فلاناً فأنت طالق فشهد أحدهما أنها كلمته غدوة والآخر عشية طلقت. الثانية والعشرون إن طلقتك فعبده حر فقال أحدهما طلقها اليوم وقال الآخر أنه طلقها أمس يقع الطلاق والعتاق الثالثة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها ثلاثاً البتة والآخر أنه طلقها ثنتين ألبتة يقضى بطلقتين ويملك الرجعة؛ ذكره في المنتقى عن هشام عن محمد بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما أنه أعتق كله والآخر أنه أعتق نصفه لا تقبل، وعلى هذا ففرق بين الطلقة والطلقتين وبين هذه، والفرق أنهما هنا اتفقا على البينونة لفظاً ومعنى وإن اختلفا في العدد بخلاف تلك. وفي العيون لأبي الليث هشام عن محمد في رجل تحته أمة فأعتقت فشهد عليه شاهدان فقال أحدهما أشهد أنك طلقتها وهي أمة ثلاثاً وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها بعد ما أعتقت ثلاثاً قال : هما تطليقتان فيملك الرجعة لأن الثلاث التي شهد بها في حال الرق واحدة منهما ليست بشيء. ولو شهد
Thirteenth: One witness testified to his acknowledgment that he took the slave, and the other to his acknowledgment that he deposited this slave with him; it is accepted because they agreed on the acknowledgment of taking. Fourteenth: One witness testified that he usurped it from him, and the other that so-and-so deposited this slave with him; judgment is given for the plaintiff, and evidence from the defendant is not accepted afterwards because the two witnesses testified to his acknowledgment of ownership. Fifteenth: One witness testified that she gave birth from him, and the other that she became pregnant from him; it is accepted. Sixteenth: One witness testified that she gave birth from him to a male, and the other said a female; it is accepted; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Seventeenth: One witness testified that he acknowledged that the house is his, and the other that he lived in it; it is accepted. Eighteenth: He denied permission to his slave, so one witness testified that he gave him permission regarding clothes, and the other that he gave him permission regarding food; it is accepted, contrary to when one says that he gave explicit permission, and the other says he saw him buying and selling and remained silent; it is not accepted. Nineteenth: The two witnesses to acknowledgment of wealth differed on whether he acknowledged in Arabic or Persian; it is accepted, contrary to divorce. Twentieth: One witness testified that he said to his slave: 'You are free', and the other said he said to him: 'Azadi' (Persian for free); it is accepted. Twenty-first: He said to his wife: 'If you speak to so-and-so, you are divorced', so one witness testified that she spoke to him in the morning, and the other in the evening; she is divorced. Twenty-second: 'If I divorce you, my slave is free' – one witness said he divorced her today, and the other that he divorced her yesterday; divorce and manumission occur. Twenty-third: One witness testified that he divorced her three times absolutely, and the other that he divorced her two times absolutely; judgment is given for two divorces, and he retains the right to take her back (raj'a); mentioned in al-Muntaqa from Hisham from Muhammad. Contrary to when one witnesses that he manumitted the whole, and the other that he manumitted half; it is not accepted. On this basis, there is a difference between one divorce and two divorces, and between this case and that. The difference is that here they agreed on legal separation (baynuna) in wording and meaning, even if they differed in number, unlike that. And in al-Uyun by Abu al-Layth: Hisham from Muhammad concerning a man who had a slave-wife; she was emancipated, and two witnesses testified against him: one said 'I witness that you divorced her while she was a slave, three times', and the other said 'He divorced her after emancipation, three times'. He said: they are two divorces, and he retains the right to take her back because the three that were witnessed during slavery, one of them is nothing. And if they witnessed...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This final segment covers cases thirteen through twenty-three, focusing on testimonies about acknowledgments, birth, permissions, divorce, and manumission. A key principle is that if witnesses agree on the underlying fact (e.g., taking a slave, acknowledgment of ownership, birth, permission, or divorce) but differ on peripheral details (e.g., the source of the slave, gender of child, specific permission item, or number of divorces), the testimony is accepted for the agreed core, often ruling for the lesser or the common denominator. The thirteenth case: one witness says the defendant acknowledged taking the slave, the other says he acknowledged depositing it; accepted because both agree on acknowledgment of taking. The fourteenth: one says usurpation, the other says deposit; judgment for the plaintiff because both imply ownership. Fifteenth and sixteenth: birth/pregnancy and gender differences are accepted. Seventeenth: acknowledgment of ownership vs. residence; accepted. Eighteenth: explicit permission vs. observed conduct; the latter is not accepted if it contradicts explicit permission. Nineteenth: language differences in acknowledgment of wealth accepted, but not in divorce, because divorce requires precise wording. Twentieth: Arabic 'anta hurr' vs. Persian 'azadi' accepted. Twenty-first and twenty-second: differences in time of condition occurrence and timing of divorce; divorce occurs. The twenty-third case is particularly detailed: if one witnesses to three divorces absolutely and the other to two, the court accepts two divorces, allowing reconciliation. This is distinguished from manumission cases where disagreement on whole vs. half is not accepted. The author explains that in divorce, both witnesses agree on the fact of legal separation (baynuna) though differing on number, whereas in manumission, the difference in quantity changes the nature of the act. Further, a case from al-Uyun illustrates a nuance: if a woman was emancipated and then divorced, testimony that counts one divorce during slavery is invalid, leaving only two divorces after emancipation.

Key Terms
البينونة (al-baynūna): Legal separation between spouses, which may be revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in).
الرجعة (al-raj'a): The right to take back one's wife during the waiting period after a revocable divorce.
البتة (al-batta): An emphasized expression meaning 'absolutely', often used with divorce or manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
One witness testifies that a man divorced his wife three times absolutely, and another testifies two times absolutely. According to the twenty-third case, the court will:
A) Reject both testimonies due to conflict
B) Accept two divorces, allowing the husband to take her back
C) Accept three divorces as the majority
D) Require a third witness

Key Takeaway
In divorce testimony, the court accepts the lower agreed number of divorces, preserving the possibility of reconciliation, unlike in manumission where a numerical difference invalidates the testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
General Rule on Discrepant Testimony (Cases 10-13)
Lists rulings for accepting or rejecting discrepant testimonies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that testimonies differing on legal description are accepted if they agree on the core fact.

Core Idea
Witnesses need not be identical; agreement on the substance suffices.

In Hanafi procedure, the substance of testimony outweighs labels. Cases 10-13 show that as long as witnesses agree that some admission or transaction occurred, their testimony is accepted even if they call it differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core event
For each case, determine what the plaintiff claimed and what the witnesses testified to. Find the common ground.
2
Locate the divergence
Note how the witnesses' statements differ – in type of transaction, language, or description.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
If the divergence does not contradict the core fact, testimony is accepted. If it makes the facts mutually exclusive (e.g., gift vs. charity), it is rejected.
4
State the ruling
For each case, state whether testimony is accepted and explain why based on the principle.

بالفارسي لا تقبل لأن العبرة في الحدود للصورة والمعنى جميعاً احتياطاً للدرء؛ كذا في البزازية . الخامسة والعشرون اختلفا في مقدار المهر يقضى بالأقل كما في البزازية. وفي جامع الفصولين : شهدا ببيع أو إجارة أن تثبت المعينة. ولو شهد بوكالة وزاد أحدهما أنه عزله تقبل في الوكالة لا في العزل، ولو شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بطلاقها وشهد الآخر أنه وكله بطلاقها وطلاق فلانة الأخرى فهو وكيل في طلاق التي اتفقا عليه كذا في جامع الفصولين. السابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما بأنه وقفه في صحته والآخر بأنه وقفه في مرضه قبلاً إذ شهدا بوقف بات إلا أن حكم المرض ينقض فيما لا يخرج من الثلث، وبهذا لا تمنع الشهادة كما لو شهد أحدهما أنه Chapter of Testimony, Section on Discrepancy in Testimony. ... (Cases 10-28): 10th: If he claimed release and one witness testified to it and the other that he gifted or gave charity or made permissible, it is accepted, unlike if one testified to gift and the other to charity, not accepted. 11th: If he claimed a gift and one testified to release and the other to gift or that he made permissible, accepted. 12th: If the surety claimed a gift and one testified to it and the other to release, accepted, and release is proven not gift because it is the lesser, so the surety does not recourse against the principal. 13th: One witness testified to his admission that he took the slave and the other to his admission that he deposited this slave with him, accepted because they agree on the admission of taking. 14th: One testified that he usurped it from him and the other that so-and-so deposited this slave with him, judgment is for the plaintiff and the defendant's evidence is not accepted thereafter because the two witnesses testified to his admission of ownership. 15th: One testified that she gave birth from him and the other that she became pregnant from him, accepted. 16th: One testified that she gave birth to a male and the other said a female, accepted. 17th: One testified that he admitted the house is his and the other that he resided in it, accepted. 18th: He denied permission to his slave, so one testified that he permitted him for clothes and the other that he permitted him for food, accepted, unlike if one said he explicitly permitted and the other said he saw him buying and selling and kept silent, not accepted. 19th: The two witnesses of the admission of wealth differed on whether he admitted in Arabic or Persian, accepted, unlike in divorce. 20th: One witnessed that he said to his slave 'You are free' and the other said he said to him 'Azadi', accepted. 21st: He said to his wife 'If you speak to so-and-so, you are divorced', so one witness said she spoke to him in the morning and the other in the evening, she is divorced. 22nd: 'If I divorce you, my slave is free', so one said he divorced her today and the other said yesterday, divorce and emancipation occur. 23rd: One witness testified that he divorced her three times completely and the other that he divorced her twice completely, judgment is for two divorces and he has the right to take her back; mentioned in al-Muntaqa from Hisham from Muhammad, unlike if one testified that he emancipated all and the other that he emancipated half, not accepted. And upon this there is a difference between one divorce and two and this case, and the difference is that here they agreed on the final separation in wording and meaning although they differed in number, unlike that case. And in al-Uyun of Abu al-Layth: Hisham from Muhammad regarding a man who had a slave woman and she was freed, then two witnesses testified against him: one said 'I witness that you divorced her while she was a slave three times' and the other said 'he divorced her after she was freed three times', he said: they are two divorces and he has the right to take her back because the three which he witnessed in the state of slavery, one of them is nothing. And if a witness testified that so-and-so divorced his wife three times completely and another testified that he divorced her twice completely, they are two divorces with the right to take her back because there is no need for his saying 'completely' in three. 24th: One witness testified that he emancipated in Arabic and the other in Persian, accepted due to agreement in meaning, unlike if one testified that he accused him of fornication in Arabic and the other in Persian, not accepted because in fixed penalties the form and meaning are both considered as a precaution to avert the penalty. 25th: They differed on the amount of the dowry, judgment is for the lesser, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If two witnesses testify to a sale, lease, divorce, or emancipation for a consideration and differ on the amount of the consideration, it is not accepted except in marriage it is accepted and the dowry is referred to the equitable dowry. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not accepted in marriage either. 26th: One witness testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation with so-and-so concerning a named house, and the other testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation about it and about something else, it is accepted for the house they agreed upon, because agency accepts specification, and agency is established in what they agreed upon, not in what one was unique in. So if he claimed a specific agency and they testified to a general agency, it seems that the specific agency should be established. And if they testified to agency and one added that he revoked it, it is accepted in agency but not in revocation. And if one testified that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the other that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the divorce of so-and-so the other, he is an agent for the divorce of the one they agreed upon. 27th: One witness testified that he made a waqf in his health and the other that he made it in his illness, it is accepted since they testified to a confirmed waqf, except that the ruling of illness operates to undo what does not come out of one-third, and by this the testimony is not prevented, just as if one testified that he endowed one-third of his land and the other that he endowed one-quarter, it is accepted. 28th: If one witness testified that he made a will to him on Thursday and another that he made a will to him on Friday, it is valid because speech is not changed by time and place.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates twenty distinct scenarios (cases 10 through 28) under the chapter on discrepancy in testimony. The author, Imam Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents rulings on whether the testimony of two witnesses who differ in certain details is accepted or rejected. The general pattern is that if the witnesses agree on the core event or transaction, their testimony is accepted even if they differ on particulars such as language, time, quantity, or specific description. However, exceptions occur when the difference touches on the essential nature of the act (e.g., gift vs. charity) or when the matter involves fixed penalties (hudud) where strict consistency is required. The cases cover a wide range of topics: debts, gifts, suretyship, possession of slaves, paternity, ownership, permission to a slave, admissions in different languages, conditional divorce, emancipation, agency, waqf, and wills. Each case is a practical illustration of the Hanafi principle that the gist of the testimony must be harmonious even if minor details vary. The text also records an internal Hanafi dispute in case 25 regarding whether testimony on the amount of a dowry is accepted in marriage contracts; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is accepted and the equitable dowry (mahr al-mithl) applies. Students should note that the rationale behind acceptance is that the witnesses agree on the underlying legal cause or admission, and the differences are immaterial to the core fact.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في الشهادة (al-ikhtilaf fi al-shahadah): Discrepancy or difference between two witnesses' testimonies in a court case.
ألبتة (al-battah): Completely, irrevocably — used in divorce to indicate a definitive separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case 10, if one witness testifies to a release and the other to a gift, what is the ruling?
A) Testimony is accepted and release is established.
B) Testimony is rejected.
C) Testimony is accepted only if both use Arabic.
D) Testimony is accepted and gift is established.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony is accepted if witnesses agree on the core fact, even if they differ on its legal description, unless the descriptions are mutually exclusive.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Discrepancies in Status and Ownership (Cases 14-18)
Lists rulings for specific factual scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on accepting testimonies that differ on the origin of ownership or status.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted if witnesses agree on a fact leading to ownership or status, even if they differ on the specific claim.

Cases 14-18 involve disputes over ownership of slaves or property, permission, and paternity. The Hanafi rule consistently accepts testimony if the witnesses agree on an underlying admission of ownership or similar right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying admission
Determine what fact the witnesses agree upon (e.g., admission of ownership, admission of giving birth).
2
Note the divergence
How do the testimonies differ? In source of ownership? In gender of child? In type of permission?
3
Apply the rule
If the divergence does not negate the underlying admission, testimony is accepted.
4
Distinguish exceptions
Case 18 presents an exception: explicit permission vs. silent observation – not accepted.

كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة قرض والآخر بألف وديعة فإنها لا تقبل منها أيضاً. العاشرة ادعى الإبراء فشهد أحدهما به والآخر على أنه وهبه أو تصدق عليه أو حلله جاز بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما على الهبة والآخر على الصدقة لا تقبل؛ كذا في البزازية الحادية عشرة ادعى الهبة فشهد أحدهما بالبراءة والآخر بالهبة أو أنه حلله جاز. الثانية عشرة ادعى الكفيل الهبة فشهد أحدهما بها والآخر بالإبراء جاز ويثبت الإبراء لا الهبة لأنه أقلهما فلا يرجع الكفيل على الأصيل وهما في البزازية. الثالثة عشرة شهد أحدهما على إقراره أنه أخذ العبد والآخر على إقراره بأنه أودعه منه هذا العبد تقبل لاتفاقهما على الإقرار بالأخذ الرابعة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنه غصبه منه والآخر أن فلاناً أودع منه هذا العبد يقضى للمدعي ولا يقبل من المدعى عليه بينة بعده لأن الشاهدين شهدا على إقراره بالملك. الخامسة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنها ولدت منه والآخر أنها حبلت منه تقبل . السادسة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنها ولدت منه ذكراً وقال الآخر أنثى تقبل ؛ كذا في البزازية . السابعة عشرة شهد أحدهما أنه أقر أن الدار له والآخر أنه سكن فيها تقبل. الثامنة عشرة أنكر إذن عبده فشهد أحدهما على أنه أذن له في الثياب والآخر على أنه أذن له في الطعام تقبل بخلاف ما إذا قال أحدهما إنه أذنه صريحاً وقال الآخر رآه يشتري ويبيع فسكت لا تقبل . التاسعة عشرة اختلف شاهدا الإقرار بالمال في كونه أقر بالعربية أو بالفارسية تقبل بخلافه في الطلاق. العشرون شهد أحدهما بأنه قال لعبده أنت حر وقال الآخر قال له آزدي تقبل. الحادية والعشرون قال لامرأته إن كلمت فلاناً فأنت طالق فشهد أحدهما أنها كلمته غدوة والآخر عشية طلقت. الثانية والعشرون إن طلقتك فعبده حر فقال أحدهما طلقها اليوم وقال الآخر أنه طلقها أمس يقع الطلاق والعتاق الثالثة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها ثلاثاً البتة والآخر أنه طلقها ثنتين ألبتة يقضى بطلقتين ويملك الرجعة؛ ذكره في المنتقى عن هشام عن محمد بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما أنه أعتق كله والآخر أنه أعتق نصفه لا تقبل، وعلى هذا ففرق بين الطلقة والطلقتين وبين هذه، والفرق أنهما هنا اتفقا على البينونة لفظاً ومعنى وإن اختلفا في العدد بخلاف تلك. وفي العيون لأبي الليث هشام عن محمد في رجل تحته أمة فأعتقت فشهد عليه شاهدان فقال أحدهما أشهد أنك طلقتها وهي أمة ثلاثاً وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها بعد ما أعتقت ثلاثاً قال : هما تطليقتان فيملك الرجعة لأن الثلاث التي شهد بها في حال الرق واحدة منهما ليست بشيء. ولو شهد شاهد أن فلاناً طلق امرأته ثلاثاً ألبتة وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها اثنتين ألبتة فهما تطليقتان يملك الرجعة لأنه لا يحتاج إلى قوله ألبتة في ثلاث ا هـ . الرابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه أعتق بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي تقبل للاتفاق في المعنى بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما أنه قذفه بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي لا تقبل لأن العبرة في الحدود للصورة والمعنى جميعاً احتياطاً للدرء؛ كذا في البزازية . الخامسة والعشرون اختلفا في مقدار المهر يقضى بالأقل كما في البزازية. وفي جامع الفصولين : شهدا ببيع أو إجارة أو طلاق أو عتق على مال واختلفا في قدر البدل لا تقبل إلا في النكاح تقبل ويرجع في المهر إلى مهر المثل. وقالا : لا تقبل في النكاح أيضاً السادسة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بخصومة مع فلان في دار سماها وشهدا الآخر أنه وكله بخصومة فيه وفي شيء آخر تقبل في دار اجتمعا عليه إذ الوكالة تقبل التخصيص وفيما اتفق عليه الشاهدان تثبت الوكالة لا فيما تفرد به أحدهما فلو ادعى وكالة معينة فشهد بها بوكالة عامة ينبغي أن تثبت المعينة. ولو شهد بوكالة وزاد أحدهما أنه عزله تقبل في الوكالة لا في العزل، ولو شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بطلاقها وشهد الآخر أنه وكله بطلاقها وطلاق فلانة الأخرى فهو وكيل في طلاق التي اتفقا عليه كذا في جامع الفصولين. السابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما بأنه وقفه في صحته والآخر بأنه وقفه في مرضه قبلاً إذ شهدا بوقف بات إلا أن حكم المرض ينقض فيما لا يخرج من الثلث، وبهذا لا تمنع الشهادة كما لو شهد أحدهما أنه وقف ثلث أرضه والآخر أنه وقف ربعها؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين من كتاب الوقف من أحكام المرضى الثامنة والعشرون ولو شهد شاهد أنه أوصى إليه يوم الخميس وآخر أنه أوصى إليه يوم الجمعة جازت لأنها كلام لا يختلف بزمان ومكان؛
Chapter of Testimony, Section on Discrepancy in Testimony. ... (Cases 10-28): 10th: If he claimed release and one witness testified to it and the other that he gifted or gave charity or made permissible, it is accepted, unlike if one testified to gift and the other to charity, not accepted. 11th: If he claimed a gift and one testified to release and the other to gift or that he made permissible, accepted. 12th: If the surety claimed a gift and one testified to it and the other to release, accepted, and release is proven not gift because it is the lesser, so the surety does not recourse against the principal. 13th: One witness testified to his admission that he took the slave and the other to his admission that he deposited this slave with him, accepted because they agree on the admission of taking. 14th: One testified that he usurped it from him and the other that so-and-so deposited this slave with him, judgment is for the plaintiff and the defendant's evidence is not accepted thereafter because the two witnesses testified to his admission of ownership. 15th: One testified that she gave birth from him and the other that she became pregnant from him, accepted. 16th: One testified that she gave birth to a male and the other said a female, accepted. 17th: One testified that he admitted the house is his and the other that he resided in it, accepted. 18th: He denied permission to his slave, so one testified that he permitted him for clothes and the other that he permitted him for food, accepted, unlike if one said he explicitly permitted and the other said he saw him buying and selling and kept silent, not accepted. 19th: The two witnesses of the admission of wealth differed on whether he admitted in Arabic or Persian, accepted, unlike in divorce. 20th: One witnessed that he said to his slave 'You are free' and the other said he said to him 'Azadi', accepted. 21st: He said to his wife 'If you speak to so-and-so, you are divorced', so one witness said she spoke to him in the morning and the other in the evening, she is divorced. 22nd: 'If I divorce you, my slave is free', so one said he divorced her today and the other said yesterday, divorce and emancipation occur. 23rd: One witness testified that he divorced her three times completely and the other that he divorced her twice completely, judgment is for two divorces and he has the right to take her back; mentioned in al-Muntaqa from Hisham from Muhammad, unlike if one testified that he emancipated all and the other that he emancipated half, not accepted. And upon this there is a difference between one divorce and two and this case, and the difference is that here they agreed on the final separation in wording and meaning although they differed in number, unlike that case. And in al-Uyun of Abu al-Layth: Hisham from Muhammad regarding a man who had a slave woman and she was freed, then two witnesses testified against him: one said 'I witness that you divorced her while she was a slave three times' and the other said 'he divorced her after she was freed three times', he said: they are two divorces and he has the right to take her back because the three which he witnessed in the state of slavery, one of them is nothing. And if a witness testified that so-and-so divorced his wife three times completely and another testified that he divorced her twice completely, they are two divorces with the right to take her back because there is no need for his saying 'completely' in three. 24th: One witness testified that he emancipated in Arabic and the other in Persian, accepted due to agreement in meaning, unlike if one testified that he accused him of fornication in Arabic and the other in Persian, not accepted because in fixed penalties the form and meaning are both considered as a precaution to avert the penalty. 25th: They differed on the amount of the dowry, judgment is for the lesser, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If two witnesses testify to a sale, lease, divorce, or emancipation for a consideration and differ on the amount of the consideration, it is not accepted except in marriage it is accepted and the dowry is referred to the equitable dowry. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not accepted in marriage either. 26th: One witness testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation with so-and-so concerning a named house, and the other testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation about it and about something else, it is accepted for the house they agreed upon, because agency accepts specification, and agency is established in what they agreed upon, not in what one was unique in. So if he claimed a specific agency and they testified to a general agency, it seems that the specific agency should be established. And if they testified to agency and one added that he revoked it, it is accepted in agency but not in revocation. And if one testified that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the other that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the divorce of so-and-so the other, he is an agent for the divorce of the one they agreed upon. 27th: One witness testified that he made a waqf in his health and the other that he made it in his illness, it is accepted since they testified to a confirmed waqf, except that the ruling of illness operates to undo what does not come out of one-third, and by this the testimony is not prevented, just as if one testified that he endowed one-third of his land and the other that he endowed one-quarter, it is accepted. 28th: If one witness testified that he made a will to him on Thursday and another that he made a will to him on Friday, it is valid because speech is not changed by time and place.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates twenty distinct scenarios (cases 10 through 28) under the chapter on discrepancy in testimony. The author, Imam Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents rulings on whether the testimony of two witnesses who differ in certain details is accepted or rejected. The general pattern is that if the witnesses agree on the core event or transaction, their testimony is accepted even if they differ on particulars such as language, time, quantity, or specific description. However, exceptions occur when the difference touches on the essential nature of the act (e.g., gift vs. charity) or when the matter involves fixed penalties (hudud) where strict consistency is required. The cases cover a wide range of topics: debts, gifts, suretyship, possession of slaves, paternity, ownership, permission to a slave, admissions in different languages, conditional divorce, emancipation, agency, waqf, and wills. Each case is a practical illustration of the Hanafi principle that the gist of the testimony must be harmonious even if minor details vary. The text also records an internal Hanafi dispute in case 25 regarding whether testimony on the amount of a dowry is accepted in marriage contracts; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is accepted and the equitable dowry (mahr al-mithl) applies. Students should note that the rationale behind acceptance is that the witnesses agree on the underlying legal cause or admission, and the differences are immaterial to the core fact.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في الشهادة (al-ikhtilaf fi al-shahadah): Discrepancy or difference between two witnesses' testimonies in a court case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case 15, what do the witnesses differ on?
A) Whether the child is male or female.
B) Whether the woman gave birth or became pregnant.
C) Whether the child is legitimate.
D) Whether the woman is a slave.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is accepted when witnesses agree on an underlying admission of right or status, even if they describe the source differently.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Discrepancies in Divorce and Emancipation (Cases 19-24)
Lists rulings for specific factual scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on accepting testimonies that differ on the language, time, or number in divorce and emancipation cases.

Core Idea
In divorce and emancipation, agreement on the act itself suffices; differences in language, time, or number within certain limits are acceptable.

Divorce and emancipation are serious matters, yet Hanafi law accepts testimony if the witnesses agree that the act occurred, even if they differ on details like language, time, or number. However, some exceptions exist, such as in fixed penalties (hudud). Cases 19-24 illustrate this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying act
Did the witnesses agree that a divorce or emancipation occurred?
2
Analyze the divergence
Does the difference affect the legal effect? (e.g., different language, different time, different number of divorces)
3
Apply the rule
If the divergence does not change the core fact (e.g., both confirm three divorces but one says 'three' and other says 'three completely'), testimony accepted.
4
Note special case of plural vs singular
If witnesses differ on one vs. two divorces, accepted; if on three vs. two, accepted (case 23). But if on full vs. half emancipation, not accepted because of quantitative difference.

بزمان ومكان؛

unlike if one testified that he emancipated all and the other that he emancipated half, not accepted. And upon this there is a difference between one divorce and two and this case, and the difference is that here they agreed on the final separation in wording and meaning although they differed in number, unlike that case. And in al-Uyun of Abu al-Layth: Hisham from Muhammad regarding a man who had a slave woman and she was freed, then two witnesses testified against him: one said 'I witness that you divorced her while she was a slave three times' and the other said 'he divorced her after she was freed three times', he said: they are two divorces and he has the right to take her back because the three which he witnessed in the state of slavery, one of them is nothing. And if a witness testified that so-and-so divorced his wife three times completely and another testified that he divorced her twice completely, they are two divorces with the right to take her back because there is no need for his saying 'completely' in three. 24th: One witness testified that he emancipated in Arabic and the other in Persian, accepted due to agreement in meaning, unlike if one testified that he accused him of fornication in Arabic and the other in Persian, not accepted because in fixed penalties the form and meaning are both considered as a precaution to avert the penalty. 25th: They differed on the amount of the dowry, judgment is for the lesser, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If two witnesses testify to a sale, lease, divorce, or emancipation for a consideration and differ on the amount of the consideration, it is not accepted except in marriage it is accepted and the dowry is referred to the equitable dowry. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not accepted in marriage either. 26th: One witness testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation with so-and-so concerning a named house, and the other testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation about it and about something else, it is accepted for the house they agreed upon, because agency accepts specification, and agency is established in what they agreed upon, not in what one was unique in. So if he claimed a specific agency and they testified to a general agency, it seems that the specific agency should be established. And if they testified to agency and one added that he revoked it, it is accepted in agency but not in revocation. And if one testified that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the other that he appointed him as agent for her divorce and the divorce of so-and-so the other, he is an agent for the divorce of the one they agreed upon. 27th: One witness testified that he made a waqf in his health and the other that he made it in his illness, it is accepted since they testified to a confirmed waqf, except that the ruling of illness operates to undo what does not come out of one-third, and by this the testimony is not prevented, just as if one testified that he endowed one-third of his land and the other that he endowed one-quarter, it is accepted. 28th: If one witness testified that he made a will to him on Thursday and another that he made a will to him on Friday, it is valid because speech is not changed by time and place.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates twenty distinct scenarios (cases 10 through 28) under the chapter on discrepancy in testimony. The author, Imam Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents rulings on whether the testimony of two witnesses who differ in certain details is accepted or rejected. The general pattern is that if the witnesses agree on the core event or transaction, their testimony is accepted even if they differ on particulars such as language, time, quantity, or specific description. However, exceptions occur when the difference touches on the essential nature of the act (e.g., gift vs. charity) or when the matter involves fixed penalties (hudud) where strict consistency is required. The cases cover a wide range of topics: debts, gifts, suretyship, possession of slaves, paternity, ownership, permission to a slave, admissions in different languages, conditional divorce, emancipation, agency, waqf, and wills. Each case is a practical illustration of the Hanafi principle that the gist of the testimony must be harmonious even if minor details vary. The text also records an internal Hanafi dispute in case 25 regarding whether testimony on the amount of a dowry is accepted in marriage contracts; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is accepted and the equitable dowry (mahr al-mithl) applies. Students should note that the rationale behind acceptance is that the witnesses agree on the underlying legal cause or admission, and the differences are immaterial to the core fact.

Key Terms
ألبتة (al-battah): Completely, irrevocably — used in divorce to indicate a definitive separation.
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): The right of a husband to take back his wife during the waiting period after a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case 23, if one witness testifies to three divorces and another to two, what is the ruling?
A) Testimony rejected.
B) Three divorces occur.
C) Two divorces occur and the husband retains the right to take her back.
D) Two divorces occur but the husband loses the right to take her back.

Key Takeaway
For divorce and emancipation, testimony is accepted if the act is agreed upon; differences in language, time, or number within reason are tolerated.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Discrepancies in Agency, Dowry, Waqf, and Wills (Cases 25-28)
Lists rulings for specific factual scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rules on accepting testimonies that differ on the scope of agency, amount of dowry, timing of waqf, or date of will.

Core Idea
In agency, waqf, and wills, testimony is accepted on agreed elements; in dowry, the lesser amount is taken, with a dispute among Hanafi authorities.

Cases 25-28 cover contracts and dispositions. The Hanafi rules show flexibility: differing on dowry amount leads to the lesser; agency testimony is accepted for the agreed scope; waqf and will testimony is accepted despite differences in time, as long as the core act is confirmed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core transaction
What is the underlying act? (dowry, agency, waqf, will)
2
Analyze the divergence
How do the testimonies differ? In amount, scope, timing?
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
For dowry, accept the lesser amount (case 25) – but note the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. For agency, accept on the agreed scope. For waqf and will, accept even if time differs.
4
Note exceptions
In sale or lease, if witnesses differ on consideration, testimony is rejected (case 25). But for marriage, it is accepted (Abu Hanifa).

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates twenty distinct scenarios (cases 10 through 28) under the chapter on discrepancy in testimony. The author, Imam Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents rulings on whether the testimony of two witnesses who differ in certain details is accepted or rejected. The general pattern is that if the witnesses agree on the core event or transaction, their testimony is accepted even if they differ on particulars such as language, time, quantity, or specific description. However, exceptions occur when the difference touches on the essential nature of the act (e.g., gift vs. charity) or when the matter involves fixed penalties (hudud) where strict consistency is required. The cases cover a wide range of topics: debts, gifts, suretyship, possession of slaves, paternity, ownership, permission to a slave, admissions in different languages, conditional divorce, emancipation, agency, waqf, and wills. Each case is a practical illustration of the Hanafi principle that the gist of the testimony must be harmonious even if minor details vary. The text also records an internal Hanafi dispute in case 25 regarding whether testimony on the amount of a dowry is accepted in marriage contracts; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is accepted and the equitable dowry (mahr al-mithl) applies. Students should note that the rationale behind acceptance is that the witnesses agree on the underlying legal cause or admission, and the differences are immaterial to the core fact.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dowry determined by the bride's peers and family status, used when the specified dowry is disputed or void.
الوكالة (al-wikalah): Agency; authorization to act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case 25, according to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when witnesses differ on the amount of dowry in a marriage?
A) Testimony is rejected entirely.
B) Testimony is accepted and the lesser amount is taken.
C) Testimony is accepted and the equitable dowry applies.
D) Both B and C are possible depending on the source.

Key Takeaway
For marriage, witnesses differing on dowry amount still have their testimony accepted, and the court determines the appropriate dowry (lesser amount or equitable dowry).

Testimony in Different Languages: Manumission vs. Hudud
Ruling on testimony when language differs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony when witnesses use different languages and distinguish between civil and hudud cases.

Core Idea
In hudud, both form and meaning matter—testimony must be identical in wording.

When witnesses testify using different languages (e.g., one Arabic, one Persian), the validity of their testimony depends on the nature of the case. In civil matters like manumission, agreement in meaning suffices. But in hudud punishments, the exact wording is crucial to avoid unjust punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: manumission (civil) and qadhf (hudud). For each, note the ruling on testimony acceptance.
2
State the Hanafi principle for hudud
For hudud, the maxim 'al-ibratu fi al-hududi li al-surati wa al-ma'na jami'an' means both form and meaning are considered. So, different wording invalidates testimony.
This is a precaution (ihtiyat) to avert punishment (dar' al-hudud).
3
Apply the principle to manumission
For manumission, agreement in meaning is sufficient because it is not a hadd case. Thus, testimony in different languages is accepted.
The same would apply to other civil contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه أعتق بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي تقبل للاتفاق في المعنى بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما أنه قذفه بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي لا تقبل لأن العبرة في الحدود للصورة والمعنى جميعاً احتياطاً للدرء؛ كذا في البزازية . الخامسة والعشرون اختلفا في مقدار المهر يقضى بالأقل كما في البزازية.
The twenty-fourth: One witness testified that he manumitted in Arabic and the other in Persian; it is accepted due to agreement in meaning, unlike if one testified that he accused someone of fornication in Arabic and the other in Persian; it is not accepted because in hudud the consideration is both form and meaning, as a precaution to avert punishment. As in al-Bazzaziyyah. The twenty-fifth: They differed on the amount of the dower; judgement is given for the lesser, as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First (Issue 24): In civil matters like manumission, testimony is accepted even if witnesses use different languages (Arabic vs. Persian), as long as the meaning is the same. But in criminal matters (hadd punishment for slander), the exact wording matters, so if one witness uses Arabic and the other Persian, the testimony is not accepted to avoid possible punishment. Second (Issue 25): In a dower dispute, when witnesses disagree on the amount, the judge rules for the lesser amount. This is because the excess is not proven.

Key Terms
العبرة في الحدود للصورة والمعنى جميعاً (al-ibratu fi al-hududi li al-surati wa al-ma'na jami'an): In hudud punishments, both the exact wording and the meaning are considered; testimony must be identical in wording.
احتياطاً للدرء (ihtiyatan li al-dar'i): As a precaution to avert (punishment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony in different languages accepted for manumission but not for qadhf (slander)?
A) Because manumission is more important
B) Because hudud require exact wording to prevent punishment
C) Because Persian is not a valid court language
D) Because witnesses must be fluent in Arabic

Key Takeaway
Testimony in different languages is accepted for civil matters but not for hudud, due to the principle of averting punishment.

Disagreement on Dower Amount
Ruling on dower amount disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when dower amount is disputed, judgement is given for the lesser.

Core Idea
When dower amount is contested, the lesser is taken because the excess is unproven.

In marriage contracts, the dower (mahr) is an essential element. If the spouses disagree on the amount and witnesses differ, which amount should the judge decide? The Hanafi school holds that the lesser amount is taken, as the extra amount is not proven.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The husband and wife disagree on the dower amount. For example, husband says it was 50, wife says 100.
2
Principle of burden of proof
The one claiming the excess must prove it. Since that proof is lacking, the excess is not established.
This aligns with the maxim 'al-asl bara'ah al-dhimmah' (presumption of innocence).
3
Apply the ruling
The judge rules for the lesser amount because the greater is unproven.
This is stated in al-Bazzaziyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه أعتق بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي تقبل للاتفاق في المعنى بخلاف ما إذا شهد أحدهما أنه قذفه بالعربي والآخر بالفارسي لا تقبل لأن العبرة في الحدود للصورة والمعنى جميعاً احتياطاً للدرء؛ كذا في البزازية . الخامسة والعشرون اختلفا في مقدار المهر يقضى بالأقل كما في البزازية.
The twenty-fourth: One witness testified that he manumitted in Arabic and the other in Persian; it is accepted due to agreement in meaning, unlike if one testified that he accused someone of fornication in Arabic and the other in Persian; it is not accepted because in hudud the consideration is both form and meaning, as a precaution to avert punishment. As in al-Bazzaziyyah. The twenty-fifth: They differed on the amount of the dower; judgement is given for the lesser, as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First (Issue 24): In civil matters like manumission, testimony is accepted even if witnesses use different languages (Arabic vs. Persian), as long as the meaning is the same. But in criminal matters (hadd punishment for slander), the exact wording matters, so if one witness uses Arabic and the other Persian, the testimony is not accepted to avoid possible punishment. Second (Issue 25): In a dower dispute, when witnesses disagree on the amount, the judge rules for the lesser amount. This is because the excess is not proven.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the dower amount is disputed and each spouse presents one witness, which amount does the Hanafi judge decree?
A) The wife's claimed amount
B) The husband's claimed amount
C) The lesser amount
D) The average of both

Key Takeaway
In dower disputes, the lesser amount is taken as the established dower.

Testimony on Agency When Witnesses Disagree on Scope
Ruling on agency testimony when witnesses disagree on scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of agency testimony when witnesses disagree on the scope of the agency and state the part of the agency that is established.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on agency scope, the agency is established only on what they both agree upon.

In legal testimony, witnesses may agree on the core fact but differ in details. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on agency testimony when witnesses describe different scopes. The key principle is that agency can be limited, so testimony is accepted only on the common ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core agreement
Determine what both witnesses affirm about the agency. This is the essential fact they both testify to.
For example, both may agree that the principal appointed the agent to sue over a house.
2
Identify the additional claims
Note what only one witness adds—additional property, a dismissal, or extra tasks.
These are not confirmed by both.
3
Apply the rule
Agency is established only on the agreed part. The additional claims are not proven because they lack the second witness's support.
The principle is: الوكالة تقبل التخصيص.
4
Examine special sub-cases
The passage gives three variations: general vs. specific agency, addition of dismissal, and divorce agency with multiple women. In each, the same rule applies.
Specific agency is established if one witness testifies generally, dismissal is not established if only one mentions it, and the agent is authorized only for the common woman in divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة والعشرون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بخصومة مع فلان في دار سماها وشهدا الآخر أنه وكله بخصومة فيه وفي شيء آخر تقبل في دار اجتمعا عليه إذ الوكالة تقبل التخصيص وفيما اتفق عليه الشاهدان تثبت الوكالة لا فيما تفرد به أحدهما فلو ادعى وكالة معينة فشهد بها بوكالة عامة ينبغي أن تثبت المعينة. ولو شهد بوكالة وزاد أحدهما أنه عزله تقبل في الوكالة لا في العزل، ولو شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بطلاقها وشهد الآخر أنه وكله بطلاقها وطلاق فلانة الأخرى فهو وكيل في طلاق التي اتفقا عليه كذا في جامع الفصولين. السابعة والعشرون شهد أحدهما بأنه وقفه في صحته والآخر بأنه وقفه في مرضه قبلاً إذ شهدا بوقف بات إلا أن حكم المرض ينقض فيما لا يخرج من الثلث، وبهذا لا تمنع الشهادة كما لو شهد أحدهما أنه وقف ثلث أرضه والآخر أنه وقف ربعها؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين من كتاب الوقف من أحكام المرضى
The twenty-sixth: One testified that he appointed him as agent in a lawsuit with so-and-so in a named house, and the other testified that he appointed him as agent in that and in something else; it is accepted for the house they agreed upon, because agency accepts specification, and for what both witnesses agree on, agency is established, not for what only one mentioned. If he claimed a specific agency and the witness testified to a general agency, the specific should be established. And if he testified to agency and one added that he dismissed him, it is accepted for the agency, not for the dismissal. And if one testified that he appointed him as agent to divorce her, and the other that he appointed him to divorce her and divorce so-and-so, then he is agent in the divorce of the one they agreed upon. As in Jami' al-Fusulayn. The twenty-seventh: One testified that he made waqf in health, and the other that he made waqf in illness; it is accepted because they both testified to an absolute waqf, except that the ruling of illness invalidates what exceeds one-third. This does not prevent acceptance of testimony, just as if one testified that he waqf one-third of his land and the other that he waqf one-quarter; as in Jami' al-Fusulayn from the book of waqf on rulings of the ill.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
These are two separate issues. In Issue 26, the focus is on agency testimony. If witnesses agree on the core but differ on additional matters, the agency is established on the common ground. If one adds a dismissal, only the agency is proven. If one mentions a specific divorce and another mentions that plus another woman, the agent is authorized only for the common one. In Issue 27, waqf testimony: if witnesses differ on whether the waqf was made in health or illness, the testimony is accepted because they agree on the waqf itself. However, if it was in illness, the waqf is limited to one-third of the estate. This is similar to a case where they differ on the fraction (one-third vs. one-quarter) – still accepted.

Key Terms
الوكالة تقبل التخصيص (al-wikalah taqbalu al-takhsis): Agency can be limited to specific matters; testimony on agency is accepted only to the extent witnesses agree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one witness says the agent was appointed to divorce Hind, and the other says he was appointed to divorce Hind and marry someone else, what is the established agency?
A) Agency to divorce Hind and marry
B) Agency to divorce Hind only
C) No agency
D) Agency to marry only

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ on the scope of agency, the agency is established only on the common ground they both affirm.

Testimony on Waqf When Witnesses Disagree on Timing (Health vs. Illness)
Ruling on waqf testimony when witnesses disagree on health/illness or fraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of testimony on waqf when witnesses disagree on the timing (health vs. illness) or on the fraction, and explain the legal effect of the difference.

Core Idea
Testimony on waqf is valid even if witnesses differ on health/illness, but the illness ruling may limit the waqf to one-third.

Testimony about a waqf may include details that seem contradictory, like whether it was made in health or illness. The Hanafi ruling is that such testimony is accepted because they agree on the waqf itself. However, if it was made in terminal illness, the waqf is limited to one-third of the estate, similar to a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core agreement
Both witnesses affirm the waqf itself. That is the essential fact they both testify to.
For example, both say that the deceased made a waqf of a specific property.
2
Identify the difference
Note what differs: one says in health, one says in illness, or they differ on the fraction of the property.
These are secondary details attached to the core fact.
3
Apply the rule
The testimony is accepted on the core agreement. The difference does not void the testimony because they both affirm the waqf.
The principle: they agree on 'waqf bat' (absolute waqf).
4
Consider the legal effect
If the illness version is true, the waqf is treated like a bequest and is limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. This does not affect the validity of the testimony itself.
The passage gives the analogy of differing on the fraction (one-third vs. one-quarter) – testimony is still accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The twenty-sixth: One testified that he appointed him as agent in a lawsuit with so-and-so in a named house, and the other testified that he appointed him as agent in that and in something else; it is accepted for the house they agreed upon, because agency accepts specification, and for what both witnesses agree on, agency is established, not for what only one mentioned. If he claimed a specific agency and the witness testified to a general agency, the specific should be established. And if he testified to agency and one added that he dismissed him, it is accepted for the agency, not for the dismissal. This does not prevent acceptance of testimony, just as if one testified that he waqf one-third of his land and the other that he waqf one-quarter; as in Jami' al-Fusulayn from the book of waqf on rulings of the ill.

Commentary
These are two separate issues. In Issue 26, the focus is on agency testimony. If witnesses agree on the core but differ on additional matters, the agency is established on the common ground. If one adds a dismissal, only the agency is proven. If one mentions a specific divorce and another mentions that plus another woman, the agent is authorized only for the common one. In Issue 27, waqf testimony: if witnesses differ on whether the waqf was made in health or illness, the testimony is accepted because they agree on the waqf itself. However, if it was in illness, the waqf is limited to one-third of the estate. This is similar to a case where they differ on the fraction (one-third vs. one-quarter) – still accepted.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): A charitable endowment, where the corpus is preserved and its usufruct is dedicated to a charitable purpose.
حكم المرض (hukm al-marad): The ruling of terminal illness: acts of donation (including waqf) during marad al-mawt are treated like bequests, limited to one-third of the estate.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Differing Amounts in Testimony
Intra-Hanafi debate on testimony with differing amounts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on testimony when witnesses differ on the amount, explain the Sahibayn's opposing view, and apply the divorce analogy to critique their argument.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ on the amount, only the Sahibayn accept testimony on the common element; Abu Hanifa rejects it entirely.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acceptance of testimony when two witnesses give different amounts. Abu Hanifa holds that the testimony is not accepted, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) accept it based on the common element. The commentator then critiques the Sahibayn's position using an analogy from divorce testimonies. This lesson will walk you through the reasoning and the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa: testimony is not accepted when witnesses disagree on the amount (e.g., one says 1000, another says 2000).
The contract for 1000 is considered a different debt than for 2000.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept the testimony to the extent of the agreed-upon lesser amount, based on the principle ‘mu’tabiru la ghair’ (only the common element is considered).
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
They argue that the witnesses agree on the existence of at least the lesser amount, so that much is proven by their combined testimony.
This is analogous to cases where partial agreement suffices.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The commentator refutes using a divorce analogy: if two witnesses testify to one divorce and two others to three, the liability for half the dower upon retraction falls only on the witnesses of three, not the witnesses of one, showing that the common element does not always impose liability.
Key distinction: in the divorce case, each testimony alone has legal effect (baynunah); in the debt case, each alone gives no right.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the claim is 2000, Abu Hanifa requires two witnesses on 2000; Sahibayn would accept one witness on 1000 and another on 2000 to prove 1000. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.
The amount is integral to the contract; disagreement prevents proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين لم تقبل) يعني عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تقبل بناء على أن المعتبر لا غير. قال الشارح : والذي يبطل مذهبهما أن الشاهدين لو شهدا بتطليقة وشهد آخران بثلاث وفرق القاضي بينهما قبل الدخول ثم رجعوا كان ضمان نصف الصداق على شاهدي الثلاث دون شاهدي الواحدة، ولو كان كما قالا أن الواحدة توجد في الثلاث لكان الضمان عليهم جميعاً ا اهـ. وأجيب عنهما بأن الكلام فيما إذا كانت كل شهادة لا توجب شيئاً بانفرادها فحينئذ قالا بثبوت ما اتفقا عليه وهو الأقل فيثبت الحق بهما، وأما هنا فكل شهادة لو انفردت أوجبت البينونة ومع شهود الثلاث زيادة فأضيفت البينونة إليهم دون شهود الواحدة لعدم الحاجة إليهم، فلما لم يضف الحكم إليهم لم يضمنوا بالرجوع لهذا المعنى لا لما ذكره قال الشارح ولا يلزم ما إذا قال لها طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً فطلقت واحدة صحته قد أمضى الوقف وهما مختلفان اهـ
His saying: (If one testifies for one thousand and another for two thousand, it is not accepted) meaning according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is accepted based on the principle that the common element is considered. The commentator said: What invalidates their view is that if two witnesses testify to one divorce and another two testify to three, and the judge separates them before consummation, then they retract, the liability for half the dower is on the witnesses of three, not on the witnesses of one. If, as they say, the one is included in the three, then liability would be on all. And it is answered for them that the discussion is when each testimony does not necessitate anything by itself; there they say that what is agreed upon (the lesser) is established, so the right is proven by both. But here, each testimony alone would necessitate final separation (baynunah), and with the witnesses of three there is an increase, so the baynunah is attributed to them without the witnesses of one because there is no need for them. Since the ruling was not attributed to them, they are not liable upon retraction for this reason, not for what he mentioned. The commentator said, and it is not necessitated that if he said to her 'divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once, its validity... he has implemented the waqf, and they are different.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The issue is: if one witness says the debt is 1000 and another says 2000, Abu Hanifa says the testimony is not accepted (because the amount is integral), while the Sahibayn say it is accepted because they agree on the existence of a debt of at least 1000. The commentator then rebuts the Sahibayn using a scenario: if witnesses of one divorce and witnesses of three divorce testify, and the judge separates them, then the witnesses retract, the liability for half the dower falls only on those who testified to three, not on those who testified to one. If, as the Sahibayn claim, the one is contained in the three, then the witnesses of one should also be liable. The response: In that case, each testimony alone would cause baynunah (final divorce), but the witnesses of one are not needed because the three already cause it; hence they are not liable. This shows that the amounts case is different because there each testimony alone would not give a right; they only combine to create the right. So the Sahibayn's principle does not apply universally.

Key Terms
معتبر لا غير (mu'tabiru la ghair): The principle that only the common element is considered in testimony.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given before a judge to prove a right.
ألف (alf): One thousand (dirhams).
بينونة (baynunah): Final separation (irrevocable divorce) that ends the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if one witness says the debt is 1000 and another says 2000, what is the ruling?
A) Testimony is accepted for 1000
B) Testimony is not accepted
C) Testimony is accepted for 2000
D) The plaintiff must choose one witness

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ on the essential subject matter (amount), Abu Hanifa holds that the testimony is not accepted, a position that is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Cases Where Differing Testimony Is Accepted (Ikhtilaf fi al-Shahada)
List of fourteen accepted ikhtilaf cases in shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting differing testimony in shahada and apply it to the fourteen specific cases listed in the passage.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, two testimonies can differ in wording yet be accepted if they agree on the essential fact.

The passage presents a series of rulings from authoritative Hanafi works (al-Qunyah, Munyat al-Mufti, Adab al-Qada', al-Is'af) demonstrating when discrepancies between witnesses' testimonies are overlooked. The common thread is that as long as the core meaning is undisputed, the testimony is valid. This lesson walks through each case to help you internalize the principle and recognize its application in various contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared essential fact
For each pair of testimonies, determine what both witnesses agree on at the most basic level (e.g., a debt, a sale, an agency, a waqf).
The essence is that there is a legal act or obligation, even if described differently.
2
Classify the type of discrepancy
Note how the testimonies differ: in legal category (hawaala vs. kafala), in mention of term/option, in specific details of agency (place, method, authority), or in aspects of waqf (time, place, beneficiary).
All these are considered variations in description, not contradictions.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
Recall the rule: ikhtilaf in descriptive details does not undermine testimony if the underlying fact is agreed. Accept the testimony as valid.
This contrasts with stricter schools that require verbal identity.
4
Check for exceptions
Confirm that none of these cases involve a direct contradiction on the core fact. For example, difference on the beneficiary (Zayd vs. Amr) is resolved by giving to the poor, preserving the intent of charity.
The principle holds consistently across all fourteen cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسعة والعشرون ادعى مالاً فشهد أحدهما أن المحتال عليه أحال غريمه بهذا المال وشهد الآخر أنه كفل عن غريمه بهذا المال تقبل؛ كذا في القنية. الثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه باعه بكذا إلى شهر وشهد الآخر بالبيع ولم يذكر الأجل. الحادية والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه باعه بشرط الخيار ثلاثة أيام ولم يذكر الآخر الخيار تقبل فيهما كما ذكره الزيلعي في باب التحالف. الثانية والثلاثون من وكالة منية المفتي شهد واحد أنه وكله بالخصومة في هذه الدار عند قاضي الكوفة وآخر قال عند قاضي البصرة جازت شهادتهما ا هـ. الثالثة والثلاثون في أدب القضاء للخصاف من باب الشهادة بالوكالة شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بالقبض والآخر أنه جراه تقبل الرابعة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه سلطه على قبضه تقبل الخامسة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه أوصى إليه بقبضه في حياته تقبل السادسة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بطلب دينه والآخر بتقاضيه تقبل. السابعة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر بتقاضيه أو طلبه تقبل. الثامنة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه أمره بأخده أو أرسله ليأخذه تقبل ا هـ . وهي في أدب القضاء وما قبلها التاسعة والثلاثون اختلفا في زمن إقراره بالوقف تقبل الأربعون اختلفا في مكان إقراره به تقبل الحادية والأربعون اختلفا في وقفه في صحته أو في مرضه تقبل الثانية والأربعون شهد أحدهما بوقفها على زيد والآخر على عمرو تقبل وتكون وقفاً على الفقراء، وهذه الثلاثة من الإسعاف.
Twenty-ninth: He claimed property, so one witness testified that the debtor transferred the debt to his creditor, and the other testified that he guaranteed for his creditor this property – it is accepted; as in al-Qunyah. Thirtieth: One witness testified that he sold it for such for a month, and the other testified to the sale without mentioning the term – it is accepted. Thirty-first: One witness testified that he sold it with a condition of option for three days, and the other did not mention the option – it is accepted in both, as al-Zayla'i mentioned in Bab al-Tahalf. Thirty-second: From Wakalah of Munyat al-Mufti: One witness testified that he appointed him for litigation in this house before the qadi of Kufa, and another said before the qadi of Basra – their testimony is valid. Thirty-third: In Adab al-Qada' of al-Khassaf from Bab al-Shahada bi al-Wakalah: One witness testified that he appointed him to receive, and the other that he made him an agent – it is accepted. Thirty-fourth: One witness testified that he appointed him to receive it, and the other that he authorized him to receive it – it is accepted. Thirty-fifth: One witness testified that he appointed him to receive it, and the other that he bequeathed to him to receive it during his lifetime – it is accepted. Thirty-sixth: One witness testified that he appointed him to demand his debt, and the other to pursue it – it is accepted. Thirty-seventh: One witness testified that he appointed him to receive it, and the other to pursue or demand it – it is accepted. Thirty-eighth: One witness testified that he appointed him to receive it, and the other that he ordered him to take it or sent him to take it – it is accepted. These are from Adab al-Qada' and what preceded. Thirty-ninth: They differed regarding the time of his acknowledgment of the waqf – it is accepted. Fortieth: They differed regarding the place of his acknowledgment of it – it is accepted. Forty-first: They differed regarding his waqf in health or in illness – it is accepted. Forty-second: One witness testified that he made a waqf on Zayd, and the other on Amr – it is accepted, and it is a waqf for the poor. These three are from al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a list of rulings (masa'il) from various sources (al-Qunyah, Munyat al-Mufti, Adab al-Qada', al-Is'af) that illustrate cases where differing testimony (ikhtilaf fi al-shahada) is accepted in Hanafi fiqh. The common principle is that as long as the witnesses agree on the essential meaning (ma'na) even if their wording differs, their testimony is accepted. For example, in the 29th case, one witness says the debtor made a transfer (hawaala) and the other says he made a guarantee (kafala); both imply the same obligation, so the testimony is accepted. Similarly, in the 30th, one mentions a term and the other does not – the sale itself is agreed upon, so it is accepted. The 31st concerns sale with option (khiyar) – the existence of the option is extra information. The 32nd is about the location of agency – both agree on the appointment but differ on the place, so testimony is valid. The 33rd to 38th all concern agency (wakala) where the witnesses describe the extent of authority differently, but the underlying agency is agreed. The 39th to 41st concern the time, place, or health/illness condition of a waqf declaration – the waqf itself is not disputed. The 42nd shows that if witnesses differ on the beneficiary (Zayd vs. Amr), the testimony is accepted and the waqf is given to the poor, because the intent of charity is preserved.

Key Terms
اختلاف في الشهادة (ikhtilāf fī al-shahāda): Discrepancy between two witnesses' testimonies in wording or detail while agreeing on the essential fact.
حوالة (ḥawālah): Transfer of debt from one debtor to another, making the transferee the new debtor.
كفالة (kafālah): Guarantee where a person becomes surety for another's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 29th case, what is the ruling when one witness says the debtor transferred the debt and the other says he guaranteed it?
A) Testimony is rejected because the legal acts differ.
B) Testimony is accepted because both imply the same obligation.
C) Testimony is accepted only if the claimant specifies which act occurred.
D) Testimony is rejected unless both witnesses use the same wording.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the substance of testimony over the exact wording, accepting differences in descriptive details as long as the essential fact is agreed.
