Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony of Differing Amounts: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shahada with talaq analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) on conflicting testimony regarding amounts, and explain the legal reasoning (including the talaq analogy) that leads to the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on amount, the common element is not independently established—Abu Hanifa's rejection is the relied-upon view.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: one witness testifies to a debt of 1000, the other to 2000. Sahibayn argue that the testimony should be accepted for the common 1000, while Abu Hanifa insists that because neither testimony alone proves the debt, the whole testimony is rejected. We will unpack the talaq analogy used to defend Abu Hanifa's position and see why his view became the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Two Positions
Begin by recognizing the core question: when two witnesses give different numbers, can the testimony be accepted for the agreed minimum? State Abu Hanifa's position (rejected) and the Sahibayn's position (accepted for 1000). Note that this is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
The Sahibayn rely on the concept of 'al-muʿtabar' (the common element).
2
Understand the Sahibayn's Analogy and Proof
The Sahibayn liken this to cases where the common element is taken (e.g., in divorce, if witnesses disagree on number, the lesser is accepted). Their dalil: since both agree on 1000, that part should be proven.
Their qiyas is based on the idea that the common amount is implicitly testified.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Refutation via the Talaq Case
The commentator presents a counter-analogy: if two witnesses say one divorce and two say three, and the qadi separates before consummation, then retraction, the liability falls only on the witnesses of three, not on the witnesses of one. This shows that the common element (one divorce) is not automatically accepted because each testimony alone would cause baynuna. In the monetary case, neither testimony alone proves the debt, so the common element cannot be taken.
The key distinction: in the talaq case each testimony alone has legal effect, while in the debt case no single testimony establishes the right.
4
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the case is dismissed because the testimony is rejected entirely. Under the Sahibayn's view, judgment is entered for 1000. This difference affects litigants directly.
Also note that later authorities (Qadikhan, al-Kafi) favor Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Its Basis
Although there is a riwayah in al-Bazzaziyya suggesting consensus on accepting the lesser in divorce, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for testimony is Abu Hanifa's view. The commentator indicates that what is in al-Bazzaziyya is an error (sahw).
The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, and Qadikhan's Fatawa confirm al-Kafi's preference for Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين لم تقبل) يعني عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تقبل بناء على أن المعتبر لا غير. قال الشارح : والذي يبطل مذهبهما أن الشاهدين لو شهدا بتطليقة وشهد آخران بثلاث وفرق القاضي بينهما قبل الدخول ثم رجعوا كان ضمان نصف الصداق على شاهدي الثلاث دون شاهدي الواحدة، ولو كان كما قالا أن الواحدة توجد في الثلاث لكان الضمان عليهم جميعاً ا اهـ. وأجيب عنهما بأن الكلام فيما إذا كانت كل شهادة لا توجب شيئاً بانفرادها فحينئذ قالا بثبوت ما اتفقا عليه وهو الأقل فيثبت الحق بهما، وأما هنا فكل شهادة لو انفردت أوجبت البينونة ومع شهود الثلاث زيادة فأضيفت البينونة إليهم دون شهود الواحدة لعدم الحاجة إليهم، فلما لم يضف الحكم إليهم لم يضمنوا بالرجوع لهذا المعنى لا لما ذكره قال الشارح ولا يلزم ما إذا قال لها طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً فطلقت واحدة صحته قد أمضى الوقف وهما مختلفان اهـ قوله فشهد أحدهما أن المحتال عليه أحال غريمه الذي في القنية أن المحتال عليه احتال عن غريمه قوله : والآخر أنه جراه تقبل) قال في شرح أدب القاضي : : لأن الجراية والوكالة سواء والجري والوكيل سواء فقد اتفق الشاهدان في المعنى واختلفا في اللفظ وأنه لا يمنع قبول الشهادة الخ قوله : (الحادية والأربعون مكررة مع السابعة والعشرين. حيث تقع واحدة لأن ذلك لكون الثلاث صار في يدها فلها أن توقع كلها أو بعضها، ولا يلزم ما إذا طلقها الزوج ألفاً حيث يقع الثلاث لأنه يتصرف عن ملك فله أن يوقع أي عدد شاء إلا أنه لا ينفذ إلا بقدر المحل ا هـ . وقدمنا عن الكافي أن المائة والمائتين والطلقة والطلقتين كالألف ،والألفين وظاهره أنه لا يقع شيء عند أبي حنيفة، وقدمنا عن البزازية في المسائل المستثناة ما يقتضي أن يقضي في الطلاق بالأقل اتفاقاً وقد صرح قاضيخان في فتاواه بما في الكافي فكان هو المذهب لأن ما في البزازية رواية المنتقى إلا أن يفرق بينهما بما قدمناه، وكذا ما في البزازية قبله لو ادعى ألفين فشهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين يقبل على ألف إجماعاً سهو كما لا يخفى .
His saying: (If one testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, it is not accepted) meaning according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is accepted based on the consideration of the common element. The commentator said: What invalidates their school is that if two witnesses testified to one divorce and another two witnesses testified to three, and the qadi separated them before consummation, then they retracted, the responsibility for half the dower falls on the witnesses of three, not on the witnesses of one. If it were as they say, that the one is included in the three, then the responsibility would be on all of them. And it was answered to them that the discussion is when each testimony individually does not establish anything; then they said the common element (the lesser) is established, so the right is proven by them. But here, each testimony if isolated would cause irreconcilable separation (baynuna), and with the witnesses of three there is an increase, so the separation is attributed to them, not to the witnesses of one, because there is no need for them. Since the ruling is not attributed to them, they do not bear responsibility upon retraction for this meaning, not for what he mentioned. The commentator said: And it does not necessitate the case where he said to her 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once – its validity because the power to give three has come into her hand, so she can execute all or some. And it does not necessitate the case where the husband divorced her a thousand times, as three occur, because he acts from his ownership, so he can execute any number, but it only takes effect to the extent of the capacity. And we have previously presented from al-Kafi that one hundred and two hundred, and one divorce and two divorces, are like one thousand and two thousand. Its apparent meaning is that nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa. And we have previously presented from al-Bazzaziyya in the exceptional issues that suggests that in divorce the lesser is decreed by consensus. And Qadikhan has stated in his Fatawa what is in al-Kafi, so it is the madhhab, because what is in al-Bazzaziyya is a narration of al-Muntaqa, unless one distinguishes between them as we have done. And similarly, what is in al-Bazzaziyya before that: if he claims two thousand and one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, it is accepted for one thousand by consensus – an error, as is clear.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding differing testimony on amounts. The matn states: if one witness says 1000 and the other says 2000, the testimony is not accepted. The commentator (here Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) clarifies that this is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it is accepted based on the common element (al-mu'tabir), i.e., the 1000. The commentator then provides an objection from the Sahibayn's perspective using a talaq analogy: if two witnesses testify to one divorce and another two to three divorces, and the qadi separates the couple before consummation, then the witnesses retract, only the witnesses of three are liable for half the dower, not the witnesses of one. If the one divorce were included in the three, as the Sahibayn argue, then all witnesses would share liability. The response to this objection is that the talaq case is different: each testimony alone suffices to cause baynuna, so the witnesses of three are alone responsible because they provided the increase. In the 1000 vs. 2000 case, each testimony alone does not establish the right, so the common element is taken. The passage then discusses further examples and nuances from al-Kafi and al-Bazzaziyya, concluding that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as Qadikhan affirms, though there is some inconsistency.

Key Terms
المعتبر (al-muʿtabar): The common element or the agreed-upon minimum in differing testimonies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is testimony of 1000 and 2000 not accepted?
A) Because the witnesses contradict each other on the exact amount.
B) Because neither testimony alone proves the debt; the common element cannot be proven without establishing the larger.
C) Because the claimant must prove the exact amount claimed.
D) Because the Sahibayn's opinion is weaker.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when witnesses give differing numerical amounts, the relied-upon position is that the testimony is rejected entirely, because the common element is not independently proven.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony of 1000 and 1500: Acceptance on Common Amount
Explains acceptance of testimony when one says 1000 and other says 1500 with claimant claiming the higher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for accepting testimony when two witnesses give different amounts and apply the requirement of reconciliation (tawfiq) to analogous cases in divorce.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted on the common element if the witnesses agree in wording, but the larger amount needs claimant's reconciliation.

When two witnesses give different figures for a debt, can the testimony be accepted at all? The Hanafi school distinguishes between cases where the amounts share a common term (like 1000 and 1500) and cases where they do not (like 1000 and 2000). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind accepting the common 1000 and the crucial role of the claimant's reconciliation. We also explore parallel rulings in divorce testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening: if one witness testifies to 1000 and the other to 1500, and the claimant claims 1500, the testimony is accepted for 1000. Note the condition: claimant must claim the greater amount.
This is the base ruling from the matn.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The witnesses agree on the word 'alf' in both wording and meaning. The extra 500 is added by conjunction, so it is a separate claim. The common element is established. Contrast with 1000 vs 2000: 'alf' and 'alfayn' are different words, so no common element is proven.
The principle is linguistic agreement.
3
Analyze the condition of claimant's claim
If the claimant does not claim the greater, the testimony is invalid (takdhib). However, if the claimant reconciles (tawfiq) by stating that his original right was the higher amount but the excess was paid or forgiven, the testimony is accepted on the lesser.
Reconciliation must be explicit; silence is insufficient.
4
Apply to analogous cases in divorce
The same reasoning applies to talaq: e.g., one witness says one talaq, another says one and a half talaq – accepted on the common one talaq. Note the cases where testimony is rejected (e.g., conditional divorces with different conditions; fractional divorces according to Abu Hanifa).
These applications test the boundaries of the principle.
5
Distinguish compound numbers
The rule differs for compound numbers like 15 (خمسة عشر) vs 10 and 5. Because 'khmsh 'shr' is a single compound word, it cannot be broken into common parts without conjunction. So 15 and '10 and 5' are treated like 1000 vs 2000 – no common element.
The presence of the conjunction 'و' (and) is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن شهد الآخر بألف وخمسمائة والمدعي يدعي ذلك قبلت على الألف) لاتفاقهما على الألف لفظاً ومعنى وقد انفرد أحدهما بخمسمائة بالعطف والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه فيثبت ما اتفقا عليه بخلاف الألف والألفين لأن لفظ الألف غير لفظ الألفين ولم يثبت واحد منهما، ولا يقال إن الألف موجود في الألفين لأنا نقول : نعم موجود إذا ثبت الألفان فتثبت الألف ضمناً فإذا لم يثبت المتضمن لا يثبت المتضمن. ومقتضى تعليلهم أنه لو شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألف وألف أن يقضى بالألف اتفاقاً إذا ادعى الأكثر. قيد بقوله «والمدعي يدعي الأكثر لأنه لو لم يدع فهي باطلة للتكذيب إلا أن يوفق فيقول أصل حقي كان كما قال إلا أني استوفيت الزائد أو أبرأته عنه فحينئذ تقبل على الأقل لظهور التوفيق. ونظير مسألة الكتاب الطلقة والطلقة ونصف والمائة والمائة والخمسون. وفي العناية : لا بد من ذكر التوفيق فيما يحتمله على الأصح فلو سكت عنه لم تقبل ا هـ. وهكذا في المعراج بخلاف العشرة وخمسة عشر حيث لا تقبل لأنه مركب كالألفين إذا ليس بينهما حرف العطف ؛ ذكره الشارح وفي القنية شهد أحدهما على خمسة عشر والآخر على عشرة وخمسة والمدعي يدعي خمسة عشر ينبغي أن تقبل وفي الخانية : ولو شهد أحدهما على تطليقه والآخر على تطليقة ونصف أو شهد أحدهما على تطليقة والآخر تطليقة وتطليقة جازت شهادتهما على الأقل عند الكل، ولو شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها إن دخلت الدار وقد دخلت وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها إن كلمت وقد كلمت لا تقبل عند الكل، وكذا لو شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها ثلاثاً وشهد الآخر أنه قال لها أنت علي حرام ونوى الثلاث لا تقبل عند الكل، ولو شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها نصف واحدة وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها ثلث واحدة لا تقبل عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا لو شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها ثلاثاً وشهد الآخر أنه طلقها فالشهادة باطلة في قول .
His saying: (If the other witness testifies to one thousand and five hundred, and the claimant claims that, it is accepted for one thousand) because they agree on one thousand in wording and meaning. And one of them has added five hundred by conjunction, and the conjoined is not the conjoined-upon, so what they agreed upon is established, contrary to one thousand and two thousand, because the wording of one thousand is not the wording of two thousand, and neither is established. It cannot be said that one thousand is present in two thousand, because we say: yes, it is present if two thousand is established, then one thousand is established implicitly. So if the implicit (two thousand) is not established, the implicit (one thousand) is not established. The implication of their reasoning is that if one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand and one (alaf wa alaf), it should be decreed for one thousand by consensus if the claimant claims the greater. He restricted it with his saying 'and the claimant claims the greater' because if he does not claim, then it is invalid due to lying (takdhib), unless he reconciles by saying: my original right was as he said, but I have received the excess or released him from it; then it is accepted for the lesser due to the appearance of reconciliation. The analogy of the book's issue is the divorce and half divorce, and the one hundred and one hundred and fifty. In al-'Inaya: It is necessary to mention the reconciliation in what is possible according to the most correct view; if he remains silent, it is not accepted. Similarly in al-Mi'raj, unlike ten and fifteen where it is not accepted because it is a compound like two thousand, as there is no conjunction between them; the commentator mentioned it. In al-Qunyah: One witness testified to fifteen, and the other to ten and five, and the claimant claims fifteen; it should be accepted. In al-Khaniya: If one witness testified to his divorce (one talaq) and the other to one and a half talaq, or one testified to one talaq and the other to one plus one talaq (i.e., two), the testimony is accepted for the lesser by all. If one testified that he divorced her if you enter the house, and she entered, and the other that he divorced her if you speak, and she spoke, it is not accepted by all. Similarly, if one testified that he divorced her three times and the other that he said 'you are forbidden to me' intending three, it is not accepted by all. If one testified that he divorced her half a divorce and the other that he divorced her one-third of a divorce, it is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, if one testified that he divorced her three times and the other that he divorced her, the testimony is invalid according to one saying.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise on the matn's ruling: if one witness says 1000 and the other says 1500, and the claimant claims 1500, the testimony is accepted on the common 1000. The reasoning is that the witnesses agree on 1000 in both wording (alf) and meaning, and the extra 500 is separate (by conjunction). This differs from the case of 1000 vs 2000 because 'alf' and 'alfayn' are different words, and the larger is not proven. The commentator explains that if the claimant does not claim the larger, the testimony is invalid unless he reconciles (tawfiq) by saying the original debt was as stated but the excess was paid or remitted. This principle is applied to similar cases in divorce (talaq) and amounts, such as one talaq and one and a half talaq, or one talaq and two talaq. However, certain forms of testimony are never accepted, such as conditional divorces with different conditions, or when one testifies to three talaq and the other to tahrim with intention of three, because they differ in the legal act itself. Also, fractional divorces (half, third) are not accepted by Abu Hanifa because the underlying act is uncertain. The text also addresses compound numbers like 15 vs 10+5, where the conjunction clarifies the common parts.

Key Terms
التوفيق (al-tawfīq): The reconciliation by the claimant that the original debt was the higher amount but excess has been paid or remitted.
العطف (al-'atf): Grammatical conjunction (e.g., 'wa') that separates the common amount from the additional amount.
المتضمن (al-mutadammin): The implicit element; e.g., 1000 is implicit in 2000 if 2000 is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony of 1000 and 1500 accepted on the common 1000 while testimony of 1000 and 2000 is not?
A) Because 1500 contains 1000 explicitly, while 2000 does not.
B) Because the witnesses' words agree on 'alf' in the first case but not in the second.
C) Because 1500 is less than 2000, so the fit is closer.
D) Because the claimant claimed 1500 in the first case.

Key Takeaway
Testimony with differing amounts is accepted on the common element only if the witnesses agree on the same word for that element; the claimant must claim the higher amount or reconcile.
